| `/api/sessions/:session/kill` | POST | Kill session — `:session` validated via `validate.ValidateName()`. Returns `200 {"ok":true}` |
| `/api/sessions/:session/windows` | POST | Create window — JSON body `{"name":"...","cwd":"..."}`. **Session-scoped** (the window does not exist yet, so there is no window ID to key on). Returns `201 {"ok":true}` |
| `/api/windows/{windowId}/kill` | POST | Kill window — `{windowId}` validated via `validate.ValidateWindowID` (`^@[0-9]+$`); `400` on malformed ID, no tmux call. Returns `200 {"ok":true}` |
| `/api/windows/{windowId}/move` | POST | Reorder window within its session — JSON body `{"targetIndex": N}`. Source addressed by stable `{windowId}`; destination remains positional. Backend resolves the source's current index from the ID, then bubble-swaps to the target position via `tmux swap-window` (insert-before semantics). Returns `200 {"ok":true}` |
| `/api/windows/{windowId}/move-to-session` | POST | Move window to another session — JSON body `{"targetSession":"..."}`. Runs `tmux move-window -s {windowId} -t {targetSession}:` (window ID source, session destination; tmux preserves the ID and auto-assigns the index). Returns `200 {"ok":true}` |
| `/api/sessions/:session/color` | POST | Set or clear session color — JSON body `{"color": "4"}` / `{"color": "1+3"}` (color-value descriptor string) to set, `{"color": null}` to clear. `handleSessionColor` validates the session name and the descriptor via the shared `validate.ValidateColorValue` (single index 0–15 OR `a+b` each 0–15; `400` on malformed) then writes/clears the tmux `@session_color` option via `tmux.SetSessionColor`/`UnsetSessionColor` — NOT `run-kit.yaml` (since `260615-6rnr`; the body was `{"color": N}` int before). Returns `200 {"ok":true}` |
| `/api/windows/{windowId}/options` | POST | **Unified partial-merge window-option setter** (since `260529-jad6` — replaced the three separate `POST /color`, `PUT /url`, `PUT /type` routes). JSON body `{"options": {"@color":"5","@rk_url":"https://…","@rk_type":null,"@rk_marker":"solid"}}` decoded as `map[string]*string`: a present key with a string sets it, an explicit `null` unsets it, an absent key is left untouched (partial-merge — never full-replace, which avoided the "client clears a field it didn't echo" bug class). **Key allowlist** `{@color, @rk_url, @rk_type, @rk_marker}` (the `optKey*` constants) — any other key → `400`, never passed to tmux (§I — bounds the option-name surface). Per-key validation (`validateWindowOption`): `@color` must be a color-value descriptor — a single ANSI index `0–15` OR a two-hue blend `a+b` (each component `0–15`), validated via the shared `validate.ValidateColorValue`; `@rk_url` non-empty after trim; `@rk_type` non-empty sets verbatim (no enum validation, preserving `handleWindowTypeUpdate`), empty/`null` unsets; `@rk_marker` must be one of `""`/`dotted`/`solid`/`double` via `validate.ValidateMarkerValue` (the closed-set rule). Like `@rk_type`, an empty-string `@rk_marker` is treated as **unset** (nil op — clear the marker). **Validate-all-before-any-tmux**: if any key fails validation the endpoint returns `400` and issues zero tmux calls (no partial application). The whole merge executes as **one atomic `\;`-chained tmux invocation** via `tmux.SetWindowOptions`, then `handleWindowOptions` wakes the SSE hub (`s.sseHub.wake(server)`, § Per-server wake seam) so the mutation repaints in one poll pass. Returns `200 {"ok":true}` |
| `/api/windows/{windowId}/rename` | POST | Rename window — JSON body `{"name":"..."}`. Returns `200 {"ok":true}` |
| `/api/windows/{windowId}/keys` | POST | Send keys — JSON body `{"keys":"..."}` (non-empty after trim). Returns `200 {"ok":true}` |
| `/api/windows/{windowId}/select` | POST | Select (activate) the window. **Session-scoped (since `260529-jad6`)**: `handleWindowSelect` resolves the owning session for `{windowId}` server-side via `ResolveWindowSession`, then issues `tmux select-window -t <session>:{windowId}` via `SelectWindowInSession` — NOT a bare `select-window -t {windowId}`. The scoped target disambiguates inside tmux session groups (group members keep independent active-window state, so a bare target may activate the window on the wrong member, causing the wrong-window-highlight symptom). The session is derived server-side; the client never supplies it. A stale `{windowId}` whose session cannot be resolved surfaces a non-2xx error and issues no select. Returns `200 {"ok":true}` |
| `/api/windows/{windowId}/split` | POST | Split the window's active pane — JSON body `{"horizontal": bool}`. Returns `200 {"ok":true,"paneId":"%N"}` |
| `/api/windows/{windowId}/close-pane` | POST | Kill the window's active pane. Returns `200 {"ok":true}` |
| `/api/windows/{windowId}/chat` | GET | **Chat backfill** — full conversation as rk-schema JSON (`260714-pmfh-chat-read-backend`; `api/chat.go` `handleChatBackfill`). Validates `{windowId}` (`parseWindowID`, `400`), resolves the window's **reconciled** `@rk_chat` rollup server-side via `resolveWindowChat` (`FetchSessions` + window lookup by `WindowID`, reading `ChatProvider`/`ChatSessionRef` — never trusts a client-supplied ref), routes to the provider adapter's `Backfill`, and returns `{"provider","sessionRef","events":[...],"pending":{...}\|null,"offset":<N>}`. **The additive `offset` field (`260717-vhvz-chat-on-state-socket`)** carries the transcript byte offset the backfill parse read up to (`Backfill` populates it from `backfillFromPath`'s end offset, formerly discarded) — it supplies the state-socket chat subscribe's `from`, so `GET(offset)→subscribe(from)` composes gap-free/duplicate-free (§ State Socket → chat kind). `resolveWindowChat` distinguishes a FetchSessions failure (`500`, mirroring `handleSessionsList`) from a genuine no-chat (`404`) so a transient tmux fault is never misreported. Errors: `404` no reconciled chat; 404-class no-adapter for a well-formed unknown provider; 404-class transcript-missing (`ErrTranscriptNotFound`) / malformed-reconciled-ref (`ErrInvalidRef`) via `writeChatReadError` (the client only supplies a windowID, so a bad ref is a property of the reconciled `@rk_chat`, not a server fault); `500` other read error. GET/read-only (§IX); curl-able. Since `260717-vhvz` this is the SOLE chat read endpoint (the live stream moved to `/ws/state`). See [chat](chat.md) |
| ~~`/api/windows/{windowId}/chat/stream`~~ | — | **No such endpoint** — there is no dedicated per-view chat SSE. The live incremental chat stream is a `kind:"chat"` subscription on `/ws/state` (subscribed on chat-lens enter, unsubscribed on leave), so a tab holds a fixed 2 WS + 0 SSE (D6). See § State Socket → chat kind and [chat](chat.md) § Live stream. (`260717-vhvz-chat-on-state-socket`) |
| `/api/windows/{windowId}/chat/send` | POST | **Chat send** — inject a typed message into the window's resolved agent PANE (`260714-jdyg-chat-send`; `api/chat.go` `handleChatSend`). Mutation ⇒ POST (§IX). Body `{"text":"<message>"}`; validates `{windowId}` (`parseWindowID`, `400`) + non-empty/decodable text (`400`), then re-resolves the target pane server-side (extended `resolveWindowChat` → `sessions.ResolveChatPane` also returns the `PaneID` — active-pane-first rollup, client supplies no pane/ref; `FetchSessions` fail → `500`, no-chat → `404`). Injection (discrete provider-agnostic `injectChatMessage` seam, v1 no provider branch): baseline `CapturePane` → `set-buffer -b rk-chat-send -- <text>` → `paste-buffer -d -p -t <paneID>` → **NOVELTY echo probe** (needle occurrence count must strictly INCREASE vs the pre-paste baseline; multiline paste-collapse chip counted only for multiline; fails closed) → `send-keys -t <paneID> Enter` ONLY on probe success. Probe failure → structured `409` (Enter withheld, pasted text left recoverable in the composer, retry-hint against duplication); tmux subprocess fail → `500`; success `200 {"ok":true}`. Busy policy Allow + probe (NO `agentState` gate, NO queue — Constitution II). Concurrency: per-`(server,paneID)` whole-sequence mutex + a nested global set→paste mutex for the shared named buffer; ONE shared context deadline (`chatSendTotalBudget` 4s) threads all subprocesses (route under the 5s rule). The generic `POST /api/windows/{windowId}/keys` is left untouched. See [chat](chat.md) § Send Path |
| `/api/directories` | GET | Server-side directory listing for autocomplete — `?prefix=~/code/wvr` returns matching dirs under `$HOME` |
| `/api/sessions/:session/upload` | POST | File upload — session from URL path (not form field). Multipart with `file` field, optional `window` field (defaults to `"0"`). Resolves project root via `ListWindows`, writes to `.uploads/{timestamp}-{name}`, auto-manages `.gitignore`. 50MB limit. Returns `200 {"ok":true,"path":"..."}` |
| `/ws/state` | GET (WS) | **State socket** — one `gorilla/websocket` connection per browser tab multiplexes ALL session-state + host-metrics streams over one connection (`260716-qf3j-state-socket`). JSON text-frame envelope protocol, `serverFromRequest`-agnostic (no `?server=` — the socket carries no server in the URL; subscriptions name servers in-band). `handleStateWS` (`api/state_ws.go`) upgrades via the shared `upgrader`, reads a mandatory first `hello` frame, replays the six cached global slots, then a read loop dispatching `subscribe`/`unsubscribe`/`preview-scope` while a per-connection writer pump drains the send channel. The whole event catalogue, cached-slot replay, per-server poll-set membership, metrics-only cadence, and the `gone` reap live under § State Socket below. **Why WS not muxed SSE**: an established WebSocket holds NO slot in the browser's 6-per-origin HTTP/1.1 pool in any engine (spike `docs/findings/socket-pool-accounting.md`), so consolidating state streams onto it clears the pool starvation that blocked terminal-relay handshakes on Firefox/WebKit for plaintext origins; in-band subscribe frames are also totally ordered with the events they gate, structurally killing the POST-vs-stream race class and the `attachServer`→SSE race. GET/read-only (§IX) |
| `/ws/terminals` | GET (WS) | **Terminals socket** — one `gorilla/websocket` connection per browser tab muxing ALL pane relay streams over one connection (`260717-803u-relay-mux`). `handleTerminalsWS` (`api/terminals_ws.go`) upgrades via the shared `upgrader`, then runs a read loop dispatching binary `[u32 BE streamId][payload]` data frames (routed to the addressed stream's PTY) and JSON control ops (`open`/`resize`/`close`) while a single writer goroutine schedules every stream's output — control/short frames ahead of bulk, round-robin across streams — through the per-stream bounded queues. Each stream runs (validate → `ResolveWindowSession` → session-scoped `SelectWindowInSession` → `forceTERM` + best-effort `ReloadConfig` → `pty.StartWithSize` at the open op's cols/rows); a stream-level failure emits a `closed` control event (4004/4001) WITHOUT closing the socket. No `?server=` in the URL (the server rides each `open` op). GET/read-only (§IX). Full protocol + write-path scheduler live under § Terminal Relay below |
| `/api/preview-scope` | POST | Declare a state-socket connection's expanded-session set for tile-grid pane previews (`260701-70a0-session-window-tile-grid`). `handlePreviewScope` (`api/preview.go`) decodes `{conn, expanded[]}` (body bounded at 64 KiB via `io.LimitReader`; malformed ⇒ `400`, empty `conn` ⇒ `400`), resolves the server via `serverFromRequest`, calls `s.initSSEHub()` (a scope POST may race ahead of the first subscribe on a fresh server) then `s.sseHub.setPreviewScope(server, conn, expanded)`, returns `200 {"ok":true}`. A `conn` matching no live connection is a silent no-op `200`. **RETAINED alongside an in-band twin** (`260716-qf3j-state-socket`, decision D4): the state socket's own `preview-scope` op (see § State Socket) addresses the SAME connection by its own `hello` conn id via the same `normalizeConnID` semantics and calls the SAME `setPreviewScope`, so the HTTP endpoint stays zero-regression while the frontend now sends preview-scope in-band (no POST-races-the-stream window). The set is per-connection, in-memory only (Constitution II — dropped on disconnect), and bounds which windows the poll captures. POST per Constitution §IX; CORS `AllowedMethods` stays `[GET, POST, OPTIONS]`. See § Session-Tile Previews |
| `/api/tmux/reload-config` | POST | Reload tmux config — server from `?server=` param (default `"default"`). Runs `source-file` on the specified server. Returns `200 {"status":"ok"}` |
| `/api/status/refresh` | POST | **Composing on-demand refresh of BOTH PR pollers** (`260715-jykd-manual-status-refresh`; superseded `POST /api/pr-status/refresh` — a single-poller synchronous handler whose sole frontend consumer, `PrStatusLine`, had zero live sites). `handleStatusRefresh` (`api/status_refresh.go`) kicks the viewer-wide collector (`prstatus.Collector.RefreshNow` — supplies the merged state via its URL-keyed join) AND the branch refresher (`prstatus.DefaultBranchRefresher.RefreshNow` — covers the sibling case: a just-opened PR appearing on a window, a 30s wait today). **Naming is "status", not "pane"**: "pane" collides with the tmux-pane meaning in this codebase; "status" matches the established vocabulary (status pyramid, StatusDot). **Non-blocking `202` via a DETACHED goroutine**: the two refreshes run on a `context.WithTimeout(context.Background(), statusRefreshTimeout=60s)` context (NOT `r.Context()`, which dies the moment the handler returns) — the branch pass is one `gh pr list` per registered pair and can exceed the 5s handler-blocking cap (`code-review.md`), so the 202-then-detach shape keeps the handler well under it (the exact detached pattern mirrors `api/waiting_push.go`). **Single frequency choke point** (so ANY trigger — button-mashing, multiple tabs, future auto-triggers — is safe to over-fire): (a) **coalescing** — if a forced refresh is in flight, no second refresh starts; (b) **min-interval throttle** — a call arriving within `statusRefreshMinInterval=10s` of the last refresh starts nothing. **Tri-state 202 body (since `260715-nwla-status-refresh-feedback`)**: started, coalesced, AND throttled calls ALL still return `202` and are all still fire-and-forget (the body is NEVER the completion signal — fresh data and completion both arrive over SSE, see below), but the body now REPORTS which fate applied so the client can give honest per-status feedback — `202 {"status":"started"}` (a new pass began; a `status-refresh` completion event will follow), `202 {"status":"coalesced"}` (a pass is already in flight; ITS completion event will follow), or `202 {"status":"throttled"}` (nothing started; NO event will come). `startStatusRefresh()` returns a small named `refreshOutcome` string type (`refreshStarted`/`refreshCoalesced`/`refreshThrottled`) instead of the former `bool` — the started/coalesced/throttled distinction was already computed internally under the mutex and is now surfaced rather than collapsed; `handleStatusRefresh` launches the detached goroutine ONLY on `refreshStarted` and writes `{"status": string(outcome)}`. **Completion broadcast**: `finishStatusRefresh()` (which runs exactly once per completed pass, at the end of the detached goroutine, after clearing the in-flight flag) calls `s.sseHub.broadcastStatusRefresh(s.now())` guarded by `if s.sseHub != nil` (the hub is lazy-initialized on the first SSE connection and absent in the direct-`&Server{}` handler tests, so the nil-guard is required) — this is the once-per-pass structural guarantee that a coalesced/throttled POST (which starts no goroutine) emits no extra completion event. The two kicks are **injectable seams** on `api.Server` (`refreshCollectorFn`/`refreshBranchFn` function fields, defaulted in `NewRouterAndServer`, mirroring the collector-injection house pattern), and the coalesce/throttle state (`refreshStatusMu sync.Mutex`, `refreshStatusInFlight bool`, `refreshStatusLast time.Time`) plus a `nowFn func() time.Time` clock seam live per-server so handler tests assert both kicks fire — and drive the started/coalesced/throttled paths deterministically — without spawning `gh` or real sleeps (`startStatusRefresh`/`finishStatusRefresh` helpers; `s.now()` also stamps the broadcast `completedAt` so it is test-controllable). The collector kick nil-guards `s.prStatus` (a partially-wired test router has no collector — no panic, branch kick still fires). Server-independent (both pollers are global, not per-`?server=`). POST per Constitution §IX (additive body + SSE event only — no new endpoint, no new verb); the CORS `AllowedMethods` allowlist stays `[GET, POST, OPTIONS]` |
| `/api/riff` | POST | **Web-UI agent spawn** (`260713-sbk1-web-spawn-agent`; dialog-v2 fields `260714-q9cg-spawn-agent-dialog-mockup`) — surfaces the extracted `internal/riff` engine (worktree + tmux window + agent launcher; full engine in [rk-riff](rk-riff.md)). `handleRiffSpawn` (`api/riff.go`): `?server=<name>`, JSON body `{task?, preset?, session, where?, worktreeName?, tier?}` (the last three are additive over the shipped body — `where` ∈ `""`/`worktree`/`checkout` (default `worktree`), `worktreeName` names the worktree in worktree mode, `tier` picks the fab agent tier). Validates `session` via `validate.ValidateName`, then the **v2 fields BEFORE deriving the repo root / touching any subprocess** (constitution §I — nothing created on a 400): an unknown `where` → `400`; a non-empty `worktreeName` **with `where="checkout"`** → `400` (it has no meaning); a non-empty `worktreeName` → `validate.ValidateWorktreeName` (`400`); a non-empty `tier` → `validate.ValidateTier` (`400`). It then **derives the repo root** from the target session's active-pane cwd (see § Riff Repo-Root Derivation below), returning `400` (nothing created) on a non-repo/empty cwd or a session-read failure. On a valid repo it calls `s.riff.Spawn(ctx, riff.Options{server, session, repoRoot, task, preset, where, worktreeName, tier})` (count fixed at 1) and returns `200 {"server","session","window","windowId"}` — enough for the client to navigate to `/$server/$window` (the sidebar row arrives via the existing SSE stream; no new SSE work). An unknown-preset engine error (`riff.ExitCodeError{Code: ExitValidation}`) maps to `400`; any other engine failure maps to `500`. **Synchronous handler with a documented 5s-rule exception** — the aggregate `wt create` (30s build-class) + tmux (≤10s each) + `fab agent [tier] --print` (10s) MAY exceed the 5s tmux-blocking review rule; each individual subprocess keeps its own bound, and the exception is documented in a comment at the handler. Task text reaches tmux only through the engine's escaped `buildSkillShellString` seam (Constitution §I). Uses a dedicated `context.Background()`-derived timeout for both the repo-root `ListWindows` (`riffRepoRootTimeout = 5s`) and the engine spawn (`riffSpawnTimeout = 90s`) — NOT `r.Context()` — so a client disconnect never truncates a half-created worktree. POST per Constitution §IX |
| `/api/riff/presets` | GET | **Riff preset + tier preflight** (`260713-sbk1-web-spawn-agent`; `tiers` added `260714-q9cg-spawn-agent-dialog-mockup`; `tiers` fab-gated `260714-gsmu-spawn-dialog-tier-gate-sidebar-entry`) — `handleRiffPresets` (`api/riff.go`): `?server=&session=`, validates `session` (`400`), derives the repo root exactly as `POST /api/riff` does, reads `fabconfig.ReadPresetsOrdered(repoRoot)` and returns `200 {"presets":[{name, layout, paneCount}], "tiers":[...]}`. `presets` is in YAML source order (`layout` empty-string when unset; `paneCount` = number of preset panes; `[]` when none). **`tiers` is GATED on `fabconfig.IsFabProject(repoRoot)` (since `gsmu`)**: a fab project (`fab/project/config.yaml` present) gets `fabconfig.ReadTiers(repoRoot)` — the union of fab-kit built-ins (`default, doing, fast, operator, review`, `default` first) and the repo's `agent.tiers` keys; a repo with **no** config is NOT a fab project and gets `tiers: []` (a non-nil empty slice so the JSON key stays `[]`, response shape additive per §IX). The rationale is honesty: in a non-fab repo every tier resolves to the same `DefaultLauncher`, so tiers would be inert noise — the empty list drives the dialog to HIDE the Agent Tier field entirely. The **absent-vs-malformed split** is deliberate: an absent config = `[]`; a malformed-but-present config is still a fab project (`IsFabProject` true) whose `ReadTiers` falls back to the built-ins (`ReadTiers`'s own contract unchanged). The dialog still populates **both** its preset and Agent dropdowns from this **one** preflight fetch (no second endpoint, constitution §IV). A non-repo cwd / session-read failure → `400`. Read-only GET (§IX) |
| `/api/push/vapid-public-key` | GET | Returns the server's VAPID public key as `{"key":"<base64url>"}` for the frontend to pass as `applicationServerKey` to `pushManager.subscribe`. Lazily generates-and-persists the keypair (`~/.rk/vapid.json`, mode 0600) on first request. Server-independent (no `?server=`). `handlePushVAPIDPublicKey` in `api/push.go`. Only the public key is served — the private key never leaves the server (`260615-xd9r-web-push-notifications`) |
| `/api/push/subscribe` | POST | Stores a browser `PushSubscription` JSON body (`{endpoint, keys:{p256dh, auth}}`) into `~/.rk/push-subscriptions.json`, de-duped by `endpoint`. | `/api/notify` | POST | Fans out a Web Push to ALL stored subscriptions. Body `{title?, body}` (empty `body` → `400`, no send); builds the `{title, body, icon}` payload and sends each subscription via `webpush.SendNotificationWithContext` under a bounded context, pruning any subscription the push service answers `404`/`410`. | `/api/update` | POST | One-click toolkit upgrade (`260713-4zap-update-notify-one-click-upgrade`; force flag + shared spawn seam `260714-3law-force-update-restart-palette`; scoped-`shll update` remediation `260718-d15e-toolkit-manifest-update-notifications`). `handleUpdate` (`api/update.go`). **Tolerant body parse**: `{"force": bool}` — an absent, empty, `{}`, or even *malformed* body all decode to `force=false` (existing clients POST `{}` and keep working byte-for-byte; a decode error is swallowed, never a 400). **Remediation branches on whether `shll` is on PATH** via the `lookShllFn` seam (default `exec.LookPath("shll")`, fail-silent): **shll PRESENT → `handleShllUpdate` (SCOPED toolkit update)** — non-force: build the matched-tool argv from `s.updateChecker.Snapshot().Matched` (each `.Tool`); an EMPTY match set → `409 {"error":"no update available"}` BEFORE spawning (never spawns `shll update` with no args on the non-force path); force: skip the 409 and keep argv `["update"]` (a full-roster sweep, "update everything, I know better"). Then `202 {"status":"updating"}` and `spawnSelfFn(shllPath, "update.log", <args…>)`. `shll update` normalizes subset order to roster order and preserves run-kit's daemon-restart side effect by delegating to `rk update --skip-brew-update`. **There is NO brew-409 on this path** — a run-kit-not-brew daemon simply never matches its OWN row (checker §), while sibling tools stay updatable. After spawning (BOTH scoped paths, non-force + force) it schedules `s.updateChecker.RecheckAfter(postRemediationRecheckDelay = 2min)` (R17) so a siblings-only consumed match — which never restarts the daemon, so nothing naturally clears it — propagates as a cleared/changed verdict within minutes instead of the 6h tick; when run-kit was in scope the daemon restarts and the process-local timer dies with it (harmless). **shll ABSENT → `handleSelfUpdate` (run-kit-self fallback, unchanged pre-manifest behavior)**: (1) `resolveSelfPathFn` (default `selfpath.Resolve`) — resolve error `500`; (2) `!selfpath.IsBrewInstalled(selfPath)` → `409` pointing at the manual path (`update manually with `rk update`… or `brew install sahil87/tap/run-kit``) — this brew-409 applies ONLY here, and it also covers dev builds server-side; (3) unless force, an empty `Snapshot().Matched` → `409 no update available`; (4) `202` then `spawnSelfFn(selfPath, "update.log", "update")`. This path needs NO re-check — it always restarts the daemon, which resets state. The shared `spawnSelfFn(selfPath, logName, args...)` seam (see § API Server version/checker wiring → shared spawn seam) is now GENERALIZED to spawn a binary at ANY path (the shll binary on the scoped path, the self path on the fallback): a **detached** `exec.Command(path, args...)` with `SysProcAttr{Setsid: true}` and stdout/stderr → `~/.rk/<logName>` (via `openRkLog`). **Deliberately NOT `exec.CommandContext`-bound** — a detached child that must outlive the server cannot inherit its context, and §I's timeout rule only guards against a subprocess *blocking* the server; argument-slice construction + no user input still hold. **No in-flight lock**: a second click spawns again, exiting harmlessly once brew reports "already up to date". POST per §IX; no `GET /api/version` (minimal surface §IV) |
| `/api/updates/check` | POST | **On-demand update check** (`260720-n2ai-shll-check-updates-delegation-palette-checks`; source-parameterized github backend `260720-wb3n-github-source-patches-check`) — the deliberate, fail-LOUD counterpart to the ambient 6h loop, backing the two palette `run-kit: Check for Updates` commands. `handleUpdatesCheck` (`api/update.go`) parses a **tolerant body** `updatesCheckRequest{Source string}` (mirroring `updateRequest`'s posture — absent / empty / `{}` / malformed body, or an absent/empty `source` key, all mean the RELEASED default; existing clients POSTing `{}` are byte-unchanged) that selects the check backend by mapping onto the closed `updatecheck.Source*` enum (nothing user-controlled reaches argv — §I): the validated `"source":"github"` requests the github backend, and any OTHER successfully-parsed non-empty `source` → `400 {"error":...}` (fail-loud; a silent released fallback would mask a client bug) WITHOUT invoking the checker. It then runs ONE immediate inline pass via `s.updateChecker.CheckNow(r.Context(), source)`: the RELEASED default is the SAME exec code path the loop uses (updating the cached verdict and firing the SSE broadcast through `OnQualify`, so a manual notable finding lights the chip immediately: manual + ambient converge on ONE cached state), while `"github"` is a SIDE-CHANNEL query (exec + verdict computation + synchronous response only — the shared cached verdict and OnQualify/SSE broadcast are deliberately UNtouched, because the github contract has no notify policy and caching it would wipe a legit released chip and starve the scoped `shll update` argv — see § `internal/updatecheck`). The fresh verdict returns SYNCHRONOUSLY as `200` JSON in the SAME shape as the SSE payload (via the shared `buildUpdateAvailablePayload`, so the two can never drift), the response **echoing the report's self-identified `source`**. The ~1-2s exec latency is acceptable for a synchronous response; the checker's `checkTimeout = 30s` exec bound keeps the handler well under the 5s-block review rule's spirit for an upstream-tool call. **Failure mapping** (deliberately fail-loud, unlike the ambient loop): a nil OR suppressed checker (dev build) → `409 {"error":...}` (mirrors `/api/update`'s dev-posture 409; guarded via `Suppressed()` before `CheckNow`); a failed check (shll missing / non-zero exit — including an older shll without `--source` support — / unparseable or wrong-schema JSON) → `502 {"error":"update check unavailable — ..."}` carrying the reason so the client raises an honest error toast. No in-flight lock — mirrors `/api/update`'s no-lock posture (a concurrent pass is idempotent). POST per §IX (mutating: the released path updates the cache + broadcasts) |
| `/api/restart` | POST | Bounce the run-kit daemon from the web (`260714-3law-force-update-restart-palette`). `handleRestart` (`api/restart.go`), body ignored (client POSTs `{}`). Wraps the existing `rk daemon restart` CLI (Constitution III) so a routine restart / wedge recovery no longer needs SSH on the remote-first box. Branches: (1) **`409` when the running version is `"dev"`** (the `devVersion` sentinel, read from `s.version` — see the restart dev guard note) — under `just dev` the serve process is air-managed (not the daemon), so spawning `rk daemon restart` would bounce the *real* daemon out from under a dev tab; a defense-in-depth mirror of the palette-side dev gate that also stops a curl/stale-tab from doing it; (2) resolve the self path via the same `resolveSelfPathFn` seam — resolve error is `500`; (3) respond `202 {"status":"restarting"}` **before** spawning (the detached `rk daemon restart` kills THIS process, so — exactly like `handleUpdate` — the client must get its response first); then `spawnSelfFn(selfPath, "restart.log", "daemon", "restart")` (spawn failure logged only — response already committed). **NO brew requirement** (restart works for any install method) and no in-flight lock (a plain stop/start is idempotent; the daemon just released its own port). **Accepted caveat** (user-decided): if `daemon.Start()` fails after the stop, the web UI is down and SSH is needed — a narrow accepted failure window; `~/.rk/restart.log` makes it diagnosable. POST per §IX |
| `/api/servers` | GET | List available tmux servers — scans socket dir, returns JSON array of `{name, sessionCount, windowCount, rank}` objects sorted alphabetically. Session counts, the per-server window count, AND the per-server rank (`@rk_server_rank`, `*int` → JSON `rank: 3` / `rank: null` when unset, since `260705-bpnr-server-tiles-drag-reorder`) are computed together by the same concurrent fan-out (WaitGroup + mutex-protected results maps): each goroutine calls `tmux.ListSessions(ctx, server)` **and** `tmux.GetServerRank(ctx, server)` — one extra tmux call per server, same concurrency pattern. `windowCount` (JSON `windowCount`, the `WindowCount int` field on the `serverInfo` response struct) is the sum of each kept session's `SessionInfo.Windows` (`#{session_windows}`) over that server's `ListSessions` result — no extra subprocess, since it rides the same fan-out call that yields the session count; the sum works for unattached servers, and group copies are excluded because `parseSessions` already dropped them (§ `internal/tmux`). Per-server `ListSessions` errors log at warn and yield `sessionCount: 0` / `windowCount: 0`; per-server rank-read errors log at warn and yield `rank: null` — neither surfaces a 5xx. Empty discovery returns `[]` (not `null`). **The array order is unchanged — still `sort.Slice` alphabetical** (an asserted API contract, `servers_test.go`); `rank` rides each entry but display ordering is composed frontend-side (see § Frontend API Client → `compareServersRanked`) |
| `/api/servers` | POST | Create tmux server — JSON body `{"name":"..."}`. Creates session "0" in `$HOME`. Returns `201 {"ok":true}` |
| `/api/servers/order` | POST | Persist the user-defined server display order — JSON body `{"order":["srv-a","srv-b",...]}` (since `260705-bpnr-server-tiles-drag-reorder`). `handleServerOrderPost` (`api/servers.go`) decodes with `DisallowUnknownFields` (`nil` order → `[]`), validates EACH name via `validate.ValidateServerName` up front (`400` before any tmux write on malformed body or invalid name), then writes rank `i` to the i-th listed server via `tmux.SetServerRank` — **best-effort per server**: one unreachable server (killed mid-reorder, momentary timeout) logs a warn and is skipped, never failing the whole request (the no-5xx fan-out stance of `handleServersList`; the next full write self-heals). On success `initSSEHub()` + `sseHub.broadcastServerOrder(order)` (server-global echo, see § SSE Hub) and returns `200 {"ok":true}`. POST per §IX; mirrors `handleSessionOrderPost` minus the GET twin (rank already rides `/api/servers`) |
| `/api/servers/kill` | POST | Kill tmux server — JSON body `{"name":"..."}`. Returns `200 {"ok":true}` |
| `/api/keybindings` | GET | Curated tmux keybindings — runs `tmux list-keys` on `?server=`, filters through a whitelist map, returns JSON array `[{key, table, command, label}]`. Returns `[]` if server not running or on error |
| `/api/settings/theme` | GET | Returns `{"theme": "..."}` — reads via `settings.Load()`. Returns `"system"` when no settings file exists. Not per-server (no `?server=` param) |
| `/api/settings/theme` | POST | Accepts `{"theme": "..."}` — writes via `settings.Save()`. (Migrated PUT→POST by `260529-jad6` per §IX; body/response unchanged.) Returns `{"status": "ok"}` on success, `400` if theme is empty. Not per-server |
| `/api/settings/server-color` | GET/POST | Per-server color preference, stored in `~/.rk/settings.yaml` `server_colors:` (string descriptors, `internal/settings`). `GET ?server=x` → `{"color": "1+3"\|null}`; bare `GET` → `{"colors": {server: descriptor}}`. `POST` accepts `{"server":"...","color":"4"\|"1+3"\|null}` — `handleSetServerColor` validates the descriptor via the shared `validate.ValidateColorValue` (`400` on malformed) then `settings.SetServerColor` (null clears). String descriptors since `260615-6rnr` (was an int `{"color":N}`; tolerant read keeps legacy int files working). Not per-`?server=` |
| `/api/settings/instance-color` | GET/POST | **Per-instance accent color ("host color")**, a SCALAR setting stored in `~/.rk/settings.yaml` `instance_color:` (`internal/settings`; `260721-1etw-instance-accent-host-color`). Mirrors `/api/settings/server-color` **minus the `server` key** — the accent is one-per-instance, not a map. `GET` → `{"color": "4"\|"1+3"\|null}` (`handleGetInstanceColor` returns the **explicit setting only** — `null` means no accent renders; there is no derived default, see ui-patterns.md § Instance Accent). `POST` accepts `{"color":"4"\|"1+3"\|null}` — `handleSetInstanceColor` validates a non-null descriptor via the shared `validate.ValidateColorValue` (`400` on malformed, nothing persisted) then `settings.SetInstanceColor` (null clears). Mutation is POST-only per §IX. Not per-`?server=` (the accent identifies the whole run-kit instance, stored authoritatively on its host so every viewing device sees the same accent — Constitution §II filesystem state, no database) |
| `/api/boards` | GET | Lists pane boards summarized across every server returned by `tmux.ListServers(ctx)` (each board's pins are server-scoped; the list is the union of board names). Derived from `_rk-pin-*` session `@rk_board` vars (since `260602-qn62`). Returns `200 [{name, pinCount}]`; `[]` when empty (never `null`). Not per-server (no `?server=` query). **Rank-aware order (since `260708-a2qd-board-list-reorder`)**: `tmux.ListBoards` still returns alphabetical, but `handleBoardsList` then applies the user-defined display order at the API layer via the pure `sortBoardsByStoredOrder(boards, settings.GetBoardOrder())` helper (`internal/tmux` stays settings-unaware) — boards present in the stored order first, by their index in `~/.rk/settings.yaml` `board_order:`, then any board absent from it after them, alphabetically; stale names in the stored order (boards that no longer exist) match nothing and are ignored on read. **The response order IS the display order** for every consumer (sidebar BoardsSection, Host-page BOARDS zone, top-bar BoardSwitcher) — there is one list source, so this is the single sort choke point: NO `rank` field is added to the summary and NO client comparator is introduced (unlike servers, which have two list sources — see `/api/servers`). With no stored order the list stays alphabetical (unchanged behavior) |
| `/api/boards/order` | POST | Persist the user-defined board display order — JSON body `{"order":["deploys","reviews",...]}` (the FULL ordered board-name list, since `260708-a2qd-board-list-reorder`). `handleBoardOrderPost` (`api/boards.go`) decodes with `DisallowUnknownFields` (`nil` order → `[]`), validates EACH name via `tmux.ValidBoardName` AND rejects a **duplicate** name — a malformed body, an invalid name, or a duplicate is `400` before any write — then persists the whole list via `settings.SetBoardOrder`. On success `initSSEHub()` + `sseHub.broadcastBoardOrder(order)` (server-global echo, see § SSE Hub) and returns `200 {"ok":true}`. POST per §IX; mirrors `handleServerOrderPost`. Every reorder replaces the full stored list, so stale names self-heal. Unlike `/api/boards/{name}/reorder` (a within-board PIN reorder via `@rk_board_order` fractional keys), this reorders the BOARDS THEMSELVES in the board list — persisted host-globally in settings, scoped to no tmux server |
| `/api/boards/{name}` | GET | Returns the board's entries (one per `_rk-pin-*` session carrying this `@rk_board`) joined with live tmux window data: `[{server, windowId, session, windowIndex, windowName, orderKey, panes}]`, sorted by `orderKey`. **Response field shape unchanged** by `260602-qn62` — `session` is now the `_rk-pin-*` pin-session, transparent to the frontend. `{name}` validated against `^[A-Za-z0-9_-]{1,32}$` (`400` on invalid). A killed pinned window's session just drops out of the live read (no stale write-back). `200 []` when no entries match the name |
| `/api/boards/{name}/pin` | POST | Pin a window to a board. Body `{"server":"...","windowId":"@1234"}`. Validates `name`, `server` (via `validate.ValidateName`), and `windowId` (`^@\d+$`). Returns `404` when the named window does not exist on the named server. Idempotent — re-pinning the same window to the same board is a no-op. Returns `201 {"ok":true}` on success and broadcasts `event: board-changed { change: "pin" }` on the source server's SSE stream |
| `/api/boards/{name}/unpin` | POST | Unpin a window from a board. Body `{"server":"...","windowId":"@1234"}`. Returns `200 {"ok":true}`. Tolerant of "entry not present" (also returns `200`). Empty board cannot exist — when this removes the last entry, the board vanishes from `GET /api/boards`. Broadcasts `event: board-changed { change: "unpin" }` |
| `/api/boards/{name}/reorder` | POST | Reorder a pin within a board. Body `{"server":"...","windowId":"@1234","before":"@5678"\|null,"after":"@9abc"\|null}`. The new `orderKey` is computed server-side via `tmux.ComputeOrderKey(beforeKey, afterKey)`; the frontend never generates keys. Returns `200 {"ok":true,"newOrderKey":"bm"}` and broadcasts `event: board-changed { change: "reorder", orderKey }` |
| `/proxy/{port}/*` | * | Reverse proxy — forwards to `http://127.0.0.1:{port}/{path}`. Port validated (1-65535, `400` on invalid). Per-port `ReverseProxy` instances cached via `sync.Map`. Handles WebSocket upgrade transparently. `ModifyResponse` rewrites `localhost:{port}` and `127.0.0.1:{port}` references in HTML responses (`text/html` content-type) to `/proxy/{port}` paths; handles gzip-compressed responses. Non-HTML responses pass through unchanged |

**`broadcastServerOrder` — server-global fan-out (vs. per-server `broadcastSessionOrder`)** (since `260705-bpnr-server-tiles-drag-reorder`): the SSE hub gains `broadcastServerOrder(order []string)` (`api/sse.go`) alongside the existing `broadcastSessionOrder(server, order)`. The distinction is load-bearing and deliberate: **session** order is a per-server concern (which server's sidebar reorders), so `broadcastSessionOrder` fans only to that server's clients and caches per-server in `previousOrderJSON[server]`. **Server** rank order is a HOST-global concern — a client viewing one server, or NONE (the bare `/` Host page on the `?metrics=1` sentinel stream), still needs to re-sort its whole server list — so `broadcastServerOrder` fans to EVERY client across every `h.clients` key (exactly like the `metrics`/`services` broadcasts) and caches in a SINGLE `cachedServerOrderJSON` slot replayed to every new client in `addClient` (NOT gated on `c.server`). It normalizes a `nil` order to `[]` so the cached JSON is always `"[]"`, never `"null"`. This is why the design chose a fresh server-global event rather than reusing the per-server `session-order` shape — the latter would neither reach `?metrics=1` clients nor fit a host-global cache.

**`broadcastBoardOrder` — server-global fan-out (vs. per-server `broadcastBoardChanged`)** (since `260708-a2qd-board-list-reorder`): the SSE hub gains `broadcastBoardOrder(order []string)` (`api/sse.go`), a verbatim structural mirror of `broadcastServerOrder` — a board is an emergent cross-server aggregate of `_rk-pin-*` sessions with no owning tmux server, so board **display order** is a HOST-global concern (exactly like server rank order, and unlike the per-server `board-changed` pin/unpin/reorder event which fans only to one server's clients). It fans `event: board-order` to EVERY client across every `h.clients` key (incl. the `?metrics=1` sentinel) and caches in a SINGLE `cachedBoardOrderJSON` slot replayed to every new client in `addClient` (NOT gated on `c.server`), normalizing a `nil` order to `[]` so the cached JSON is always `"[]"`, never `"null"`. Payload `{"order":[...]}`. Fired synchronously by `handleBoardOrderPost` after the `settings.SetBoardOrder` write; it deliberately does NOT reuse the per-server `board-changed` event (which is scoped to a tmux server and uncached), since an order write is host-global.

**`broadcastStatusRefresh` — server-global, BROADCAST-ONLY (no cached slot, no replay)** (since `260715-nwla-status-refresh-feedback`): the SSE hub gains `broadcastStatusRefresh(completedAt time.Time)` (`api/sse.go`), fanning `event: status-refresh` with payload `{"completedAt":"<RFC3339 UTC>"}` (`completedAt.UTC().Format(time.RFC3339)`) to EVERY client across every `h.clients` key incl. the `?metrics=1` sentinel, under `h.mu.Lock()` with the same drop-on-full `slog.Warn` debounce as its siblings. A manual PR-status refresh is a HOST-global concern (both PR pollers are process-wide, not per-`?server=`), so it fans out like `broadcastServerOrder`/`broadcastUpdateAvailable`, NOT to one server's clients like `broadcastBoardChanged`. **Unlike server-order/board-order/version/update-available it is the sole broadcast fn with NO cached slot and NO `addClient` replay case** — a completion pulse is transient by design; a client connecting after a pass completes is NOT owed a replayed event because freshness for a late connector is surfaced independently by the StatusDotTip's "checked Xs ago" line (`PrFetchedAt`), so a missed pulse loses nothing. Emitted from `finishStatusRefresh()` (nil-guarded, once per completed pass — see the `POST /api/status/refresh` row above); the frontend routes it through `session-context.tsx`'s `subscribeStatusRefresh` fan-out to clear the PANE-header refresh button's spinner (ui-patterns.md § WindowPanel refresh button).

**`event: version` (set-once cached slot) + `event: update-available` (broadcast + cached replay)** (since `260713-4zap-update-notify-one-click-upgrade`): two more server-global cached slots on `sseHub`, both delivered to EVERY client across every `h.clients` key including the `?metrics=1` sentinel (fan-out identical to `server-order`/`board-order`), replayed on connect from `addClient` (after the server-order/board-order sends, both gated on a non-empty cached string; NOT gated on `c.server`). They differ in whether they broadcast:

- **`event: version`** — the RUNNING daemon version (ldflags `main.version`, sentinel `"dev"` for local builds), payload `{"version":"0.5.3","boot":"<per-process id>","brew":<bool>}` (the `boot`+`brew` fields additive since `260714-3law-force-update-restart-palette`), cached in `cachedVersionJSON`. Seeded ONCE via `sseHub.setVersion(version, boot, brew)` (called from `Server.SetVersion` after `NewRouterAndServer` — see § API Server version/checker wiring); the running version cannot change for the process lifetime, so there is **NO broadcast path** — it is a **replay-on-connect-only** slot (an empty version is ignored, leaving the slot empty → no event; `boot`/`brew` ride the same set-once slot). **`boot`** is a per-process identity generated ONCE at startup (16 hex chars from `crypto/rand` via `cmd/rk`'s `newBootID`), in-memory only (Constitution II); a *fresh* boot on every daemon start is what lets a reconnecting tab detect a **same-version** restart and reload (the reconnect after a restart is exactly the signal the frontend reload guard keys on — see ui-patterns.md § Update Notification → Reload guard). **`brew`** is `selfpath.IsBrewInstalled` computed ONCE at startup in `serve.go` (`resolveBrewInstalled`; a resolve failure reports `false` → the palette's brew-gated force-update entry safely stays hidden); it gates the client-side force-update palette entry. This is the sole version-exposure mechanism — deliberately no `GET /api/version` (minimal surface §IV); the SSE connect IS the moment the client needs it.
- **`event: update-available`** — the current toolkit-update verdict (`260718-d15e` generalized it from a single run-kit version to the matched-tool set; `260720-n2ai` extended each tool row to the FULL per-tool verdict), payload `{"tools":[{"tool":"fab-kit","current":"2.16.0","latest":"2.17.0","updateAvailable":true,"notable":true},…],"key":"fab-kit@2.17.0,run-kit@3.9.0","current":"","latest":"","source":"released"}`, cached in `cachedUpdateAvailableJSON`. The `tools` array now carries EVERY tool with a pending update — including sub-threshold `notable:false` rows — so the client can filter EITHER check view (default = `notable` only; incl.-patches = all `updateAvailable`); `key`/`current`/`latest` stay NOTABLE-derived (unchanged). **One shared builder** `buildUpdateAvailablePayload(verdict updatecheck.Result)` (`api/sse.go`) maps `verdict.Tools` onto `[]updateAvailableTool{Tool, Current, Latest string, UpdateAvailable, Notable bool}` (camelCase `updateAvailable`/`notable` per the rk payload convention) + `key`/`current`/`latest` + `source` (`verdict.Source`, appended LAST on `updateAvailablePayload` so existing byte-fragment assertions on `"current":…,"latest":…` adjacency stay valid) — serving BOTH `broadcastUpdateAvailable` and the `POST /api/updates/check` response so the two shapes can never drift. The ambient SSE slot therefore also carries `source:"released"`, which is harmless. `broadcastUpdateAvailable(verdict)` builds that payload, marshals it, sets the cache, and fans the frame to every client under `h.mu.Lock()` (drop-with-`slog.Warn` on a full channel). Empty until the first check changes the key. Invoked via the `Checker.OnQualify(Result)` callback wired in `serve.go`, which fires on ANY key change — so a newly-matching tool or newer latest re-broadcasts AND a **CLEARED verdict** (empty `tools`/`key`, fired when a match is consumed) is NOT skipped: it is broadcast and REPLACES the cached slot exactly like a populated one, so a tab connecting after a consumed-match clear replays the cleared state rather than a stale match. A late-connecting client gets the cached slot on connect (`replayGlobalSlots` special-cases nothing).

### Riff Engine Injection + Repo-Root Derivation

The `POST /api/riff` + `GET /api/riff/presets` handlers surface the extracted `internal/riff` spawn engine (full engine in [rk-riff](rk-riff.md)) (260713-sbk1-web-spawn-agent). Two seams are load-bearing:

**`RiffEngine` interface — a DEDICATED dependency, NOT folded into `TmuxOps`** (`api/router.go`): `type RiffEngine interface { Spawn(ctx, riff.Options) (riff.Result, error) }`, injected onto the `Server` struct as a nil-safe `riff RiffEngine` field mirroring the `metrics`/`services`/`prStatus` collector-injection pattern. `riff.Options` carries `{Server, Session, RepoRoot, Task, Preset}` plus the dialog-v2 spawn-shaping fields `{Where, WorktreeName, Tier}` (since `260714-q9cg`). Production wiring is `prodRiffEngine{}` (delegates to `riff.Spawn`); tests inject a focused mock via the new `NewTestRouterWithRiff(logger, sf, ops, engine, hostname)` constructor (its recorded-inputs mock also records `Where`/`WorktreeName`/`Tier`). **Why a separate field rather than a `TmuxOps` method**: `TmuxOps`/`mockTmuxOps` are shared by every handler test, so a spawn method there would force a mock method into dozens of unrelated tests; the dedicated field keeps the blast radius to the riff handler + its own mock. `NewTestRouter` leaves `riff` nil (riff-unrelated tests never reach it).

**New-field validation is at the handler, before repo-root derivation** (since `260714-q9cg`): `handleRiffSpawn` runs the full v2 validation ladder — `where` enum, `worktreeName`+`checkout` rejection, `validate.ValidateWorktreeName`, `validate.ValidateTier` — **before** `deriveRepoRoot` or any subprocess, so a malformed request `400`s with nothing created (constitution §I). See the `/api/riff` endpoint row above and [rk-riff](rk-riff.md) § Security / Trust Boundary. `handleRiffPresets` additionally reads `fabconfig.ReadTiers(repoRoot)` into the response so the dialog's Agent dropdown rides the one preflight fetch — **gated on `fabconfig.IsFabProject(repoRoot)` since `260714-gsmu-spawn-dialog-tier-gate-sidebar-entry`** (a non-fab repo, no `fab/project/config.yaml`, returns `tiers: []` so the dialog hides the Agent Tier field — see the `/api/riff/presets` endpoint row and [rk-riff](rk-riff.md) § `IsFabProject`).

**Repo-root derivation from the target session's active pane** (`deriveRepoRoot` in `api/riff.go`, shared by both handlers): `ListWindows(ctx, session, server)` → the active window (`IsActiveWindow`, else the first) → that window's active pane (`PaneInfo.IsActive`, else the first pane, else the window's `WorktreePath`) → `Cwd` → `config.FindGitRoot`. It returns `(root, cwd, err)` so a non-repo caller can name the offending cwd in its `400`. The three no-root outcomes are distinguished: a derived-but-non-repo cwd, a session with no window/pane to derive a cwd from (the practical nonexistent-session path — the real `ListWindows` swallows its tmux error into an empty result), and a tmux-read failure (surfaced as a `400` "does it exist?" message, since a named-session read failure is most likely a gone session, client-correctable). This uses the existing `ListWindows` surface — no new tmux primitive — and is session-scoped (not window-scoped) because the endpoint's spawn target is a session, not a window.

### Frontend API Client

`app/frontend/src/api/client.ts` — typed fetch wrappers for all endpoints using POST-only mutations with path-based intent. Uses relative URLs — works with both Vite proxy in dev and same-origin in production. Exports individual functions per endpoint:

| Function | Method | Path |
|----------|--------|------|
| `getHealth()` | GET | `/api/health` |
| `getSessions()` | GET | `/api/sessions` |
| `createSession(name, cwd?)` | POST | `/api/sessions` |
| `killSession(session)` | POST | `/api/sessions/:session/kill` |
| `createWindow(server, session, name, cwd?, rkType?, rkUrl?)` | POST | `/api/sessions/:session/windows` (session-scoped — no window ID yet) |
| `killWindow(server, windowId)` | POST | `/api/windows/{windowId}/kill` |
| `moveWindow(server, windowId, targetIndex)` | POST | `/api/windows/{windowId}/move` (source by ID, body `{targetIndex}`) |
| `moveWindowToSession(server, windowId, targetSession)` | POST | `/api/windows/{windowId}/move-to-session` |
| `renameWindow(server, windowId, name)` | POST | `/api/windows/{windowId}/rename` |
| `setWindowOptions(server, windowId, options)` | POST | `/api/windows/{windowId}/options` — partial-merge; `options` is `Record<string, string \| null>` (since `260529-jad6`) |
| `updateWindowUrl(server, windowId, url)` | POST | delegates to `setWindowOptions` → `/api/windows/{windowId}/options` (`{"@rk_url": url}`) |
| `updateWindowType(server, windowId, rkType)` | POST | delegates to `setWindowOptions` → `/api/windows/{windowId}/options` (`{"@rk_type": rkType === "" ? null : rkType}`). **Deletion candidate since `260714-t97o-web-view-lens`** — that change removed both view-switch call sites (the `IframeWindow` `>_` button and the `toggle-iframe-terminal` palette action / tty-branch hint bar), so zero non-test references remain (only its own `client.test.ts` case). Kept for now; the backend `POST /options` endpoint stays regardless (shared with `updateWindowUrl`, and `@rk_type` remains legitimate substrate state an external process may set) |
| `getDirectories(prefix)` | GET | `/api/directories?prefix=...` |
| `selectWindow(server, windowId)` | POST | `/api/windows/{windowId}/select?server=...` |
| `splitWindow(server, windowId, horizontal, cwd?)` | POST | `/api/windows/{windowId}/split` |
| `closePane(server, windowId)` | POST | `/api/windows/{windowId}/close-pane` |
| `reloadTmuxConfig()` | POST | `/api/tmux/reload-config?server=...` |
| `uploadFile(session, file, window?)` | POST | `/api/sessions/:session/upload?server=...` |
| `listServers()` | GET | `/api/servers` — returns `Promise<ServerInfo[]>` where `ServerInfo = { name: string; sessionCount: number; windowCount?: number; rank?: number \| null }`. Both `windowCount` and `rank` are optional (mirroring each other — the backend always sends them, but test fixtures may omit them): `windowCount` is the per-server total window count summed server-side from `#{session_windows}`; `rank` mirrors `@rk_server_rank` (`null`/absent when unset — unranked servers sort after ranked ones, added by `260705-bpnr-server-tiles-drag-reorder`). `ServerInfo` is exported alongside `listServers` from `app/frontend/src/api/client.ts`. All consumers (`SessionProvider`, `Sidebar`, `ServerPanel`, `ServerListPage`, `app.tsx` palette actions) read `.name` from each entry; the sidebar `ServerPanel` tile also reads `windowCount` (§ ui-patterns Sidebar `server-panel.tsx`) |
| `createServer(name)` | POST | `/api/servers` |
| `setServerOrder(order)` | POST | `/api/servers/order` — persists the user-defined server display order (backend writes rank `i` to the i-th listed server and broadcasts server-global `event: server-order`). **Server-independent** (like `listServers`/`createServer`/`killServer`) — the order spans the whole `/api/servers` list, not one server, so it takes NO `server` arg and hits the bare URL (no `withServer`). Added by `260705-bpnr-server-tiles-drag-reorder` |
| `killServer(name)` | POST | `/api/servers/kill` |
| `getKeybindings()` | GET | `/api/keybindings?server=...` |
| `getThemePreference()` | GET | `/api/settings/theme` |
| `setThemePreference(theme)` | POST | `/api/settings/theme` (migrated PUT→POST by `260529-jad6`) |
| `setServerColor(server, color)` | POST | `/api/settings/server-color` (migrated PUT→POST by `260529-jad6`) |
| `getInstanceColor()` | GET | `/api/settings/instance-color` — resolves `Promise<string \| null>` (the explicit descriptor, or `null` when unset — no accent renders; there is no derived default). Server-independent (no `?server=`), uses `deduplicatedFetch`. `260721-1etw` |
| `setInstanceColor(color)` | POST | `/api/settings/instance-color` — `Promise<void>`, body `{"color": string \| null}` (null clears); rejects on non-2xx via `throwOnError` so the caller can toast the `400`. Server-independent (no `?server=`), plain `fetch`. `260721-1etw` |
| `setWindowColor(server, windowId, color)` | POST | delegates to `setWindowOptions` → `/api/windows/{windowId}/options` (`{"@color": color === null ? null : String(color)}`; since `260529-jad6`) |
| `setSessionColor(session, color)` | POST | `/api/sessions/:session/color` |
| `setSessionOrder(server, order)` | POST | `/api/sessions/order` (migrated PUT→POST by `260529-jad6`) |
| `refreshStatus()` | POST | `/api/status/refresh` — kicks BOTH server-side PR pollers (viewer collector 90s + branch→PR refresher 30s) on demand (`260715-jykd-manual-status-refresh`; renamed/repointed from `refreshPrStatus()` → `/api/pr-status/refresh`). The server responds `202` immediately and runs the refreshes on a detached goroutine; refreshed statuses arrive via the SSE `sessions` stream (~2.5s cadence), never the response body. **Returns the tri-state 202 body (since `260715-nwla-status-refresh-feedback`)**: `Promise<{ status: "started" | "coalesced" | "throttled" }>` (exported `RefreshStatusOutcome` union) — parsed from `{"status": ...}` and **defaulted to `"started"` for any unknown/missing value** (an older daemon returns the opaque `{"status":"refreshing"}`, so defaulting to `started` = spin-until-event, the safe superset). Completion is NOT the promise resolution — it arrives as the server-global `status-refresh` SSE event; the button consumes both (branch the resolved status, then wait for the event). Server is the single frequency choke point (coalescing + min-interval throttle), so this is **safe to over-fire** — extra calls coalesce/throttle server-side and still 202. Best-effort / fire-and-forget (a non-2xx rejects via the shared `throwOnError`; the button swallows it). Server-independent (no `?server=`). Triggered by the PANE-header refresh button (§ ui-patterns → WindowPanel refresh button) and the `PR: Refresh Status` palette action |
| `triggerUpdate()` | POST | `/api/update` — one-click toolkit upgrade (`260713-4zap-update-notify-one-click-upgrade`). `Promise<void>`, no args, empty JSON body `{}`; **rejects on non-2xx** via `throwOnError` (so the chip/palette caller can surface the `409` reason as a toast). Server-independent (no `?server=`), plain `fetch` not `deduplicatedFetch` — follows the `refreshStatus`/`initTmuxConf` empty-body POST-helper idiom. The server responds `202` then spawns the scoped remediation (`shll update <matched…>` when shll is present, else the `rk update` self path — see the `/api/update` row); on a run-kit-in-scope update the ensuing daemon restart drops the state socket and the reconnect's differing `event: version` drives the frontend reload guard, while a siblings-only update clears via the post-remediation re-check's `update-available` key change. Imported into `session-context.tsx` and wrapped as the context `updateNow()` |
| `triggerForceUpdate()` | POST | `/api/update` with body `{"force":true}` (`260714-3law-force-update-restart-palette`). `Promise<void>`, no args; **rejects on non-2xx** via `throwOnError`. Same server-independent plain-`fetch` shape as `triggerUpdate`, but the `{"force":true}` body makes the server skip the empty-match 409, so a **patch release** — unreachable via the match-gated `triggerUpdate()` — is installable from the web (a full-roster `shll update` sweep when shll is present, else the brew-gated `rk update` self path). Wrapped as the context `forceUpdateNow()`; backs the `run-kit: Update Now` palette entry |
| `triggerRestart()` | POST | `/api/restart` with empty body `{}` (`260714-3law-force-update-restart-palette`). `Promise<void>`, no args; **rejects on non-2xx** via `throwOnError` (e.g. `409` on a dev build). Server-independent plain `fetch`. The server responds `202` then spawns a detached `rk daemon restart`; the reconnect's differing `boot` id (same version) drives the reload guard. Wrapped as the context `restartNow()`; backs the `run-kit: Restart Daemon` palette entry |
| `setPreviewScope(server, conn, expanded)` | POST | `/api/preview-scope` (via `withServer`) — declares the SSE connection `conn`'s expanded-session set so the poll captures previews only for those windows. Body `{conn, expanded}`. Called by `SessionProvider`'s context `setPreviewScope`; best-effort (errors swallowed) (`260701-70a0-session-window-tile-grid`) |
| `spawnRiff(server, session, opts?)` | POST | `/api/riff` (via `withServer`) — spawns a riff agent window in `session`'s repo. Signature changed by `260714-q9cg` to an **options object** `SpawnRiffOptions = {task?, preset?, where?, worktreeName?, tier?}` (was positional `task?, preset?`). Body is built by omitting each field when unset/**default** — `task`/`preset`/`worktreeName` when falsy, `where` when `"worktree"` (the backend default), `tier` when `"default"` (resolves the same tier as an omitted value) — so a **defaults-only call is byte-identical to the shipped two-field body**. `where` is the typed `RiffWhere = "worktree" | "checkout"` union. Resolves the parsed `RiffSpawnResult = {server, session, window, windowId}`. Throws via `throwOnError` on a non-ok response (a `400` carries a human-readable message, e.g. non-repo cwd). Consumed by the spawn-agent dialog (`260713-sbk1`, extended `260714-q9cg`) |
| `getRiffPresets(server, session)` | GET | `/api/riff/presets?session=<session>` (via `withServer` + `deduplicatedFetch`) — the dialog's **preflight**. Return type changed by `260714-q9cg` to `RiffPreflight = {presets: RiffPreset[]; tiers: string[]}` (was bare `RiffPreset[]`), tolerantly unwrapping the `{presets, tiers}` envelope (`presets ?? []`, `tiers ?? []`). `RiffPreset = {name, layout, paneCount}`. Throws on a non-ok response; the dialog treats a failure as "no presets, tier `default` only" and still allows a task-only spawn (`260713-sbk1`, extended `260714-q9cg`) |

All API functions (except `listServers`, `createServer`, `setServerOrder`, `killServer`, `getDirectories`, `getHealth`, `getThemePreference`, `setThemePreference`, `getInstanceColor`, `setInstanceColor`, `refreshStatus`, `triggerUpdate`, `triggerForceUpdate`, `triggerRestart`) append `?server={active}` via a module-level `setServerGetter()` mechanism. The `SessionProvider` sets the getter on mount. No multiplexed `action` field — each mutation is a separate function with its own URL path.

**Request deduplication**: A module-level `deduplicatedFetch` wrapper maintains a `Map<string, Promise<Response>>` of in-flight GET requests. When a GET to a URL already has an in-flight promise, the existing promise is returned (with `Response.clone()` so each caller can independently consume the body). POST/PUT requests always make fresh `fetch()` calls. Promises are cleaned up via `.finally()` on resolve or reject. All GET functions (`getHealth`, `getSessions`, `getDirectories`, `listServers`, `getKeybindings`, `getThemePreference`) use `deduplicatedFetch`; all mutation functions use plain `fetch`. Deduplication key is the full URL string (after `withServer()` appends `?server=`), so requests scoped to different tmux servers are not incorrectly merged.

## State Socket (`/ws/state`)

**One WebSocket per tab multiplexes every session-state + host-metrics stream** (`260716-qf3j-state-socket`) — a single established WebSocket carries what per-server + `?metrics=1` EventSource connections would otherwise. There is no `GET /api/sessions/stream` / `handleSSE` (D2). **Why**: SSE holds an HTTP/1.1 pool slot in EVERY browser engine and the pool caps at 6 per origin (spike `docs/findings/socket-pool-accounting.md`); a multi-server host held all 6 slots from SSE alone on plaintext origins, and on Firefox/WebKit a saturated pool **blocks new WebSocket handshakes entirely** — so terminal relays could never connect. An **established WebSocket holds NO pool slot** in any engine, dropping steady-state pool usage to ~zero and immune to multi-tab aggregation. A muxed *SSE* was rejected: it still holds one slot and needs out-of-band subscribe POSTs, reintroducing the POST-races-the-stream race class (memory: `relay-connect-select-alignment`). In-band subscribe frames are totally ordered with the events they gate, which also structurally fixes the long-standing `attachServer`→SSE race (memory: `multi-server-group-expand-async-race`, now the change's explicit acceptance test). Terminal relays ride a second WebSocket, `/ws/terminals` (`260717-803u-relay-mux`, see § Terminal Relay), kept SEPARATE from this socket (D6 — bulk binary terminal output must not share a send buffer/scheduler with state events). Chat rides THIS socket as a `kind:"chat"` subscription (`260717-vhvz-chat-on-state-socket`, see § chat kind below). Every route holds a fixed 2 WS + 0 SSE.

### Wire protocol (JSON text frames both directions)

`app/backend/api/state_ws.go` owns the envelope types + `handleStateWS`. Client → server ops: `hello` (once, first frame, carrying a client-generated `conn` id), `subscribe {kind, key?, server?, from?, req}`, `unsubscribe {kind, key?, server?}`, `preview-scope {server, expanded[]}`. (`clientMsg` gained `From int64` (`from`) for the chat kind, `260717-vhvz`.) Server → client frames:

- **`ack {req, snapshot?, offset?}`** — answers a subscribe. For `server`/`metrics` it carries the current `snapshot` (the same payload the SSE `event: sessions` / cached-metrics slot carried); `snapshot` is `json.RawMessage` (empty → `null`, tolerated). For a `kind:"chat"` subscribe it carries the tail-start byte `offset` (`ackFrame.Offset int64`, `omitempty`) and **NO snapshot** (`260717-vhvz`, D5 — the transcript came from the GET backfill).
- **`event {kind, key?, type, data}`** — a producer event. `data` is `json.RawMessage` embedded **verbatim** — byte-identical to the retired SSE frame's `data:` body (**contract-preservation rule**, load-bearing: today's SSE event names + payloads move into `type`/`data` unchanged, so every consumer above the `subscribe*` seams is untouched). Per-server events carry `kind:"server"` + `key`; host-global events carry `kind:"global"`; chat events carry `kind:"chat"` + `key:<windowId>` (`260717-vhvz`).
- **`gone {kind, key, reason}`** — replaces the SSE `event: server-gone` (§ dead-server reap below).
- **`error {req, message}`** — a malformed/unhonorable op; `req` echoes the offending op's `req` (0 when none). The socket stays live.

**Event catalogue** — the `type` string equals the retired SSE event name for every session/host type (`sessions`, `session-order`, `preview`, `board-changed` as `kind:"server"`; `metrics`, `services`, `server-order`, `board-order`, `version`, `update-available`, `status-refresh` as `kind:"global"`). Their producers, cached slots, poll cadence, `metricsOnlyServer` sentinel semantics, PR-status join, previews, and every `broadcast*`/`setVersion`/`setPreviewScope` helper are **identical** to the pre-change hub — see the § SSE Hub family below (Event-Driven SSE Loop, PR-Status Join, Session-Tile Previews, `broadcastServerOrder`/`broadcastBoardOrder`/`broadcastStatusRefresh`, version/update-available slots). **`kind:"chat"` (`260717-vhvz`) adds three types** — `chat` (`ChatEvent[]`) and `chat-state` (`{pending}`) byte-identical to the retired chat SSE, plus a NEW lightweight `chat-reset` (`{}`) rotation/shrink signal — driven NOT by the poll set but by a per-subscription producer goroutine (§ chat kind below).

### Hub edge refactor (`api/sse.go`)

The `sseClient` (single-server, channel of pre-rendered SSE bytes) generalizes to a per-connection **subscription set**: a `stateConn` holds `ch chan hubEvent`, `connID`, and `subs map[string]*sseClient` (one routing record per subscribed server key). **`hubEvent`** is the structured unit producers fan out — `{kind, typ, key, data}` plus a `gone bool` marker and a `raw []byte` escape hatch for pre-composed frames (the `ack`, and `error` frames) that must ride the SAME ordered channel as the subscription's events. The producer edge renders each `hubEvent` via `renderEnvelope()` into the JSON envelope; a parallel `hubEvent.String()` renders the legacy SSE-frame shape used ONLY by tests (deletion candidate — relocate to a test helper). **Every producer/collector/broadcast signature is unchanged** (decision: generalize the client edge, keep producers frozen — the whole machinery is proven, so only the send/route path changed).

- **Metrics subscription = the retained `metricsOnlyServer` sentinel as the internal registry key** (Design Decision 6, as **amended in rework** — the intake's original assumption-5 shape was NOT implemented). The wire protocol exposes `subscribe kind:"metrics"`, but `stateSubscribe` registers it internally under the reserved `metricsOnlyServer = "\x00metrics-only"` key — the same sentinel the retired `?metrics=1` stream used. This leaves `safetyIntervalEffective`'s coverage gate and ALL poll logic **untouched** (minimal diff; the fast-cadence-on-`/` behavior is verified by acceptance A-003). Only the sentinel's HTTP-routing branch inside `handleSSE` (the `?metrics=1` → sentinel mapping) was retired.
- **Server-key validation on the WS edge** (Constitution §I barrier preserved). The retired SSE edge validated the server via `serverFromRequest`; the WS edge restores it: `validate.ValidateServerName` guards `stateSubscribe`/`stateUnsubscribe`'s `kind:"server"` key (`api/sse.go`) and the in-band `preview-scope` op's `server` (`api/state_ws.go` calls `hub.emitError`). An invalid name / unknown kind gets an `error` frame carrying the offending `req` (routed through the send channel so ONLY the writer pump ever writes to the socket — gorilla forbids concurrent writes), never a silent drop. `sse.go`'s "validated by ValidateServerName" comment is truthful again.
- **Ack ordering** (rework cycle 2 fix — the load-bearing correctness property). `stateSubscribe` reads the ack snapshot (`previousJSON[key]` for a server, `cachedMetricsJSON` for metrics) **inside the SAME `h.mu` critical section that enqueues the ack**, AFTER `addClient` registers the routing record. This guarantees the ack's snapshot is ≥ every `sessions`/`metrics` frame already on the channel: a concurrent poll tick either ran before this lock (the read sees its value) or after the ack (the client's newest-wins apply is correct). Reading under an EARLIER lock — as the first cut did — let a poll tick enqueue a NEWER `sessions` event ahead of a stale-snapshot ack; the client applies the ack's snapshot last and `previousJSON` dedup then suppresses re-emission, stranding stale UI on a quiet server. Regression-tested by `TestStateWS_SubscribeAckNotStaleUnderPollInterleave` (proven to FAIL against the earlier-read shape, clean under `-race`).
- **Writer-pump cleanup** (rework cycle 1, mirrors `relay.go`). The per-connection writer pump drains `sc.ch` to the socket. On a `WriteMessage` failure it `cancel()`s AND sets a short read deadline (`stateWSCleanupWait = 100ms`) on the connection, so the read loop's parked `conn.ReadMessage()` returns promptly and runs `dropStateConn` cleanup instead of leaking the goroutine + its hub subscriptions until TCP teardown. The connection's lifecycle context is rooted at `context.Background()` (NOT `r.Context()` — the request context may be cancelled at the WS upgrade / hijack).

### Dead-server `gone` reap

The existing SSE poll-set reap on a dead-server fetch error (memory: `tmux-sessions` § SSE Poll-Set Lifecycle) now also fans an in-band `gone` frame: when `poll()` fetch returns `tmux.IsServerGone`, the loop-local `deadServers` collect, and the post-loop reap block sends `hubEvent{gone: true, key: server}` (rendered as `{"op":"gone","kind":"server","key":...,"reason":"server-exited"}`) to that server's subscribed connections before deleting it from every per-server map. A later re-subscribe re-registers the server cleanly. This is the `gone` frame's ONLY emit path (replaces the SSE `event: server-gone\ndata: {}` frame). Full reap mechanics + concurrency contract: `tmux-sessions.md`.

### chat kind — a per-subscription producer, NOT the poll set

Chat's live stream is a `kind:"chat"` subscription (`app/backend/api/chat_ws.go`; full contract in [chat](chat.md) § Live stream). It is deliberately **NOT** a poll-set member: transcript appends generate no tmux events (the recorded reason chat had a dedicated stream), so each subscription instead owns a **per-subscription producer goroutine** (`chatProducer`), tracked in a per-connection `chatProducers` map on `stateConn` (keyed `server\x00windowID`) that is **separate from `subs`** (the `h.clients`/poll routing records — Design Decision: a chat sub is a goroutine+cancel, not a fan-out record). A `chatResolver` function field on `sseHub` (default over `h.fetcher.FetchSessions` + `sessions.ResolveChatPane`, mirroring the `captureFn`/`fetcher` injection idiom) resolves the window's chat without giving the hub a `*Server`.

- **Subscribe** (`startChatSubscribe`): validates `msg.Key` (`ValidateWindowID`) + `msg.Server` (`ValidateServerName`) → `error` frame carrying `req` on failure (no producer). Following the **terminals-mux S2 pattern**, it registers a placeholder producer synchronously under `h.mu`, then does resolve+`Lookup`+ack in the producer goroutine (never on the socket read loop — a stalled `FetchSessions` must not freeze the connection's other ops). The ack carries `offset: from` + NO snapshot, enqueued before the producer's first emit (ack-before-first-emit). A repeat subscribe for the same key cancels+replaces the prior producer.
- **Producer** (`runChatProducer`): a TAIL/DORMANT machine. **TAIL** = an incremental `chat.Adapter.TailFrom(ref, from)` (the self-priming `Tail` was retired) emitting `Events`→`chat`+`chat-state`. **DORMANT** = on a ~2s `chatRefResolveInterval` re-resolve seeing a fresh ref (rotation) or a shrink `Reset`, it CANCELS the tail and does NOT re-tail from 0 (that would re-stream a whole conversation over the shared socket, D5), emitting a single `chat-reset` **only once the rotated-to transcript EXISTS** (`transcriptExists` probe); the fresh tail belongs to the client's re-subscribe. Lazy-transcript not-yet tolerance is preserved on initial subscribe AND rotation. A dropped `chat`/`chat-state` `hubEvent` under channel pressure sets `pendingReset`, flushed as one `chat-reset` when the channel drains (`sendConnLockedOK`/`flushPendingReset`).
- **Teardown**: the producer ctx is cancelled on unsubscribe, on `dropStateConn` (which cancels every chat producer + clears `chatProducers`), and on repeat-subscribe — no goroutine outlives its subscription (Constitution II). The `chat-error` (`{error}`) type is reserved client-facing protocol tolerance the producer never emits today (every failure converges via the subscribe-time `error` frame or DORMANT→`chat-reset`; `chatEventError` is a zero-emit deletion candidate).

### Frontend `StateSocket` client (`src/lib/state-socket.ts`)

One `StateSocket` per tab owns the `/ws/state` WebSocket. On open it sends `hello` (conn id via `crypto.randomUUID()`) then resubscribes every active subscription (each re-acks with a fresh snapshot — the reconnect recovery path); on drop it reconnects with **exponential backoff 1s → 15s cap**. It exposes `subscribeServer`/`unsubscribeServer`/`subscribeMetrics`/`unsubscribeMetrics` (idempotent, **ref-counted** by a stable id `"server:<name>"` | `"metrics"` so overlapping consumers — e.g. the current server plus an expanded sidebar group naming the same server — share one wire subscription), a `sendPreviewScope(server, expanded)` in-band twin, and `onEvent`/`onAck`/`onGone`/`onConnectionChange` callbacks that demux the envelope back into `(kind, type, key, data)`. It tracks a `reqToKey` map to route an `ack` back to its subscription's kind/key, and **drops the pending `reqToKey` entry on an `error` frame** so a rejected subscribe doesn't leak a row. Pure/testable (injectable conn id; the WS is the standard browser global). The **Vite dev proxy gained a `/ws` entry with `ws: true`** (`app/frontend/vite.config.ts`) so the upgrade is forwarded in dev. **Chat (`260717-vhvz`)** adds `subscribeChat({server, windowId, from})`/`unsubscribeChat({server, windowId})` (sub id `chat:<server>:<windowId>`, `from` on the subscribe frame) and dispatches `kind:"chat"` events + the chat ack `offset` to handlers; because chat's `from` is a stateful cursor a blind resubscribe would send stale, **chat is EXCLUDED from the `onopen` blind reconnect resubscribe loop** (kept out of `this.subs`) — the owner hook re-runs fetch→subscribe on reconnect instead (there is an OPEN-guard on the `req` recording). The chat seam is exposed to consumers through `session-context` (`subscribeChat`/`unsubscribeChat`/`registerChatHandlers`/`socketConnected`); the successor hook `use-chat-subscription.ts` holds no socket handle. See ui-patterns.md § Chat View and [chat](chat.md) § Chat View Frontend.

### `session-context.tsx` transport swap (seams preserved)

`session-context.tsx` replaces the per-server EventSource pool + the dedicated host-metrics EventSource effect with one `StateSocket` held in `socketRef` (survives effect re-runs / StrictMode remounts). `attachServer` and every `subscribe*` helper keep their exact signatures — no consumer above the seams changed. The `attachedSet` drives a diff effect that `subscribeServer`/`unsubscribeServer`s; a `metrics` subscription is opened when `attachedSet` is empty (the `/` Host case) and dropped when a server is attached (the host-global `metrics` event rides every server subscription). Acked snapshots + events route into the existing slice-update paths; version/update/order/preview/`setPreviewScope` behave identically, and `setPreviewScope` now sends **in-band** over the socket (no POST-races-the-stream window).

- **Connection dots = socket-connected AND subscription-acked** (with the existing 3s debounce). Per-server `isConnected` flips true on that server's subscription `ack` (mirrors the pre-change "first sessions event"); `ackedServersRef` tracks acked subscriptions and an `applyServerConnected` pass publishes `isConnected` on every socket connection-state change. `hostMetricsConnected` = the dedicated metrics subscription's debounced health when no server is attached, else true iff ANY attached server slice is connected (the host-global `metrics` event is delivering through that subscription). Reconnect nuance (nice-to-have): on socket re-open a previously-acked server flips Connected before its fresh re-ack lands (ms-scale window). See ui-patterns.md § connection dots / reload guard.
- **StrictMode safety** (rework cycle 2 MUST-FIX). `main.tsx` wraps in `<StrictMode>` (the real dev + e2e runtime), which double-mounts the provider. The socket-construction effect destroys+recreates the `StateSocket` across the remount, but the guard refs (`metricsSubscribedRef`, `subscribedServersRef`, `ackedServersRef`) survive in refs — so mount 2 would see its guards already true and never re-subscribe on the FRESH socket, permanently losing the metrics subscription on `/` (Host dot dead forever; when this tab is the hub's only client the poll loop never starts). Fix: the socket effect's **cleanup resets all three guard refs**, so the remount re-subscribes cleanly. StrictMode-wrapped unit tests cover metrics + server re-subscription.
- **`onGone` releases the subscription** (rework cycle 1). On a `gone` for a still-attached server, `onGone` deletes it from `ackedServersRef` + `subscribedServersRef` AND calls `socketRef.current.unsubscribeServer(key)`, releasing the StateSocket ref-count so the diff effect re-subscribes cleanly when `attachedSet` recomputes (via `onGone`'s `fetchServers`) and the server is still desired — no permanently-dead UI for a server the user restarts.

## Terminal Relay — `/ws/terminals` mux

**One `/ws/terminals` WebSocket per tab carries ALL pane relay streams.** Change `260717-803u-relay-mux` **retired `GET /relay/{windowId}` + `handleRelay`** (decision D2 — the frontend was the sole consumer, no API-compat contract; constitution IV) and replaced the per-pane relay socket with a single muxed connection: a board with N panes now holds ONE terminals socket instead of N, giving one reconnect path and one upgrade handshake instead of N. Combined with change 1's state socket the tab's steady-state connection budget is a **fixed 2 WebSockets** (`/ws/state` + `/ws/terminals`) and zero SSE. **Why**: this is connection hygiene (TCP count, handshake count, one backoff loop) — the user-facing HTTP/1.1-pool fix rode change 1 (an established WS holds no pool slot, but every extra WS *handshake* can block behind a saturated pool on Firefox/WebKit — spike `docs/findings/socket-pool-accounting.md`). Same port as the API, no separate relay port; `gorilla/websocket` + `creack/pty`.
