Handler in `app/backend/api/terminals_ws.go` (sibling of `state_ws.go`); `relay.go` retains only the shared `upgrader` + `forceTERM`, both consumed by the mux.

### Wire protocol (binary data frames + JSON control ops)

Lifted verbatim from the plan §Terminal socket. **Binary data frames `[u32 BE streamId][payload]`** in both directions (server→client PTY output, client→server keystrokes). **JSON text frames for control**:

- Client → server: `{"op":"open","id":<u32>,"server":..,"windowId":"@N","cols":<u16>,"rows":<u16>}`, `{"op":"resize","id":<u32>,"cols":<u16>,"rows":<u16>}`, `{"op":"close","id":<u32>}`.
- Server → client: `{"op":"opened","id":<u32>}`, `{"op":"closed","id":<u32>,"code":4004|4001|1000,"reason":..}`.

Stream IDs are **client-allocated u32s, unique within a socket connection** (the `open` op carries the client's chosen id). A malformed control frame is ignored (the socket stays live, forward-compat); an unknown op is ignored. **Today's WS close codes `4004`/`4001` become per-stream `closed` control events with the same code/reason — the SOCKET itself never closes for a stream-level failure** (`4004` = session pick (pin-session-first / ResolveWindowSession) or SelectWindowInSession failed / bad window ID; `4001` = `pty.StartWithSize` failed; `1000` = graceful client `close` op or PTY EOF).

### Per-stream lifecycle — reproduces `handleRelay` exactly, per stream

Each stream reproduces the retired `handleRelay` per-stream (same resolve → session-scoped select → direct attach → PTY pump). `startStream` runs on the socket read loop but does only cheap synchronous work there — validate the (already JSON-decoded) `windowId` via **`validate.ValidateWindowID`** (the same validator `decodeWindowID` wraps, so the REST and mux entry points share one validator and cannot drift — bug #205; the mux path needs no percent-decode since its id arrives decoded in JSON, not a URL segment) and **register a PLACEHOLDER stream (queue + closed chan, nil ptmx) under the connection mutex** — then dispatches the blocking tmux work to a goroutine (`attachStream`), so a resolve (≤5s) + select + `ReloadConfig` + attach never serializes behind other panes' keystrokes/opens (rework S2). The placeholder-first registration makes duplicate-id checks and racing resize/close ops deterministic (a resize/close arriving mid-attach finds the placeholder). `attachStream`:

1. **Picks the attach session with a pin-session-first preference** (`260718-co9z-link-based-board-pinning`) — a board-pinned window is LINKED into BOTH its home session AND its single-window `_rk-pin-*` pin-session, so the stream probes `HasSession` on the derivable `PinSessionName(windowID)` FIRST and attaches the pin-session when it exists; otherwise `s.tmux.ResolveWindowSession(ctx, server, windowID)` (5s timeout) resolves the window's HOME (non-pin) session. Attaching the pin-session (whose sole window is permanently active) gives the stream an independent current-window pointer and leaves the home session's active-window pointer untouched — merely viewing a pinned window never moves the home pointer. A missing/unresolvable window → per-stream `closed` 4004, socket open. (`ResolveWindowSession` no longer assumes "exactly one session" — under dual membership it re-resolves a `_rk-pin-*` naive result to the non-pin home; see `tmux-sessions.md` § Impact on Other Operations → `ResolveWindowSession`.)
2. **Session-scoped select** via `s.tmux.SelectWindowInSession(session, windowID, server)` scoped to whichever session step 1 picked — a bare `select-window -t @N` is ambiguous inside a tmux session group, so select and attach must agree on the same session (the group-ambiguity rationale carried over from the old `relay.go:88-99`; for a pin-session the select is a no-op in effect, its sole window already active, but the path stays uniform). Failure → `closed` 4004.
3. **Initial size rides the `open` op** — `pty.StartWithSize` at the open frame's `cols`/`rows` (falls back to 80×24 on zeros), **replacing the old wait-for-first-`resize`-message dance**. Best-effort `tmux.ReloadConfig(server)` first (true-color terminal-overrides on a foreign server), then `tmux [-L server] attach-session -t <session>` via `creack/pty` with `forceTERM` (TERM=xterm-256color). Attach failure → `closed` 4001.
4. **Publishes the attach into the placeholder under the lock** (if the stream was torn down mid-attach, the just-started attach is cleaned up rather than orphaned), then **enqueues `opened` onto the stream's OWN bounded queue BEFORE starting the PTY reader** (rework M2). Channel FIFO + the scheduler's short-frame priority then guarantees the client sees `opened` before the first data frame — the ordering the client's deferred-reset re-arm depends on (data-before-`opened` wiped the reset). A `closed` for a FAILED open rides a reserved control pseudo-stream (`controlStreamID = math.MaxUint32`), never a real pane id — a failed open produced no data, so its `closed` has no ordering concern.
5. **Per-stream cleanup** (client `close` op, PTY EOF, socket teardown): `sync.Once`-guarded cancel + ptmx close + attach-process kill, remove from the registry — exactly as `handleRelay`'s cleanup, no orphaned attach processes. Socket teardown tears down every stream.

### Write path — per-stream bounded queues + fair scheduler (D3, a v1 protocol requirement)

**Per-stream bounded send queue (`streamQueueDepth = 8` × `streamFrameSize = 4096B`) drained by a SINGLE writer goroutine** that schedules control/short frames (`shortFrameMax = 256B`; a keystroke echo) ahead of bulk output and round-robins across ready streams — **never FIFO across streams** (gorilla forbids concurrent writes, so all output funnels through this one writer). **This is a protocol requirement, not an optimization** (decision D3): spike 2 measured a shared FIFO at **1.66s** interactive echo p50 under a co-stream 1 Mbps flood vs **32ms** with per-stream queues + this scheduler at identical goodput (`docs/findings/relay-mux-hol.md`). The per-stream PTY reader is the queue producer; a **full queue PAUSES that stream's PTY reader** (backpressure into tmux's per-client buffering — the same mechanism a stalled per-pane TCP socket exerted before the mux) and **NEVER drops bytes** (dropping mid-stream corrupts VT state). The kernel TCP send buffer is the shared tail after the scheduler (default autotuning acceptable — the scheduler bounds everything above it). `writeFrame` is an **injectable seam** (production writes the socket; the HOL unit test substitutes a paced writer). *(Note: exact RR variant — plain vs deficit — is unobservable to the pinned test bound; D8 left it to apply. The shipped `drainReady` is a single short/control-priority pass with a round-robin bulk handoff per stream.)*

### Frontend — `RelayMux` singleton + `TerminalClient` port

Frontend consumes the mux via a `RelayMux` singleton (`app/frontend/src/lib/relay-mux.ts`) — see `ui-patterns.md` § Terminal Write Batching and § Terminal Relay (frontend). `terminal-client.tsx:813`'s `new WebSocket('/relay/...')` was the ONLY socket-creation site replaced; the stream handle is surfaced through the existing `wsRef` seam via a WebSocket-shaped adapter (`readyState`/`send`/`close`). Socket-level reconnect is owned by `RelayMux` (exponential backoff, one loop for the whole tab); a stream-level `closed` is handled per-pane (4004 → `onSessionNotFound` redirect; non-4004 → print `[reconnecting…]` + one probed re-open, else `[disconnected]`). RefreshButton remains the manual full-page recovery affordance.

**No startup sweep, no ephemeral** (unchanged from `260602-qn62`): the relay attaches directly to a durable session (the window's pin-session when pinned, else its home session) — there is no per-connection ephemeral relay session and no in-server session class to reap. See `tmux-sessions.md` § Terminal Relay.

### HOL scheduler Go unit test (`terminals_ws_test.go`)

`TestScheduler_EchoNotHeadOfLineBlocked` ports the spike harness with **no real network**: the scheduler is wired to a paced `writeFrame` (sleeps ∝ bytes written), stream A floods 4096B frames, a stream-B echo frame is enqueued, and the test asserts B is written within a small **bounded number of A frames** (pins the observable non-FIFO fairness bound, not the exact RR algorithm). Relay behaviors are re-asserted per-stream against `/ws/terminals`: `opened` precedes the first data frame (`TestTerminals_OpenedPrecedesData`, pinning M2), initial-size attach + TERM forcing (`_InitialSizeAndTERM`), `resize` sets the PTY size (`_ResizeSetsClientSize`), client `close` → `closed` 1000 (`_ClientCloseYields1000`), bad/missing window → `closed` 4004 with the socket still open (`_BadWindowIDClosed4004`/`_MissingWindowClosed4004`), and `-race`-clean across the terminals+scheduler suite.

## Daemon Lifecycle

The Go binary manages its own daemon lifecycle via the top-level `rk daemon` subcommand tree (sibling of `rk serve`, not nested under it). The daemon runs in a dedicated tmux server (socket `rk-daemon`, session `rk-daemon`, window `serve`) — separate from the `runkit` server used for agent sessions. The session name matches the socket name so the combined exact-match target (`=rk-daemon:=serve`) cannot collide with user-facing sessions via tmux prefix matching. `LegacySessionName = "rk"` is consulted only by `Stop`/`Restart` (via `runningSessionCtx`, which checks `SessionName` first then falls back to the legacy name) so a daemon started by a pre-rename binary can still be stopped cleanly during the first upgrade. Daemon helpers live in `internal/daemon/`; the CLI surface lives in `app/backend/cmd/rk/daemon*.go` (one file per subcommand: `daemon.go` parent, `daemon_start.go`, `daemon_stop.go`, `daemon_restart.go`, `daemon_status.go`, plus `daemon_portowner.go` for the shared port-owner helper).

- `rk daemon start [--force]` — start daemon (errors if already running)
- `rk daemon stop [--force]` — graceful shutdown via C-c to the tmux pane, with a mode pre-cancel and a force-kill fallback (see `Stop()` sequence below); prints `rk daemon not running` and exits 0 when no session exists
- `rk daemon restart [--force]` — idempotent: stop existing daemon (the full `Stop()` sequence below — mode pre-cancel → C-c → wait up to `stopGracePeriod` 12s for graceful exit, an independent grace-deadline timer sized to cover the inner serve's ~10s worst-case shutdown — see `internal/daemon` row; a session that vanished on its own counts as a clean stop, and a C-c that fails to deliver now degrades to `kill-session` rather than wedging) then start new one; starts fresh if no daemon running
- `rk daemon status [--json]` — read-only report of daemon state (running / not running, socket, session, window, target) AND port owner (free / held by the daemon / held by another process). `--json` emits a structured machine-readable form (`daemon.{running,socket,session,window,target,pid}` + `port.{host,port,state,holder_pid,holder_command}`)
- `rk update` — auto-restarts daemon after successful `brew upgrade` using `RestartWithBinary(brewBinPath)` where `brewBinPath` is `<brewPrefix>/bin/run-kit` derived from the resolved `/Cellar/run-kit/` path (resolves to the new Cellar version post-upgrade, avoiding stale `os.Executable()` path from the running process; the `run-kit` bin/Cellar identity since `260709-gidk-swap-canonical-cli-name-run-kit`). Operates at the Go API layer, not the CLI surface

`rk serve` is foreground-only: it accepts no `-d`/`--restart`/`--stop` flags (daemon lifecycle lives entirely under `rk daemon`), so invoking those surfaces cobra's standard `unknown flag` error. (`260528-5zvv-rk-daemon-cli-restructure`)

**Naming collision note**: `rk daemon status` is distinct from `rk status` (the top-level tmux session summary in `cmd/rk/status.go`). The collision is sibling-namespaced — cobra disambiguates cleanly — but `rk daemon status --help` includes a one-line note pointing this out so users typing `rk status` expecting daemon info land at the right command.

**`--force` semantics** — consistently "override the safety check that prevents claiming the port from a non-rk-daemon owner":

- `rk daemon start --force` — lazy / on-error. The happy path is identical to the non-forced path (`daemon.Start()` → port-probe). Only when `Start()` returns the port-in-use error does the command look up the port owner, refuse to kill if the holder identifies as the rk daemon (`daemon.InnerServePID()` match), otherwise SIGTERM the owner with graceful-then-forceful escalation, and retry `Start()`.
- `rk daemon stop --force` — stop the daemon first (if running), then regardless of step 1's outcome probe the port. If still held by a non-daemon process, SIGTERM it. If the port is free at probe time, exit 0 silently (no `Killed port owner` line). If the holder identifies as the rk daemon itself, exit non-zero with a "manual investigation needed" message.
- `rk daemon restart --force` — stop the daemon if running, then proactively probe the port BEFORE the start step. Any non-daemon holder is SIGTERMed (with graceful-then-forceful escalation) before `daemon.Start()` is called.

`rk daemon status` is read-only and does NOT accept `--force` — passing it produces cobra's `unknown flag` error.

**`Stop()` sequence** (`internal/daemon/daemon.go`, resolved-session target `targetFor(session)` throughout so the legacy `rk` name is handled): (1) **mode pre-cancel** — `copy-mode -q` runs FIRST, before the C-c send, best-effort (a failure is `slog.Debug`-logged and never aborts `Stop()`). This defends against a root-cause wedge: a pane left in tmux copy-mode does NOT receive C-c as a literal key — tmux looks the key up in the mode key table (`copy-mode` binds `C-c` → `send-keys -X cancel`, a non-read-only command) and dispatches that binding through the session's only attached client, run-kit's own read-only `-CC` control bridge (attached with `-r` — see the `internal/tmuxctl` production dial), which tmux rejects with `client is read-only`, so the interrupt never reaches the serve process. `copy-mode -q` returns the pane to normal mode so the subsequent send injects C-c literally; it is idempotent (exit 0 when the pane is not in a mode — `-q` since tmux ≥3.2), so it runs unconditionally on every `Stop()`. (2) **C-c send** — `send-keys ... C-c` triggers graceful shutdown; on failure it MUST NOT early-return (an `slog.Warn` fall-through) so the grace-timer → `kill-session` fallback below stays reachable on any graceful-delivery failure. Returning the wrapped send error instead would wedge `Stop()` and everything layered on it (`rk daemon restart`, `rk update`'s `RestartWithBinary`, `POST /api/restart`) even though the force-kill would have stopped the daemon. (3) **grace-timer → kill-session** — the independent `stopGracePeriod` (12s) timer + `stopPollInterval` (200ms) polls (each under a fresh `cmdTimeout` context, per the per-command-context discipline documented in the `internal/daemon` row); the full grace is still waited before the kill even when the C-c send failed (no shortened-grace special case). A session that vanished on its own by kill-time — or after a `kill-session` that errored — is the success outcome (returns nil); only a session still alive after a failed kill surfaces an error.

Binary resolution: `Start()` uses `os.Executable()` + `filepath.EvalSymlinks()` (works for the standard `rk daemon start` / `restart` paths where the running binary is valid). `StartWithBinary(path)` accepts an explicit binary path and resolves its symlinks (used by `update` after `brew upgrade` deletes the old Cellar directory). Both delegate to shared `startSession(exe)` for tmux session creation.

**Server-birth CWD pin — the highest-leverage seam** (`260720-ji0k-pin-server-birth-cwd-home`): `startSession`'s `new-session` BIRTHS the rk-daemon tmux server, so it runs via `runTmuxInDir(ctx, tmux.ServerBirthDir(), args...)` — a dir-carrying variant of the shared `runTmux` helper (which delegates with an empty dir), preserving the file's `cmdTimeout` + stderr-capture pattern while landing `cmd.Dir` on the actual `exec.CommandContext`. This pins the daemon server's CWD to `$HOME` (fallback `/`) regardless of where `rk daemon start` ran. It is the highest-leverage of the four birth seams because `rk serve` runs inside this session and **every later server birth inherits `rk serve`'s CWD** — without this pin, an `rk daemon start` from a git worktree that is later deleted parks the daemon server (and thus every downstream server) on a dead inode, silently breaking new-pane `-c` chdir on tmux 3.7. The daemon session's env is unchanged (only CWD is pinned — `config.Load` needs the `RK_*` env; see the `internal/tmux` module row). Full failure-mode analysis and the shared `tmux.ServerBirthDir()` helper: `tmux-sessions.md` § Server-Birth CWD Pin.

Detection: `tmux -L rk-daemon has-session -t =rk-daemon` (anchored `=` prefix forces exact-match — see PR #196). `runningSessionCtx` consults `=rk-daemon` first, then falls back to `=rk` for transparent stop/restart of pre-rename daemons. No polling loop, no signal files, no supervisor script.

**Port-based liveness probe**: Before `Start()`/`StartWithBinary()` create the tmux session — and AFTER the `IsRunning()` check passes — they call `guardPortAvailable()`, which loads `config.Load()` and runs `net.DialTimeout("tcp", host:port, 400ms)` against `RK_HOST:RK_PORT`. Wildcard/empty hosts (`""`, `"0.0.0.0"`, `"::"`, `"[::]"`, `"[::1]"`) substitute `127.0.0.1` via `probeHost()` — dialing `0.0.0.0` itself is platform-inconsistent and not a reliable liveness signal. If the dial succeeds (something is listening), `Start` returns an error containing the substrings `already serving on`, `not under the rk-daemon`, and `RK_PORT` so scripts can pattern-match. Cobra `RunE` propagates the non-zero exit. This closes the split-brain detection gap where a foreground `rk serve` was invisible to the tmux-only `IsRunning()` check.

**Stale-socket reaping**: When `IsRunning()` is false AND the port probe passes, `Start`/`StartWithBinary` call `reapStaleDaemonSocket(ctx)` which invokes `runTmux(ctx, "kill-server")` — scoped strictly to `serverSocket = "rk-daemon"` (never the agent-session `runkit` server). Idempotent: tmux's "no server running" surface on cold start is the common case. Errors are logged at `slog.Debug` and never block startup; if anything is genuinely broken, the subsequent `startSession` surfaces it. This self-heals the orphaned-socket state left when an inner serve dies on a port collision.

**Startup logging via `RK_DAEMON_LOG`**: `startSession` resolves `os.UserCacheDir()/rk/daemon.log` (e.g. `~/.cache/rk/daemon.log` on Linux, `~/Library/Caches/rk/daemon.log` on macOS) via `resolveDaemonLogPath()` and passes it to the inner `tmux new-session` via `-e RK_DAEMON_LOG=<path>`. The serve startup's `setupSlog(level)` reads the env var, `os.MkdirAll(filepath.Dir(p), 0o755)`, opens the file with `O_APPEND|O_CREATE|O_WRONLY` (mode 0o644), and wraps `io.MultiWriter(os.Stderr, file)` so slog output is teed to both the tmux pane (preserves `tmux attach` debugging) and a durable log file. Open failures fall back to stderr-only with one `slog.Warn("daemon log unavailable", ...)`; `UserCacheDir()` failure in `startSession` spawns the inner serve without the env var (single `slog.Warn` upstream). Logging is best-effort — never blocks daemon creation. Constitution §VI compliance: the log is a passive append-only artifact, no supervisor, no signal file, no liveness derivation from contents.

The exported constant `daemon.LogEnvVar = "RK_DAEMON_LOG"` is the single source of truth (consumed by both `internal/daemon/startSession` and `cmd/rk/serve.go/setupSlog`).

**Port-owner lookup (`daemon_portowner.go`)**: shared helper used by all four `rk daemon` subcommands. `findPortOwner(ctx, host, port) (*PortOwner, error)` queries who is listening on the configured TCP port via `lsof -ti:<port>` (primary), falling back to `ss -tlnp '( sport = :<port> )'` when `lsof` is unavailable or errors. Both queries are port-only — the `host` argument is pass-through for display (both tools correctly cover loopback and wildcard binds). Holder command is resolved via `/proc/<pid>/comm` on Linux, `ps -p <pid> -o comm=` on macOS. Returns `(nil, nil)` when nothing is listening; `(nil, error)` only when both tools fail. The companion `terminateOwner(ctx, owner)` mirrors `daemon.Stop`'s graceful escalation: `syscall.Kill(pid, syscall.SIGTERM)` → 200ms polling for exit via `syscall.Kill(pid, 0)` up to a 5s grace period → `syscall.Kill(pid, syscall.SIGKILL)` on timeout. Signal delivery uses `syscall.Kill` directly — never a shell `kill` invocation. All subprocess calls (`lsof`, `ss`, `ps`) use `exec.CommandContext` with a 5s `context.WithTimeout` per Constitution §I. `var findPortOwner = findPortOwnerImpl` is overridable in tests so CLI tests drive `--force` paths without spawning the real tools.

**Holder-identity check (`daemon.InnerServePID()`)**: small helper in `internal/daemon` that returns the PID of the `rk serve` process running inside the daemon tmux pane, derived from tmux's `pane_pid` format spec via `tmux -L rk-daemon list-panes -t =rk-daemon:=serve -F '#{pane_pid}'` (a new `runTmuxOutput` internal captures stdout where `runTmux` would have discarded it). Returns `(0, error)` when the daemon session is absent or the tmux query fails. Used by every `--force` code path and by `rk daemon status` to recognize the daemon as the port owner — when `owner.PID == innerServePID`, the port is classified as held by us (no signal sent in `--force`; `held-by-daemon` state in `status`). The CLI layer wires this through a package-level `var innerServePIDFn = daemon.InnerServePID` so tests can drive the self-recognition branch.

## tmux Control-Mode Subscription (`internal/tmuxctl`)

Package `app/backend/internal/tmuxctl/` owns the long-running `tmux -CC` control-mode subscriptions that drive sub-500ms SSE freshness. It is the **only sanctioned bypass** of the `internal/tmux/` boundary — every other tmux interaction goes through the request-response helpers in `internal/tmux/tmux.go` with their 10s `context.WithTimeout`. The bypass exists because a single long-lived subscription is structurally incompatible with the `exec.CommandContext`-plus-timeout shape of `internal/tmux/`. The package's `doc.go` documents the boundary explicitly.

### Core types

- **`Client`** (`client.go`) — one PTY-backed `tmux -CC` subscription per tmux server (identified by socket name). Runs `tmux [-L <socket>] -CC attach-session -t =<bootstrap> -r` via `creack/pty.Start` (the `-r` flag puts the connection in read-only mode — see Design Decision below). The `=`-anchored target prevents prefix-match collisions, matching the convention established in PR #196. A single goroutine reads lines via `bufio.Scanner` and dispatches them through `ParseLine`. Public surface:
  - `Open(ctx, socket, sink) (*Client, error)` — non-blocking; errors only on initial PTY allocation or process start failure.
  - `Close() error` — idempotent; cancels the Client's context, kills the subprocess, terminates the reconnect loop.
  - `Generation() int64` — atomic per-server counter incremented on every handled notification.
  - `Wait(after int64) <-chan struct{}` — returns a channel closed once generation > after. Single-use; callers re-call after each consumed event.
- **`Supervisor`** (`supervisor.go`) — owns `map[socket]*Client` guarded by `sync.Mutex`, plus an `fsnotify.Watcher` on the watch directory. Resolves the watch dir from `TMUX_TMPDIR` if set, else `/tmp/tmux-<euid>/`; missing directories are created via `os.MkdirAll(dir, 0o700)` and watched as sockets appear. `Start(ctx)` enumerates existing sockets synchronously (so the SSE hub never races an empty Client map for sockets that already exist on disk) and then runs an fsnotify event loop. Re-creating a socket of the same name closes the prior Client before opening a new one. `Stop(ctx)` closes every Client and the watcher; bounded 5s in production. `Get(socket) *Client` is the lookup used by the SSE bridge.
- **`EventSink`** (`event_sink.go`) — consumer interface with 8 callbacks (`OnSessionWindowChanged`, `OnWindowAdd`, `OnWindowClose`, `OnWindowRenamed`, `OnSessionsChanged`, `OnLayoutChange`, `OnConnectionLost`, `OnConnectionEstablished`). All callbacks dispatch from a single goroutine — the Client's read loop. Sink implementations MUST NOT block. The production sink in `api/tmuxctl_bridge.go` (`hubSink`) is active since `260530-v6hm-active-window-event-derivation`: it records per-group active-window state into a per-Client `ActiveWindowTracker` (see § SSE Hub Bridge). The SSE hub still observes *change* via the per-server generation counter (that path is untouched); the sink's tracking is an additive side effect that supplies the Tier-1 active-window signal to the fetch path. `NoOpSink` is exported for tests, PTY-unavailable scenarios, and as the degraded sink a `nil` SinkFactory produces.
- **`ParseLine(line string) Event`** (`parser.go`) — pure function (no I/O, no time dependence). Recognises the six relevant tmux 3.6a notifications (`%session-window-changed`, `%window-add`, `%window-close`, `%window-renamed`, `%sessions-changed`, `%layout-change`) and framing markers (`%begin`/`%end`/`%error`). `%output` and `%unlinked-window-*` are silently dropped. Unknown notification names return `UnknownEvent{Raw}` and log `slog.Debug` exactly once per unique name (surfaces protocol additions without log noise). Malformed input returns `MalformedEvent{Raw}` — never panics.

### Reconnect FSM

When the PTY read loop encounters EOF or any error other than a Close-driven context cancellation, the Client calls `sink.OnConnectionLost()` exactly once, tears down the subprocess (`cmd.Process.Kill()` if still running, `cmd.Wait()` to reap), waits a backoff, then retries `pty.Start`. The backoff sequence is `initialBackoff = 250ms` → `500ms` → `1s` → `2s` → `5s` → `5s` … capped at `maxBackoff = 5 * time.Second`. The backoff resets to `initialBackoff` on the first non-`%begin` event after a successful reconnect (see `client.go` `handleEvent`). Reconnect retries continue indefinitely until `Close()` is called. Test injection points: `dialFn` and `sleepFn` are swappable so the FSM can be exercised with stubbed I/O and a fake clock.

### Anchor session (`_rk-ctl`)

`tmux -CC` requires an attached session to emit notifications. `resolveBootstrap` (in `client.go`) **always** creates a hidden anchor session named `_rk-ctl` via `tmux [-L <socket>] new-session -d -s _rk-ctl` — unconditionally on every observed server, not only when the server is empty (changed by `260602-a1wo-prevent-exit-empty-server-death`; the anchor is now a permanent **session floor** that keeps the server's session count above zero so tmux's `exit-empty` cannot reap it — see § Constitution Alignment §VI below and `tmux-sessions.md` § `_rk-ctl` Anchor). The anchor is tagged with the server-scoped user-option `@rk_ctl_keepalive 1` via `set-option -t =_rk-ctl @rk_ctl_keepalive 1` (constant `tmuxctl.AnchorKeepaliveOption = "@rk_ctl_keepalive"`). The tag is a defensive marker only — v1 has no runtime consumer, but it allows future code to identify the anchor without depending on the literal session name. A "duplicate session" error from `new-session` (concurrent `rk serve` created the anchor first) is treated as benign by `isDuplicateSessionError` and the Client proceeds to attach. The anchor's `new-session` is built by the extracted `anchorCommand(ctx, socket)`, which pins `cmd.Dir = tmux.ServerBirthDir()` (the server-birth CWD pin — the anchor's `new-session` is birth-capable) and `cmd.Env = tmux.CleanEnvForServer()` (the same env sanitization `CreateSession` uses, closing the second birth-path asymmetry) while preserving the stderr-capture-into-error `isDuplicateSessionError` relies on (`260720-ji0k-pin-server-birth-cwd-home`; see `tmux-sessions.md` § `_rk-ctl` Anchor). **Floor vs. attach target are decoupled**: the anchor is always created (the floor), but the control-mode attach target still prefers the first existing real session (`firstSessionName`, which now skips `_rk-ctl` so the always-present anchor is not picked), falling back to `_rk-ctl` only when no real session exists. The anchor is hidden from user-facing surfaces via `tmux.ControlAnchorSessionName` — see `tmux-sessions.md` § `_rk-ctl` Anchor for the filtering chokepoints, the `exit-empty off` backstop, and the explicit-kill-only lifetime contract.

### SSE Hub Bridge (`api/tmuxctl_bridge.go`)

The `api` package owns the bridge between `tmuxctl.Supervisor` and the SSE hub. Three artefacts:

- **`WindowChangeSubscriber`** (interface defined in `api/sse.go`) — the interface the hub uses to receive per-server change notifications. Methods: `Generation(server string) int64` and `Wait(server string, after int64) <-chan struct{}`. Generation semantics mirror `tmuxctl.Client`: every observed notification increments the counter; `Wait(after)` returns a channel closed once `generation > after`.
- **`supervisorSubscriber`** — the production adapter. Forwards `Generation` and `Wait` calls to `Supervisor.Get(server).Generation()` / `.Wait(after)`. When no Client exists for a server (PTY-unavailable host, socket not yet allocated), `Wait` returns a **never-closing** channel via `neverChan()` so `selectFirst` falls through to the safety-net timer rather than busy-looping `FetchSessions`. Exported via `NewSupervisorSubscriber(sup)`.
- **`hubSink`** — the production EventSink, one per Client, built by the `SinkFactory` returned from `NewHubSinkFactory()` (the `Supervisor` calls the factory per socket, passing that socket's own `ActiveWindowTracker` — see § Active-Window Event Derivation below; `NewHubSink()` was removed by `260530-v6hm`). Beyond the generation-counter path (which the Client bumps itself, before invoking the sink, so the hub still observes *change* via `Wait`), `hubSink` records active-window state into its tracker: `OnSessionWindowChanged(sid, wid)` resolves `sid`→group via the tracker's cached map (O(1), no subprocess) and records `wid` as that group's active window (latest-event-wins; an unresolved `sid` is dropped for tracking, never errors/blocks); `OnSessionsChanged` refreshes the `$sid`→group map; `OnConnectionEstablished` re-seeds the tracker (refresh map + seed Tier 1 from current `#{window_active}` per group). The two re-seed callbacks issue read-only tmux queries that could block, so they are **offloaded to a goroutine** (the read loop returns immediately — honoring the EventSink "MUST NOT block" contract); the tracker's concurrency-safety makes a slightly-delayed refresh racing an event harmless. The read-only query seams (`listSessionGroups`/`listActiveByGroup`) are injectable struct fields so tests stub them without spawning tmux. The remaining callbacks (`OnWindowAdd`/`Close`/`Renamed`/`OnLayoutChange`/`OnConnectionLost`) stay no-ops.

`Server.SetWindowChangeSubscriber(sub)` materialises the lazy SSE hub (`initSSEHub`) and stores the subscriber. Safe to call before any SSE client connects. `Server.SetActiveWindowProvider(provider)` (since `260530-v6hm`) injects the Tier-1 `ActiveWindowProvider` (the Supervisor) into the production `prodSessionFetcher` so the REST + SSE fetch paths derive `isActiveWindow` from control-mode events; it is a no-op when the fetcher is a test-injected fake, keeping the seam optional.

### Active-Window Event Derivation

The active-window highlight is **event-derived per session group** rather than read from the base session's `#{window_active}` pointer alone. The base pointer goes stale whenever an attachment moves the active window while another group member keeps an independent active-window pointer — historically the per-WebSocket `rk-relay-*` ephemeral, and still `rk riff` / an external `new-window`; reading the base pointer produced the wrong-highlight bug. This whole derivation subsystem (`internal/tmuxctl/*`) was scoped *investigate-only, NOT deletable* by `260602-qn62-move-based-board-pin-sessions` (it is driven by the `_rk-ctl` anchor and serves the SESSIONS highlight independent of boards) and is **left untouched** — note that `260602-qn62` removed the `rk-relay-*` ephemeral, so the relay is no longer one of the stale-pointer sources, but the subsystem's internal comments still reference relays (out of scope for that change). The fix corrects the *read signal* — it does not change any window creator. (260530-v6hm-active-window-event-derivation)

**Tracker** (`internal/tmuxctl/active_window.go`) — `ActiveWindowTracker` is a concurrency-safe, in-memory (Constitution §II) store for ONE server, owned by one `Client` (the read-loop goroutine is the sole writer; the fetch path reads). Two `sync.RWMutex`-guarded maps: `byGroup` (group name → active `@wid`, latest-event-wins via `Set`, bulk re-seeded via `SeedGroups`) and `sidGroup` (`$sid` → group, resolved via `ResolveGroup`, refreshed wholesale via `ReplaceSidGroups`). `Get`/`Snapshot` are the read accessors.

**Ownership/wiring** — `NewSupervisor(factory SinkFactory)` takes a `SinkFactory` (a `nil` factory degrades every Client to `NoOpSink` — control-mode observed only via the generation counter, no tracking). `Supervisor.openSocket` allocates a fresh tracker per socket and binds the sink to it (a close-then-reopen gets a new tracker so stale state never leaks across the gap — `OnConnectionEstablished` re-seeds it). `Supervisor.ActiveWindow(server, group) (wid, ok)` is the server-keyed read accessor — a server with no Client, or a group with no tracked entry, returns `("", false)` so the caller falls back to Tier 2. The Supervisor satisfies `sessions.ActiveWindowProvider` directly. Wired in `cmd/rk/serve.go`: `tmuxctl.NewSupervisor(api.NewHubSinkFactory())`, then after `Start` both `SetWindowChangeSubscriber(NewSupervisorSubscriber(supervisor))` and `SetActiveWindowProvider(supervisor)`.

**Two-tier derivation** (`internal/sessions/sessions.go`) — `FetchSessions(ctx, server, provider)` threads an `ActiveWindowProvider` (nil ⇒ Tier-2-only, exactly today's behavior). Per session it queries `provider.ActiveWindow(server, sessionName)` — the user-facing session name IS the group key after `parseSessions` filtering. **Tier 1 (authoritative):** when a tracked `@wid` exists, the pure helper `applyActiveWindow(windows, trackedWid)` marks exactly the matching window active and clears the rest, overriding the parsed `#{window_active}` flag. **Tier 2 (fallback):** no tracked entry ⇒ the base-pointer flag from `parseWindows` stands. Tier 1, once set, is authoritative — the base pointer never overrides it; external clients (iTerm/Ghostty) also emit `%session-window-changed`, so "latest event wins" subsumes them with no override path. `applyActiveWindow` also enforces the single-highlight-per-session invariant and falls back to Tier 2 for a session when the tracked `@wid` matches no live window (e.g. closed between event and fetch) rather than highlighting nothing. The fetcher reaches `FetchSessions` via `prodSessionFetcher` (holding the provider) in `api/router.go`. Frontend auto-follow needs no change — the existing `app.tsx` URL-writeback effect navigates once the corrected `isActiveWindow` arrives via SSE; board panes pin explicit window IDs and never read it.

### Event-Driven SSE Loop

`app/backend/api/sse.go` refactored its per-server snapshot loop from a 2.5s ticker to an event-driven `select` with a 12s safety-net backstop. Three constants govern the cadence:

| Constant | Value | Role |
|----------|-------|------|
| `safetyPollInterval` | `12 * time.Second` | Backstop when a `WindowChangeSubscriber` is wired (production). Heals missed events across reconnect gaps; primary freshness driver is the Client's `Wait` channel. |
| `legacyPollInterval` | `2500 * time.Millisecond` | Used when no subscriber is wired (PTY-unavailable startup, unit tests). The snapshot-rebuild cadence is then the only freshness guarantee. |
| `metricsPollInterval` | `2500 * time.Millisecond` | Cadence for `metrics.Collector` host CPU/memory polling. Deliberately decoupled from the SSE intervals so metrics sampling frequency is not coupled to the SSE event/safety cadences. |
| `prStatusPollInterval` | `90 * time.Second` | Cadence for `prstatus.Collector`'s single batched `gh` call (`260610-596o-pr-status-sidebar`). Deliberately slow (~40 calls/hr vs. the 5000/hr authenticated limit) — the SSE hot path reads the cached snapshot, never `gh`, so PR-status freshness is decoupled from the SSE cadence; on-demand `POST /api/status/refresh` covers the "I want it now" case (`260715-jykd`; was `POST /api/pr-status/refresh`). |

`sseHub.safetyIntervalEffective()` picks `safetyPollInterval` when `subscriber != nil`, else `legacyPollInterval` — preserves correctness for the PTY-unavailable case and for tests exercising the hub without a control-mode driver.

The loop body (`poll` + `waitForNext` + `selectFirst`) blocks on a `select` over (a) one `subscriber.Wait(server, perServerGen[server])` channel per active server (only when a subscriber is wired), (b) one **wake** channel per polled server (always — see below), and (c) `time.NewTimer(safetyIntervalEffective())`. When a subscriber fires, the winning server's prior generation is refreshed and the server is marked event-driven so the next iteration invalidates its 500ms `cache` entry and observes the post-mutation tmux state immediately. Non-winning servers are peeked non-blockingly so their backlog isn't replayed unnecessarily. `selectFirst` reads `timer.C` in the outer select to avoid the goroutine leak that would otherwise occur if a subscriber wins the race and the timer goroutine blocked on `timer.C` forever (`Stop` does not deliver on `C`). Heartbeat is wall-clock-based (`sseHeartbeatPeriod = 15 * time.Second`) — wall-clock cadence prevents the slower safety interval from starving heartbeats.

**Per-server wake seam** (`sseHub.wake(server)`) — a second freshness driver alongside the control-mode subscriber, for mutations tmux control mode never announces. User-option writes (`@color`, `@session_color`, `@rk_url`, `@rk_type`, `@rk_marker` — `set-option`) emit **no** `tmux -CC` notification (the tmuxctl parser handles only session/window add/close/rename/active-window/layout events), so before the wake seam these mutations repainted only on the 12s safety tick (0–12s, mean ~6s — the reported color-apply lag). `wake(server)` closes the server's entry in a `wakes map[string]chan struct{}` guarded by a **dedicated `wakeMu`** (separate from `h.mu` so a mutation handler never contends on the poll lock): a closed channel means a wake is pending. It is non-blocking, safe from any goroutine, and coalescing — a double `wake` before consumption is a no-op via `select { case <-ch: default: close(ch) }` (never a double-close panic); N wakes before consumption trigger 1..N passes (redundant passes suppressed by the `previousJSON` dedup). Two `wakeMu`-guarded helpers serve `waitForNext`: `wakeChannel(server)` returns the current (lazily-created) channel to add as a wait case, and `consumeWake(server)` retires a *closed* channel by replacing it with a fresh open one and reporting `true` — the replace happens BEFORE the next fetch, so a wake landing between observation and fetch closes the fresh channel and triggers one more pass (**at-least-once**, never a busy-loop). `waitForNext` builds a wake case for **every** polled server **independent of `h.subscriber`** (tagged `waitCase.isWake`), so wakes work even when `subscriber == nil` (unit-test hubs, PTY-unavailable hosts) — the old early timer-only return for the nil-subscriber path is gone. After `selectFirst` unblocks, a single non-blocking peek over all cases routes each fired case by `isWake`: a wake win calls `consumeWake` and, only when it retires a pending wake, sets `eventDrivenServers[server] = true` (so `poll()` invalidates the 500ms fetch cache and the woken pass observes post-mutation state, not a stale cached fetch) — it never touches `perServerGen`/`Generation()` (every `h.subscriber` deref is guarded, so a wake-only path with `subscriber == nil` never nil-panics); a subscriber win keeps its existing bookkeeping unchanged. The tmuxctl bridge, `supervisorSubscriber.Wait`'s `neverChan()` contract, and the timer/coverage machinery are untouched — the seam is purely additive within `sseHub`/`waitForNext`/`selectFirst`. Effect: user-option mutations repaint every consumer (sidebar rows, session tiles, boards, all tabs) within one poll pass — sub-second, since the tmux write has already landed when the wake fires. Call sites: `handleWindowOptions` (`windows.go`, `POST /api/windows/{windowId}/options`) and `handleSessionColor` (`sessions.go`, `POST /api/sessions/{session}/color`) each run `s.initSSEHub(); s.sseHub.wake(server)` after a successful tmux write and before the `{"ok": true}` response — no wake on validation failure or tmux error (the handlers return early), no API-contract change. Mirrors the established `handleSessionOrderPost` wake-after-write pattern. **Known limitation**: the dead-server reap block deletes `perServerGen`/`eventDrivenServers`/`h.cache`/`h.clients` for a gone server but NOT `h.wakes[server]`, so the `wakes` map can slowly grow with churning ephemeral server names (a per-server closed/open `chan struct{}` — small; not yet reaped). (`260718-xpur-hub-wake-option-mutations`)

### No Killed-Window Board Cleanup Diff (removed)

Since `260602-qn62-move-based-board-pin-sessions`, the SSE hub no longer detects killed windows to clean up board membership. The old `detectKilledWindowIDs(prev, current) []string` pure function, the per-server `sseHub.previousWindowIDs` tracking, the per-tick window-kill cleanup loop, and the `BoardEntriesFetcher.RemoveAllByWindowID` dependency are all **deleted**. Board membership is derived live from `_rk-pin-*` sessions, so a killed pinned window's pin-session simply drops out of the next `ListBoardEntries` read — the frontend's refetch on the next session-list change picks it up. There is also no `@rk_board` first-poll bootstrap broadcast (`broadcastBoardBootstrap`/`boardBootstrapPayload`/`previousBoardJSON` removed) and no cached-board send on `addClient`. `BoardEntriesFetcher` is now a one-method interface (`ListBoardEntries`) kept only so tests can stub the tmux dependency; `broadcastBoardChanged` (pin/unpin/reorder) remains and the `"cleanup"`/`"bootstrap"` change strings are gone.

### PR-Status SSE Join

The SSE hub attaches live PR status to **any window with a derived `PrURL`** on each poll via a PURE in-memory read — the 2.5s hot path makes ZERO network/`gh` calls (the `gh` cost lives entirely on the collector's 90s background tick, the branch→PR refresher's 30s tick, and the on-demand `POST /api/status/refresh` — which kicks BOTH, since `260715-jykd`). Since `260705-dmex-generic-agent-state-tier` the change-bound gate is gone: `PrURL` is derived from the pane's branch (§ Branch→PR Derivation), so PR status now appears for any pane on a branch with an open PR, not only fab-change-bound windows. (260610-596o-pr-status-sidebar)

**Seam + wiring**: `PRStatusSnapshotter` (one method, `Snapshot() map[string]prstatus.PRStatus` — URL-keyed, since PR numbers are only unique per repo, in `api/sse.go`) is implemented by `*prstatus.Collector` and held on the hub (`sseHub.prStatus`). `newSSEHub(fetcher, mc, svc, pc)` takes it as the fourth arg; `NewRouterAndServer` constructs `pc := prstatus.NewCollector(prStatusPollInterval); pc.Start(ctx)` next to the metrics collector, stores it on `Server.prStatus`, and `Server.initSSEHub` passes it through — but as a true nil interface when `s.prStatus` is nil (the explicit `var pc PRStatusSnapshotter; if s.prStatus != nil { pc = s.prStatus }` wrap avoids the typed-nil-interface trap so the hub's `h.prStatus == nil` check actually fires). A nil `prStatus` degrades gracefully (no PR fields attached) — used by tests and unwired routers.

**`attachPRStatus(sess []sessions.ProjectSession)`**: called in `poll()` AFTER the 500ms session-cache write (so the cached snapshot slice stays free of mutable PR fields conceptually, though it operates on the same slice by reference). For every window it FIRST resets the **collector-only** fields (`PrChecks/PrReview/PrIsDraft` → zero, `PrFetchedAt` → nil since `260715-nwla-status-refresh-feedback`) so a window that lost its PR (merged/closed → dropped from the snapshot) clears cleanly even on a cached result slice; **`PrState` is deliberately NOT reset here** — it is dual-sourced (the branch-derived `MapBranchState` fallback seeded upstream by `enrichWindowPR`), so it survives a collector miss and is overridden below only on a collector hit. THEN, gating only on a **non-empty `PrURL`** (`w.PrURL == nil || *w.PrURL == ""` → skip; the `FabChange` gate was **dropped** by `260705-dmex-generic-agent-state-tier` per R7), it looks `*w.PrURL` up in the URL-keyed `Snapshot()` and copies `State/Checks/ReviewDecision/IsDraft` onto the window, plus `PrFetchedAt = &fetchedAt` where `fetchedAt := st.FetchedAt` — a per-hit copy of the snapshot value scoped to the loop body, so taking its address yields a stable pointer independent of the range variable. `PrFetchedAt` (`prstatus.PRStatus.FetchedAt`, stamped `now` on each collector rebuild) is thus collector-join-owned exactly like the `PrChecks`/`PrReview`/`PrIsDraft` siblings — set on a URL hit, nil on a miss (a URL-miss/empty/nil-`PrURL` window carries no stale freshness timestamp) — and is surfaced as the StatusDotTip's ambient "checked Xs ago" line (ui-patterns.md § Status Dot hover-card). The join key is the **canonical PR URL, never a bare number** — numbers are unique only per repo, so a number join can pick up an unrelated repo's PR state (the collision the URL-keying fixed). No-op when `h.prStatus == nil`. `PrURL`/`PrNumber` are NOT touched here — since `260705-dmex` they come from the branch→PR enrichment in `internal/sessions` (`enrichWindowPR` → register + snapshot-join against the `prstatus` branch refresher), upstream of the hub.

### Branch→PR Derivation

`PrURL`/`PrNumber` are **derived server-side from the pane's git branch**, no longer joined from `fab pane map` (Constitution §X — PR links are derivable, not pushed). This surfaces PR status for **any** pane on a branch with an open PR, in any repo under any workflow — not only fab-change-bound windows. (260705-dmex-generic-agent-state-tier)

**Two layers, both network-isolated from the SSE hot path:**

1. **Background `BranchRefresher`** (`internal/prstatus/prstatus_branch.go`): resolves each registered `(repoDir, branch)` → PR via `gh pr list --head <branch> --state all --json number,url,state,updatedAt` (run in the repo via `cmd.Dir`, `exec.CommandContext` + `ghTimeout` + explicit argv — §I), on a 30s tick (`branchPRRefreshInterval`, mirroring `Collector.Start`'s immediate-warm-then-tick lifecycle). It gates on ONE availability probe per pass (`checkAvailable` — the `ghAvailable` verdict is cached positive AND negative for 60s so an unauthenticated gh never re-probes per pair), keeps the last-good entry on a transient exec/network error OR malformed JSON (true stale-while-revalidate — never fail-to-negative), records a **successfully parsed empty/no-PR result as a valid negative** (`nil pr` — clears the entry directly; no grace/negative-stamp retention), and ages out pairs no longer observed after 5m. `pickBranchPR` selects by **precedence — open > merged > closed** (`branchStateRank`, case-insensitive), most-recently-updated within a class, skipping URL-less nodes and returning `nil` for an empty/all-skipped array. **Before the per-pair gh call, the refresher applies the default-branch exclusion** (§ Default-Branch Exclusion below): a pair whose branch equals the repo's default branch is resolved to an authoritative negative with no gh call at all. Started in `router.go` via `prstatus.DefaultBranchRefresher.Start(ctx)` next to the viewer-wide collector.

2. **Hot-path register + snapshot-join** (`internal/sessions.enrichWindowPR`): the FetchSessions loop does ZERO network work — it `prstatus.Register(repoDir, branch)`s the observed pair (a cheap lock-guarded set touch) and `prstatus.SnapshotBranchPR(repoDir, branch)`s the last-good derived PR from the in-memory snapshot, assigning `WindowInfo.PrURL`/`PrNumber`. The window's `(repoDir, branch)` is `windowBranchRepo`'s choice: the active pane's cwd/branch, else the first pane with a resolved branch.

**D2 merged durability — state-all + precedence, stateless/restart-proof** (revised by `260706-4h26-durable-merged-pr-register-keys`; status-pyramid.md § Open Decisions — D2): the earlier `260706-y1ar` shape (`--state open` lookup + a `branchPRMergedGrace` 10-min grace clock on a `wentNegativeAt` field) DROPPED a PR the moment it merged, then leaned on an in-memory grace window to keep serving the last-known PR so the purple/orange **done-square** survived. That grace clock **decayed the merged square into a green fab square minutes after merge** and was **wiped by any rk restart** (in-memory state, Constitution II). The revised model derives durability **from `gh` directly, statelessly**: the branch query is now `--state all` (§ prstatus package row + layer 1 above), so a merged PR keeps resolving to a positive result on **every** refresh pass — `pickBranchPR` ranks it by precedence (open > merged > closed) and serves it as the last-good entry. There is **no grace clock to expire and none to wipe on restart** — a cold `BranchRefresher` (fresh process, no prior positive) serves the merged PR on its first pass, so the done-square is durable **statelessly and restart-proof end-to-end**. `refresh` now clears the entry directly on a successfully parsed empty/no-PR result (a true negative) and keeps last-good only on a transient exec error or malformed JSON (stale-while-revalidate) — the `branchPRMergedGrace` const, the `wentNegativeAt` field, and the grace/negative-stamp retention branch in `refresh` were **deleted**. The viewer-wide collector (which queries OPEN/MERGED/CLOSED) supplies the merged `prState` via the URL join, so the dot shows the done-square; a **closed-unmerged** PR (still derived for the register/tip) has its fall-back to the live fab tier handled **frontend-side** (`statusDotState`'s `prOwnsDot` drops PR ownership for `prState === "closed"` — see [ui-patterns](/run-kit/ui-patterns.md) § Status Dot D2). The **branch-reuse edge**: an open PR always outranks an older merged PR on the same branch (state precedence beats recency across classes), so a reopened branch's live PR wins.

**Default-Branch Exclusion — no branch-PR derived for a default-branch pane** (`260718-0vuz-skip-branch-pr-default-branch`): a pane parked on its repo's **default branch** never gets a branch-PR derived — `Snapshot`/`SnapshotBranchPR` returns `(nil, false)`, so `enrichWindowPR` leaves `PrURL`/`PrNumber`/`PrState` unset and the pane panel renders no `pr` row (the StatusDot falls through to the lower fab/agent/tmux tiers). The branch→PR feature links *feature* branches to *their* PRs; a default branch never "has its own PR" in that sense — every `gh pr list --head <default>` match for it is degenerate (a fork PR whose head ref is named `main`/`master`, or an old same-repo PR whose head happened to be the default branch). Because the derivation is stateless and durable (`--state all`, open > merged > closed precedence, no grace clock — D2 above), such a degenerate match would otherwise re-resolve positive every 30s pass forever, restart-proof. Excluding the default branch removes the whole degenerate class in one move — no per-PR heuristics (`isCrossRepository` cross-repo/fork filtering was deliberately rejected: it removes only the fork variant and leaves the same-repo-historical variant in place).

- **Refresher-only, hot path unchanged**: the exclusion lives in `BranchRefresher.refresh()`, applied per pending pair **before** the gh call. `Register`/`Snapshot` stay dumb zero-subprocess set-touches (default-branch pairs still register); recognition happens on the background tick, honoring the documented zero-subprocess SSE hot-path invariant (Constitution §II/§X). An excluded pair makes **no `gh pr list` call** (saves a subprocess/network round-trip per pass).
- **Authoritative negative, not skip** — clears a stale positive: an excluded pair sets its entry's `pr = nil` directly (exactly like a genuinely-empty parsed result), overwriting any previously-cached PR. This is what makes a live stale line disappear within one refresh tick — e.g. a fork-PR match cached for `main` before the exclusion applied (or before `origin/HEAD` resolved) is cleared on the next pass, never stale-kept by the stale-while-revalidate rule. Treating the exclusion as a transient skip would keep serving the wrong PR indefinitely, defeating the fix.
- **Branch-scoped, not repo-scoped**: only the pair whose branch matches the default is excluded; a feature-branch pair in the same repo resolves normally via `gh pr list`.
- **Local, network-free default-branch detection** (`branchDefaultExec` seam + `parseDefaultBranch`): `git symbolic-ref refs/remotes/origin/HEAD` run in `repoDir` (`exec.CommandContext` + `ghTimeout` + explicit argv, `cmd.Dir = repoDir` — no user input in argv, §I; a local ref read, never the network). `parseDefaultBranch` strips the `refs/remotes/origin/` prefix + surrounding whitespace (`refs/remotes/origin/main` → `main`); missing-prefix or empty output is a parse failure. `branchDefaultExec` is a package-var seam mirroring `branchPRExec`, defaulted onto the per-instance `defaultExec` field in `NewBranchRefresher` so tests stub it — the third injectable seam alongside `exec`/`available`.
- **Per-repo, TTL-cached, fail-open** (`defaultBranch(ctx, now, repoDir)` + `defaultBranchEntry` + `branchDefaultBranchTTL = 5m`): the lookup runs on the refresher goroutine only and is cached per `repoDir` (the `defaultBranches` map, `mu`-guarded), so each repo costs at most one `git symbolic-ref` per TTL window regardless of pair count — never one per pair per pass (mirrors the `availValid`/`availAt` gh-availability cache). BOTH outcomes are cached with a taken-at timestamp: a resolved name (`ok=true`) and a **fail-open failure** (`ok=false` — `origin/HEAD` unset/never-initialized, no `origin` remote, git absent/error, unparseable output). On `ok=false` the pair falls through to the normal `gh pr list` path (current behavior), so a missing local ref does not silently disable the feature repo-wide; caching the failure verdict avoids a per-pass `git symbolic-ref` retry storm. The default-branch resolution runs **outside** the `mu` critical section (like `r.exec`), so a hung `git symbolic-ref` never blocks `Register`/`Snapshot`; the entry write takes the lock. No persistent state (Constitution §II). `sessions.go` (`enrichWindowPR`) is untouched — an excluded pair simply misses the snapshot join, indistinguishable from "no PR exists".

This is the T007/T008 **rework shape** (from `260705-dmex`): the original apply resolved `gh` inline in the enrichment loop, which broke `api/sse.go`'s zero-network-call hot-path invariant and code-review.md's 5s cap; review flagged it must-fix and it was restructured to register-off-tick + snapshot-join. The `prstatus` viewer-wide collector (URL-keyed live state/checks/review) is untouched and composes exactly as before: derive `PrURL` here → `attachPRStatus` joins live status by that URL.

The old **`FabChange` gate is dropped** from `attachPRStatus` (R7) — see § PR-Status SSE Join. The cross-repo contract for the fab-kit divestment this enables is in [`docs/specs/agent-state.md`](../../specs/agent-state.md); the run-kit-side agent-state tier that landed alongside it is [agent-state](agent-state.md).

### Web Push on Sustained Waiting

The SSE poll seam fires exactly **ONE Web Push per sustained-`waiting` episode** — an agent blocked on a HUMAN (the most notification-worthy state) that stays `waiting` for ≥ `waitingPushSustain` (15s). `idle`/`active` never push. It rides the per-server poll tick where the rolled-up window `AgentState` already exists — **no new goroutine, no new poller** (Constitution II applies to *durable* state; the episode map is in-memory only, mirroring the metrics/prstatus collectors). Logic lives in `api/waiting_push.go`; the seam wiring is in `api/sse.go`'s `poll()`. (260706-y1ar-status-pyramid-ui-surfacing)

**Episode model + tracker** (`waitingPushTracker`, own mutex — independent of the hub lock): a waiting EPISODE is a maximal run of consecutive `waiting` ticks for one window, keyed `waitingKey(server, windowID)` (`server\x00windowID` — window ids are unique only within a server). `waitingEpisode{since, pushed}` stamps when the current run began and whether it has pushed. The **pure `decide(wins []pushWindow) []waitingPush`** advances the tracker for one server's windows at `now` and returns the pushes to send: waiting + no run → start the run; waiting + run < sustain → wait; waiting + run ≥ sustain + `!pushed` → PUSH once + mark pushed; not-waiting → **delete the key** (re-arm — the next `waiting` run is a fresh episode that can push again). It is pure w.r.t. its inputs + the tracker map (the only side effect is mutating that map, which IS the episode memory). `decide` is the extracted testable helper (drives enter/sustain/push/continue/leave/re-enter — A-022/A-023).

**Sync decision, detached send** (T014 rework — the load-bearing invariant): `notifyWaiting(server, sess)` runs `decide` **synchronously** (in-memory map mutation, no I/O — the caller observes the tracker advance in-tick) but fans the actual `push.Notify` sends out in a **detached `context.Background()` goroutine** — a slow/hung Web Push endpoint can NEVER stall the SSE poll loop's documented zero-network hot path. Push errors are logged (`slog.Warn`), never surfaced (matches the `/api/notify` posture). Body: window name + `"waiting for input"`. The `notify` send fn is a seam (defaults to `push.Notify`, stubbed in tests).

**Scoped reap** (`retain(live, polled)` — the other T014 rework): the poll loop accumulates `liveWaitingKeys` across all polled servers, then reaps episodes for windows that vanished (so a re-created window id can't inherit a stale `pushed` flag). The sweep is **SCOPED to servers actually observed this tick** — the ones successfully polled (`polledServers`) PLUS the ones confirmed gone (`deadServers`). A server whose fetch failed TRANSIENTLY (non-`IsServerGone`) is in neither set and contributes zero live keys, so scoping the sweep leaves its still-waiting episodes untouched — otherwise its `since`/`pushed` would reset every failing tick, re-arming and firing a DUPLICATE push the moment the server recovered. `retain` recovers the server from a key by splitting on the NUL separator and reaps only `polled[server] && !live[key]`.

**Wiring**: `sseHub` gained a `waitingPush *waitingPushTracker` field (`newWaitingPushTracker()` in `newSSEHub`); in `poll()`, after `attachPRStatus(result)` for each successfully-fetched server, `h.waitingPush.notifyWaiting(server, result)` runs and its returned live keys accumulate into `liveWaitingKeys`; after the server loop, `h.waitingPush.retain(liveWaitingKeys, polledServers∪deadServers)` sweeps. Uses the existing `internal/push` subsystem (§ Web Push Notifications) — no new endpoint. `@rk_agent_msg` question text in the body is a **future tenant** (out of scope; the body is the fixed `"waiting for input"`).

**Deep-link URL (`260714-r7rq-chat-read-frontend`)**: each `waitingPush` now carries a `url` — the notification's click target, built by the pure `waitingPushURL(server, windowID, hasChat)`: `/{server}/{N}` where `N` is the window id's numeric part (tmux `@N` sans `@`, matching `windowIdToUrlSegment`), with `?view=chat` appended **iff the window is chat-capable** (`hasChat`), else the plain window URL (which resolves the window's own view pref on load). `server` and the numeric segment are `url.PathEscape`-d so a reserved-character name stays a valid same-origin relative URL. `hasChat` is read off the rolled-up window's `ChatProvider != ""` in `pushWindowsForServer`. The URL threads through `decide` → `waitingPush.url` → the detached-goroutine `t.notify(ctx, title, body, url)` → `push.Notify`. Go units (`waiting_push_test.go`) cover the chat-vs-plain URL construction.

### Session-Tile Previews — `event: preview` + preview-scope

The `SessionTiles` density view (`ui-patterns.md` § Session Tiles) shows a periodic **text snapshot** of each expanded window's active pane. Snapshots ride the existing SSE hub as a **dedicated `event: preview`** — deliberately NOT extending the `sessions` payload and NOT a live xterm/relay per tile (that would re-trigger the documented HTTP/1.1 6-per-origin pool starvation — the load-bearing constraint). This decoupling keeps the `sessions` dedup/order machinery lean (growing preview text never bloats the sessions dedup cache) and lets preview cadence stay independent of structural updates. `WindowInfo` is **unchanged** — no `preview` field. (260701-70a0-session-window-tile-grid)

**Per-connection expanded-set scope**: each `sseClient` carries `connID` (from the `?conn=` stream query param) and `expanded map[string]bool` (the session names that connection currently has expanded). Both are in-memory only (Constitution II) and drop with the client on disconnect (`removeClient` deletes the whole `*sseClient` — no leaked hub state, no separate cleanup path). `setPreviewScope(server, connID, expanded)` finds the client whose `connID` matches (under the hub lock) and replaces its `expanded` set; a `connID` miss is a silent no-op. It also immediately emits the cached preview subset for the just-changed set via `sendCachedPreviewLocked` (a no-op when the set is empty or nothing is cached).

**Capture in `poll()` (rides the existing tick — no new goroutine/loop)**: after the `sessions` broadcast for a server, the poll computes `expandedUnionLocked(clients)` — the union of every client's expanded session names on that server. When the union is empty (capture-nothing default — previews are opt-in per expansion), nothing is captured. Otherwise `capturePreviews(result, union, server, h.captureFn)` captures each window in a union session **once per tick, deduped by window ID** (`h.captureFn` defaults to `capturePreviewForWindow`; tests inject a stub so the broadcast path runs without a live tmux server). The full `{windowId → text}` union map is cached in `previousPreviewJSON[server]` (seeds cached-on-connect), then each client is sent a **per-connection-filtered subset** (`previewSubsetFor`, keyed off its own `expanded` set via `windowsBySession(result)`) over `event: preview`. The tmux captures run OUTSIDE the hub lock (each is an exec with its own timeout); only the cache write + per-client emit take the lock.

**Capture primitive (reused, no new tmux helper)**: `capturePreviewForWindow(w, server)` in `api/preview.go` picks the window's active pane via `activePaneID(w)` — the `PaneInfo` in `WindowInfo.Panes` whose `IsActive` is true, falling back to the first pane, `("", false)` when the window has no panes — then calls the existing `tmux.CapturePane(paneID, previewCaptureLines, server)` (Constitution I — `exec.CommandContext` + timeout, arg slices). `previewCaptureLines = 18` (named constant, within the ~15–20 range). Best-effort: a no-pane window or a capture error yields no entry (skipped, never a hard failure). **No new tmux resolution helper was added** — the active pane ID is already on `WindowInfo.Panes` from `ListWindows`'s `list-panes` enrichment (apply Assumption #1; the intake's conditional `tmux-sessions` memory modify did NOT trigger).

**Cached-on-connect**: `addClient` calls `sendCachedPreviewLocked` after the metrics cached-on-connect send, mirroring the `sessions`/`session-order`/`metrics` pattern — filtered to the new client's current expanded set (a no-op for a fresh connection, since scope is declared by a POST that arrives after connect).

**Frontend seam** (`app/frontend/src/contexts/session-context.tsx`): since `260716-qf3j-state-socket` the transport is the single `StateSocket` (one `hello` conn id per tab, not a per-server `connId` — the pooled per-server EventSource + `&conn=<id>` stream-URL append are gone). The provider routes the `preview` event through the socket's `onEvent` demux (merging the `{windowId → text}` map into that server's slice so a preview for one window doesn't clobber the others), exposes `previewsByServer: Map<string, Record<string,string>>` + a `setPreviewScope(server, expanded[])` context method, and that method sends the scope **in-band** via `socketRef.current.sendPreviewScope(server, expanded)` (addressed by the socket's own conn id — decision D4; no POST-races-the-stream window). The `api/client.ts` `setPreviewScope(server, conn, expanded)` HTTP helper is now unimported — a deletion candidate; the server-side `POST /api/preview-scope` endpoint stays (D4). The `SessionTiles` view calls the context method whenever its expanded set changes.

### `rk serve` Wiring

`cmd/rk/serve.go` instantiates the Supervisor after `tmux.EnsureConfig()` but BEFORE the `server.ListenAndServe()` goroutine, so the SSE hub never races an empty Client map for sockets that already exist on disk. (Since `260602-qn62-move-based-board-pin-sessions` there is no longer a `sweepOrphanedRelaySessions(ctx)` step between them — relay ephemerals are gone and pin-sessions are persistent, so `serve_sweep.go` was deleted and the startup ordering dropped to `EnsureConfig → Supervisor.Start → ListenAndServe`.) The Supervisor is constructed with `api.NewHubSinkFactory()` (since `260530-v6hm` — the per-socket tracker-bound sink factory) and started synchronously; per-socket `Open` failures (PTY unavailable, etc.) are logged inside the Supervisor and never block startup. Once `Start` returns, `apiServer.SetWindowChangeSubscriber(api.NewSupervisorSubscriber(supervisor))` wires the change-notification bridge and `apiServer.SetActiveWindowProvider(supervisor)` wires the Tier-1 active-window read path (see § Active-Window Event Derivation) — if `Start` itself fails (rare; usually fsnotify allocation), a single `slog.Warn` falls back to safety-net-only mode without aborting the server.

On SIGINT/SIGTERM, the shutdown handler runs `supervisor.Stop(ctx5s)` BEFORE `server.Shutdown(ctx)`. Stop errors are logged at `slog.Warn` and never block shutdown — matches PR #197's daemon-log graceful-degradation pattern. The 5s bounded teardown matches the existing `tmux.TmuxTimeout = 10s` shape (control-mode subprocesses are expected to close cleanly within half that bound).

### API Server version/checker wiring

The version-exposure + update-checker wiring lives in `cmd/rk/serve.go` (NOT `NewRouterAndServer`) because it needs the ldflags-injected `main.version`, which is known only in `cmd/rk`. Immediately after `router, apiServer := api.NewRouterAndServer(ctx, logger)`: (260713-4zap-update-notify-one-click-upgrade)

```go
selfBrew := resolveBrewInstalled()                                 // computed ONCE, shared by SetVersion + New
apiServer.SetVersion(version, newBootID(), selfBrew)               // seed SSE event: version (version+boot+brew) + hold version on Server
updateChecker := updatecheck.New(version, selfBrew)                // construct with the running version + its brew-install status
updateChecker.OnQualify = apiServer.WireUpdateAvailableBroadcast() // bind BEFORE Start
updateChecker.Start(ctx)                                           // background poll, bound to serve ctx
apiServer.SetUpdateChecker(updateChecker)                          // inject so /api/update reads its snapshot
```

`newBootID()` / `resolveBrewInstalled()` are `cmd/rk/serve.go` helpers (since `260714-3law-force-update-restart-palette`): `newBootID` returns `hex.EncodeToString` of `bootIDBytes = 8` random bytes (⇒ 16 hex chars) from `crypto/rand`, or `""` on a rand failure (degrades to version-only reload — no worse than before boot ids); `resolveBrewInstalled` resolves the self path once and tests the Cellar marker (`selfpath.Resolve` → `selfpath.IsBrewInstalled`), reporting `false` on a resolve error. `selfBrew` is computed ONCE per `rk serve` start and passed to BOTH `SetVersion` (the `event: version` `brew` field) and `updatecheck.New` (the run-kit-row self-match brew gate — a go-install/dev rk never self-matches).

The three `*api.Server` seams (all in `api/tmuxctl_bridge.go`, co-located with `SetWindowChangeSubscriber`/`SetActiveWindowProvider`):

- **`SetVersion(version, boot string, brew bool)`** — (signature extended by `260714-3law-force-update-restart-palette` from the single-string `SetVersion(version)`) stores `s.version = version` (a held copy) AND calls `s.initSSEHub()` + `s.sseHub.setVersion(version, boot, brew)` to seed the cached `event: version` slot with all three additive fields. Safe to call before any SSE client connects. **`s.version` now has a live reader**: `handleRestart`'s dev guard reads `s.version == devVersion` to `409` a restart on a dev build (see `/api/restart` in the API Layer table) — so the struct field is read (`4zap`, `3law`).
- **`SetUpdateChecker(c *updatecheck.Checker)`** — stores `s.updateChecker = c` so `handleUpdate` reads its `Snapshot().Matched` (the scoped-update argv + the non-force empty-set 409 gate) and calls `RecheckAfter` post-remediation. A nil checker makes `/api/update` report `409 no update available` on the non-force paths (the test/unwired-router degradation).
- **`WireUpdateAvailableBroadcast() func(updatecheck.Result)`** — `initSSEHub()`s then returns a closure `func(verdict) { s.sseHub.broadcastUpdateAvailable(verdict) }`, assigned to `checker.OnQualify`. The end-to-end chain: `updatecheck.checkOnce` → `OnQualify(verdict)` → this closure → `broadcastUpdateAvailable` → `buildUpdateAvailablePayload` (the shared builder, `{tools[…updateAvailable,notable], key, current, latest}`) → caches `cachedUpdateAvailableJSON`, fans `event: update-available` to all clients (a cleared verdict broadcasts + replaces the slot too). The SAME closure fires whether the pass is the ambient tick or a manual `POST /api/updates/check` → `CheckNow`, so both paths converge on the one cached slot.

The whole block sits before the tmuxctl Supervisor start and the HTTP listen. The checker suppresses itself for the `"dev"` sentinel / unparseable versions (so a local `go build` never fetches or notifies), and its goroutine exits on `ctx.Done()`.

#### Shared detached spawn-self seam (`spawnSelfFn`)

Both self-restarting handlers spawn a detached `rk <subcommand>` child through **ONE shared package-var seam** in `api/update.go` (generalized from `4zap`'s `spawnUpdateFn`, which was update-only): (260714-3law-force-update-restart-palette)

```go
var spawnSelfFn = func(selfPath string, logName string, args ...string) error { … }  // exec.Command(selfPath, args...), Setsid, logs to ~/.rk/<logName>
```

- `handleUpdate` calls it `("update.log", "update")`; `handleRestart` calls it `("restart.log", "daemon", "restart")` — two call sites, one implementation, no per-verb duplication. The two log names are `const`s (`updateLogRelPath` / `restartLogRelPath`) so the update and restart spawn logs stay independent.
- **Detached shape** (identical to `4zap`'s): `SysProcAttr{Setsid: true}` (own session/process group — the child MUST outlive the server, because both `rk update` and `rk daemon restart` restart the daemon and kill the serving process mid-request), stdout/stderr redirected to `~/.rk/<logName>` via the generalized `openRkLog(logName)` (`O_APPEND|O_CREATE|O_WRONLY` 0644, `~/.rk` mkdir'd; **a log-open failure is non-fatal** — the spawn proceeds without redirection), and a deferred parent-side `logFile.Close()` after `cmd.Start()` dups the fd into the child (the child keeps its own copy, so the log stays open for the detached process).
- **Deliberately NOT `exec.CommandContext`-bound** — the Constitution §I timeout rule exists to stop a hung subprocess *blocking* the server, and a detached child that must survive the server cannot inherit the request/server context and cannot block it; argument-slice construction + no user-provided argv still hold.
- **Test seam**: the package var lets handler tests record `(logName, args)` without launching a real child — the same seam pattern `4zap` established (mirrors `upgrade.go`'s `runBrewFn`/`restartDaemonFn`). The `resolveSelfPathFn` seam (default `selfpath.Resolve`) is shared by both handlers too.

### Constitution Alignment

- **§I (Security First)** — all subprocess calls in `tmuxctl/` use `exec.CommandContext` with explicit argument slices; no shell strings. The Client's `tmux -CC` invocation has no overall timeout because the connection is long-lived (per-call timeouts are not appropriate); the context is cancelled by `Close()` and propagates through the goroutine.
- **§II (No Database)** — no file is written under `~/.run-kit/`, `~/.cache/rk/`, or anywhere else. The Supervisor's `map[socket]*Client` mirrors the kernel-observable filesystem view of tmux sockets; nothing persists across `rk serve` lifetimes. The only persistent artefact in this neighbourhood is `~/.cache/rk/daemon.log` from PR #197, unchanged by this package.
- **§VI (Tmux Sessions Survive Server Restarts)** — `tmuxctl` observes tmux state changes and pushes them to SSE clients; it never mutates *user* sessions (it creates/reads only the `_rk-ctl` anchor and sets the server-scoped `exit-empty off` option — never touching any window, pane, or user session). Since `260602-a1wo-prevent-exit-empty-server-death` the `_rk-ctl` anchor is created **on every observed server** (including the user's `default` with live sessions), as a permanent session floor — NOT, as before, only on servers with zero pre-existing sessions. This is itself the deliberate Constitution VI *prevention*, not a violation: the floor + the server-global `set-option -g exit-empty off` (set imperatively in `productionDial` before the anchor on every dial/reconnect, plus baked into the embedded conf) together stop tmux's default `exit-empty on` from reaping a server when its session count momentarily hits zero — the recurring failure (`runWork`/`utils`/`kit`, ≥3x) that killed live agent sessions. (Pre-`260602-qn62` this happened when the last real session closed and the remaining `rk-relay-*` ephemerals drained to zero; since `qn62` removed those ephemerals, the same backstop now also keeps an *empty home session* alive after its only window is pinned away into a `_rk-pin-*` session — pin-session persistence relies on `exit-empty off`.) The anchor is harmless on a server with real sessions: it is filtered from every user-facing list (`tmux.ControlAnchorSessionName` chokepoint in `parseSessions`), ungrouped, and the control-mode connection attaches read-only (`-r`). Managed servers now die only via explicit `kill-server` / `rk reaper`; empty anchor-only servers persist by design (no auto-reaping, no cross-process state per §II).
- **No new network surface** — the Client is a local subprocess attached via PTY. `ss -tlnp` still shows only the existing HTTP listener.

## SPA Static Serving

Dual-mode SPA serving in `app/backend/api/spa.go`. `hasEmbeddedAssets()` checks if the `embed.FS` contains real build output (more than `.gitkeep`):

- **Production** (`mountEmbeddedSPA`): serves from `embed.FS` via `fs.Sub(build.Frontend, "frontend")` + `http.FS`. SPA fallback rewrites to `index.html`.
- **Development** (`mountFilesystemSPA`): serves from `app/frontend/dist/` on the local filesystem. Path traversal prevented (resolved path must stay within SPA directory).

Both modes: any request not matching `/api/*`, `/relay/*`, or `/proxy/*` serves `index.html` for client-side routing. In development, Vite handles SPA fallback natively.

## Chrome Architecture

**Lazy-loaded components**: `CommandPalette`, `ThemeSelector`, and `CreateSessionDialog` are loaded via `React.lazy()` with dynamic `import()` (not static imports). Each uses `.then(m => ({ default: m.X }))` to re-wrap named exports for `React.lazy()` compatibility. Render sites wrapped in per-component `<Suspense fallback={null}>` boundaries. These components are overlays/dialogs that render conditionally — lazy loading keeps them out of the initial bundle for faster first paint.

**Shell wrapper (CSS Grid topology)** — `<Shell>` (`app/frontend/src/components/shell/shell.tsx`) is the shared chrome wrapper used by both `AppShell` and `BoardPage`. The shell is a single CSS Grid root carrying `height: 100%` — it fills the root layout's `flex-1` content region. The TopBar is NOT part of the Shell grid (since `260707-4vq2`): it mounts once as `RootTopBar` in the persistent root layout, full-width above this Shell. The `--app-height` var (iOS keyboard handling) is maintained by `useVisualViewport()` in `RootWrapper` on the root layout div — Shell no longer calls the hook or reads the var. Desktop topology (`>= 640px`):

```
grid-template-areas:
  "sidebar content"
  "sidebar bottombar"
grid-template-rows:    1fr auto
grid-template-columns: ${sidebarWidth}px 1fr   (when sidebarOpen)
grid-template-columns: 0 1fr                   (when !sidebarOpen)
transition: grid-template-columns 150ms ease-out
```

Sidebar is full-height — it spans both rows and owns the entire left column. Content/bottombar stack in the right column. Sidebar collapse zeroes the first grid column (no 48px rail) — the content/bottombar cells extend their left edge to page.left automatically; no JS-side conditional rendering or component mutation.

The `sidebar` grid area is **Shell-owned**: on desktop `Shell` renders the `<aside style={{ gridArea: "sidebar" }} aria-label="Sidebar">` itself from its `sidebarChildren` prop, gated `!isMobile && sidebarOpen && !!sidebarChildren` (fully unmounts on collapse — no zero-width rail). Consumers place ONLY the `content` and `bottombar` grid areas; they never grid-area-place `sidebar`. The aside wraps `sidebarChildren` in a `flex-1 min-w-0 overflow-hidden` content wrapper and accepts an optional `sidebarResizeHandle?: ReactNode` slot rendered at its right edge — the desktop drag-resize handle. AppShell passes its handle through this slot; BoardPage passes none (drag-resize is intentionally absent on the board route). The aside carries `border-r border-border` ONLY when no handle is passed (BoardPage): with a handle the 3px handle bar is the visual seam, so a border would double it. Drag-resize wiring stays AppShell-only — all drag state/handlers (`handleDragHandlePointerDown`, width persistence, aria-value bounds) live in AppShell; the handle rides through the slot as an opaque node, so `Shell` stays dumb about drag logic. The mobile overlay never renders the handle. The handle is hidden when `sidebarOpen === false` (the only re-open affordance is the hamburger).

Mobile topology (`< 640px`): single column, `grid-template-areas: "content" / "bottombar"`. Sidebar renders as an overlay child of the Shell positioned via `gridRow: "1 / 3"` (spans content + bottombar, leaves the root-layout topbar above the Shell visible). Backdrop and `<aside>` use `position: absolute` (NOT `fixed inset-0`) so the overlay starts below the topbar — matches the existing project convention recorded in `fab/project/context.md`. The aside carries `role="dialog" aria-modal="true"`. Sidebar overlay open/close is driven by the same `sidebarOpen` state — `drawerOpen` is removed from `ChromeContext`.

**Hamburger placement** — the hamburger icon is statically rendered at `TopBar.left` in both `sidebarOpen` states.
