Visual "relocation" on collapse is a side effect of the grid column collapsing; there is no component-level relocation logic. When `sidebarOpen === true`, the hamburger sits at the sidebar.right / topbar.left seam (pixel-identical to "attached to sidebar"). When `sidebarOpen === false`, it sits at page.left because the topbar grid cell has extended to page.left.

**Keyboard toggle** — `Cmd+\` (macOS) / `Ctrl+\` (Linux/Windows) toggles `sidebarOpen` from any route that mounts `<Shell>`. The chord is registered in the `KeyboardShortcuts` modal under "Toggle sidebar" per Constitution V (Keyboard-First). The chord is suppressed when focus is inside a real text input/textarea/contenteditable, but NOT when focus is on xterm.js's helper textarea (recognized by `target.closest('.xterm') != null`) — without the xterm exception, the most common focus state would silently swallow the toggle.

**Sidebar width persistence** — width state lives in `ChromeContext` (`sidebarWidth`). The dispatch surface is split: `setSidebarWidth(width)` updates in-memory state only (called per-pointermove during drag), and `persistSidebarWidth(width)` writes `localStorage["runkit-sidebar-width"]` (called once at drag-end). This explicit split avoids localStorage thrash on every pointer event. Callers like the AppShell drag handler track the last-seen width in a ref (`dragLastWidthRef`) and call `persistSidebarWidth` once in `handleEnd`.

**Routing branches inside the `content` grid area**:
- AppShell (`/$server/$window`): `<TerminalClient>` (the `tty` lens) | `<IframeWindow>` (the `web` lens) | `<ChatView>` (the `chat` lens) | `<SessionTiles>` (no window param). The renderer is chosen by the **resolved view** (`chatViewActive ? ChatView : resolvedView === "web" && rkUrl ? IframeWindow : TerminalClient`, `chatViewActive = resolvedView === "chat"`), NOT by `@rk_type` identity — the chat lens folds into the SAME `resolveView` machinery; see `ui-patterns.md` § Window Views (Lens Model). (`260714-t97o-web-view-lens`, `260714-r7rq`)
- BoardPage (`/board/$name`): `DesktopRow` / `MobileCarousel` body (the existing horizontal-scroll panes), flush with `sidebar.right` (no left gutter).

No `max-w-4xl` constraint — all zones span full width.

**ThemeProvider** (`app/frontend/src/contexts/theme-context.tsx`) — outermost provider. Split into ThemeStateContext (preference + resolved theme) and ThemeActionsContext (setTheme). Three modes: system, light, dark. Preference persisted to `localStorage` key `runkit-theme`. System mode listens to `matchMedia("(prefers-color-scheme: dark)")` change events. Theme applied via `data-theme` attribute on `<html>`. Blocking inline script in `index.html` `<head>` reads localStorage and sets `data-theme` before first paint (no-flicker initialization).

**ChromeProvider** (`app/frontend/src/contexts/chrome-context.tsx`) — split into two React contexts: `ChromeStateContext` (read-only state: `currentSession`, `currentWindow`, `sidebarOpen`, `sidebarWidth`, `isConnected`, `fixedWidth`) and `ChromeDispatchContext` (stable setter functions: `setCurrentSession`, `setCurrentWindow`, `setSidebarOpen` — persists to `localStorage["runkit-sidebar-open"]`, `setSidebarWidth` — in-memory only, `persistSidebarWidth(width)` — writes localStorage on drag-end, `setIsConnected`, `toggleFixedWidth`). `drawerOpen`/`setDrawerOpen` were removed when the rotated shell collapsed the desktop-vs-mobile sidebar split into a single `sidebarOpen` boolean (the rendering form differs per breakpoint, the state does not). Chrome derives its content from the current selection — no slot injection. `setLine2Left`, `setLine2Right`, `setBottomBar` removed; top bar and bottom bar read the selection directly. `Breadcrumb` type includes optional `dropdownItems` for session/window switching.

**FocusedTerminalContext** (`app/frontend/src/contexts/focused-terminal-context.tsx`) — tracks the currently-focused terminal across the app so the shell-level `BottomBar` can target the right WebSocket regardless of route. Mounted in `RootWrapper` between `SessionProvider` and `OptimisticProvider`; provider tree order is `ThemeProvider > ChromeProvider > RootWrapper(SessionProvider > OptimisticProvider > FocusedTerminalProvider > Outlet)`. Shape:

```ts
type FocusedTerminal = {
  wsRef: React.RefObject<WebSocket | null>;
  server: string;
  session: string;
  windowIndex: string;
} | null;

type FocusedTerminalContextValue = {
  focused: FocusedTerminal;
  setFocused: (t: FocusedTerminal) => void;
};
```

Producers: `TerminalClient` registers on mount when its `registerFocus` prop is `true` (single-terminal route default) and clears on unmount. `BoardPane` registers when its `isFocused` prop becomes true (and on initial pane mount); it manages the registration itself and passes `registerFocus={false}` to its inner `TerminalClient` to avoid producer contention. `BoardPane` clears the focused terminal on **unmount** iff it is still the registered pane (ref-guarded still-mine check) so leaving a board for `/$server` does not strand a stale target; a pane-focus SWITCH does not unmount the losing pane, so the next pane to gain focus overwrites.

Consumers: the shell-level `BottomBar` reads `focused?.wsRef` (replacing the removed `wsRef` prop); the docked compose strip (`ComposeStrip`, § ui-patterns § Docked Compose Strip) reads `focused` live and sends to `focused.wsRef` at send time (the live-target model — no target frozen at open). When `focused === null` (e.g. the `/$server` tiles route), the strip renders disabled and BottomBar input handlers natural-no-op via the existing `wsRef.current?.readyState !== OPEN` guard. The docked-strip enablement is the persisted `composeStripEnabled` chrome preference (`ChromeContext`), not context state here.

**SessionProvider** (`app/frontend/src/contexts/session-context.tsx`) — root-mounted multi-server React Context. One `SessionProvider` instance lives above `<Outlet />` in `RootWrapper` and is shared by every route (`/`, `/$server/...`, `/board/$name`); it does NOT remount on server-route switches. State is keyed per server: `sessionsByServer: Map<string, ProjectSession[]>`, `sessionOrderByServer: Map<string, string[]>`, `isConnectedByServer: Map<string, boolean>`, `metricsByServer: Map<string, MetricsSnapshot | null>`. It also exposes a scalar `hostMetricsConnected: boolean` (host-metrics source health for the Host-page connection dot, `260704-9o7k` — see § Server-independent host-metrics subscription). The `/` page component is `HostOverviewPage` (`host-overview-page.tsx`); the `top-bar` page-mode strings are `"host"` (`/`) and `"server"` (`/$server`). (`260715-zs1y-host-tmux-server-rename`) `currentServer: string | null` is dispatched from the matched route via `useMatches()` — `params.server` for `/$server/...`, `null` for `/board/$name` and `/`. Consumers read the per-server slice they need via `ctx.sessionsByServer.get(name)`. Provider tree order: `ThemeProvider > ChromeProvider > RootWrapper(SessionProvider > OptimisticProvider > Outlet)`. The provider mirrors `currentServer`'s connection state into `ChromeProvider` so existing chrome consumers (top-bar connection dot) keep working unchanged. Persists most-recently active server to `localStorage` key `runkit-server` (single value, not split per server).

**State-socket transport** — the provider owns ONE `StateSocket` per tab (`src/lib/state-socket.ts`, § State Socket above) held in `socketRef`. The current server is auto-attached; non-current servers attach lazily via the `attachServer(name)` API exposed on context. The `attachedSet` drives a diff effect that `subscribeServer`/`unsubscribeServer`s (ref-counted on the socket); each subscribe `ack` updates only that server's slice. When a server disappears from `/api/servers` it is unsubscribed and its entries removed from every per-server map. A 3-second disconnect debounce runs per server, driven by socket-level connection-state changes — an `onerror` doesn't flip a still-acked server's `isConnectedByServer` until the debounce fires. `useBoards` and `useWindowPins` call `attachServer` for every known server when the sidebar mounts, costing nothing on the pool budget (one shared WS). (`260716-qf3j-state-socket`)

**`subscribeBoardChange`** (`session-context.tsx`) — context API that lets any consumer register a `(server: string) => void` handler and receive cross-server `board-changed` events through the one shared socket. `useBoards` and `useWindowPins` use it to react to per-server board mutations without opening their own connections — the state socket already streams `board-changed` (as `kind:"server"`), so multiplexing through one subscriber API keeps the wire-subscription count bounded. (Signature unchanged across the transport swap — it always operated above the transport seam.)

**Server-independent host-metrics subscription + `useHostMetrics()`** (`session-context.tsx`, since `260701-vshd-cockpit-host-console-home`; transport is the state socket's `metrics` subscription since `260716-qf3j-state-socket`) — a `subscribeMetrics()` on the shared socket (the in-band `kind:"metrics"` op, internally the retained `metricsOnlyServer` sentinel) that receives ONLY the server-independent `metrics`/`services` global events, so host health is available where there is no `currentServer` and no per-server subscription to carry it (the Host-page host-console home `/`; see ui-patterns.md § HOST HEALTH Zone). It is **opened only when `attachedSet.size === 0`** (`hostMetricsWanted`) and dropped once any server attaches — the per-server subscription's `metrics` event already fans the same server-global payload into the shared `hostMetrics` state. The dedicated-stream mutual-exclusion holds, though not for pool-budget reasons: the one WebSocket holds no HTTP/1.1 pool slot at all (the connection-starvation motivation that drove this is exactly what the state socket eliminated — see § State Socket / ui-patterns.md § Desktop Relay-Connection Suspension). A `metricsSubscribedRef` guard drives the subscribe/unsubscribe; the socket effect's cleanup resets it (+ `subscribedServersRef`/`ackedServersRef`) so a StrictMode remount re-subscribes on the fresh socket (§ State Socket → StrictMode safety). The parsed snapshot lands in provider state `hostMetrics` (`MetricsSnapshot | null`, `null` pre-tick) exposed via `HostMetricsContext` + the `useHostMetrics(): MetricsSnapshot | null` hook. **`useHostMetrics()` is NOT `currentServer`-gated** — unlike `useMetrics()` (which returns `currentServer ? metricsByServer.get(currentServer) : null`, hence `null` on `/`); both hooks use the same undefined-sentinel throw-outside-provider idiom. `useMetrics()` (current-server-scoped, for `HostPanel`'s sidebar call site) is unchanged. Backend contract for the `metrics` subscription / `metricsOnlyServer` sentinel: see § State Socket + § API Layer `/ws/state`.

**Host-metrics stream health (`hostMetricsConnected`, `260704-9o7k-top-bar-button-pyramid`)** — the health of the host-metrics *source*, exposed on `SessionContextType` as a `hostMetricsConnected: boolean` for the **Host-page connection dot** (`host-overview-page.tsx` passes it as `isConnected` to `<TopBar mode="host">`; see ui-patterns.md § Chrome (Top Bar) → connection dot). It tracks the dedicated `?metrics=1` stream's health. Two sources, mirroring the dedicated-stream ↔ per-server-fan-out switch above:
- **Dedicated-subscription health** — while `hostMetricsWanted` (attached set empty, so the `metrics` subscription IS the source), a `dedicatedMetricsConnected` state tracks it: set `true` on the metrics subscription's `ack` (or a recovered socket connection while it is acked), cleared via a **3s debounce** driven by the socket's `onConnectionChange` — so a transient socket blip doesn't flicker the dot. The flag is reset when a server attaches (the `hostMetricsWanted → false` branch unsubscribes metrics and drops `METRICS_SUB` from `ackedServersRef`). `false` until the first metrics `ack`. (Transport swapped from a dedicated `?metrics=1` EventSource to the shared socket's `metrics` subscription by `260716-qf3j-state-socket`.)
- **Per-server fan-out fallback** — when a per-server subscription is attached (metrics subscription dropped, the fan-out now carries host metrics), the derived value reads `true` iff **any** attached server slice `isConnected` (that server is delivering the server-global `metrics` event).

The exposed `hostMetricsConnected` is a `useMemo` selecting between the two: `hostMetricsWanted ? dedicatedMetricsConnected : (any slice connected)`. It is added to the context type, both provider `value` memos (+ deps), and `StandaloneSessionContextProvider` defaults (`false`).

**Kill-redirect gate (`currentWindowEverSeen`)** — The "session/window gone" redirect in `app/frontend/src/app.tsx` (around the `useEffect` that calls `computeKillRedirect` from `app/frontend/src/lib/navigation.ts`) MUST NOT fire for a freshly-navigated URL whose (session, window) pair has not yet been observed as valid in the SSE `sessions` stream. `computeKillRedirect` accepts a `currentWindowEverSeen?: boolean` param (defaults to `true` for legacy callers and unit tests) and short-circuits to `null` when false — bypassing both the "session gone → dashboard" and "window gone → nearest sibling" branches. The caller maintains two refs: `currentWindowEverSeenRef` (boolean, flipped `true` whenever the memoized `currentWindow` is non-null) and `lastObservedUrlKeyRef` (string, `${server}|${session}|${window}`). Any URL-key change resets the seen flag to `false`. This gates two transient SSE states that are not proof the URL is unreachable: (a) a stale cached first payload that replays an older server snapshot before delivering current data, and (b) a session whose `windows` array is briefly empty while tmux enumeration propagates into the next poll tick. Without the gate, either state makes `currentSession` or `currentWindow` null on the first SSE event after navigation, the redirect fires, and `TerminalClient` unmounts mid-initialization — surfacing as an e2e flake where `.xterm-screen` briefly appears then disappears. Genuine kills from another client still redirect normally, because the URL key only resets on navigation, not on SSE payload changes: once the seen flag is `true`, a subsequent payload that drops the window triggers the redirect as before.

**Window state (Zustand)** — window optimistic state is managed by a Zustand store at `app/frontend/src/store/window-store.ts`, keyed by the immutable tmux `windowId` (`@N`). `zustand` is a production dependency in `app/frontend/package.json`. The store tracks `killed` and `pendingName` overrides per window ID, and ghost windows awaiting SSE confirmation. `AppShell` drives `setWindowsForSession` from SSE `rawSessions`. `OptimisticContext` retains session and server optimistic state only (name-based keys, not index-based). See ui-patterns.md "Zustand Window Store" section for full shape and action surface.

**`WindowInfo` type** (`app/frontend/src/types.ts`) — includes `windowId: string` (non-optional) as the immutable tmux `@N` identifier, alongside `index: number` (tmux ordering, display-only, not used as a store key). Backend populates `windowId` from `#{window_id}` in the `ListWindows()` format string. `color?: string` — optional color-value descriptor (`"4"` single index or `"1+3"` blend) from the tmux `@color` user option (was `number` before `260615-6rnr-expand-swatch-palette-blends`); `ProjectSession.sessionColor?: string` is the analogous per-session field. `panes?: PaneInfo[]` is an optional field (undefined when absent — existing fixtures omit it without type error). `PaneInfo` type: `{ paneId: string; paneIndex: number; cwd: string; command: string; isActive: boolean }`. `rkType?: string` — `"iframe"` or undefined; determines frontend renderer (terminal vs iframe). `rkUrl?: string` — URL for iframe windows; populated from tmux `@rk_url` user-defined option. `marker?: string` — the window's left-gutter marker state (`""`/`dotted`/`solid`/`double`) from the tmux `@rk_marker` option, threaded from `WindowInfo.Marker` (Go, JSON `marker,omitempty`) → the `sd.windows` pass-through onto the state-socket window payload exactly like `color`/`rkType` (no new socket event); consumed by the sidebar left-edge label zone (ui-patterns.md § Left-Edge Label Zone). All three (`rkType`/`rkUrl`/`marker`) use `omitempty` on backend / optional on frontend — terminal windows omit them. `WindowEntry` in `window-store.ts` gains `panes: PaneInfo[]` (non-optional, defaults to `[]` when absent from incoming `WindowInfo`); `setWindowsForSession` syncs panes from incoming data on every SSE tick.

**`MetricsSnapshot` type** (`app/frontend/src/types.ts`) — mirrors the backend `metrics.MetricsSnapshot` struct. Fields: `hostname` (string), `cpu` (`{ samples: number[], current: number, cores: number }`), `memory` (`{ used: number, total: number }` bytes), `load` (`{ avg1, avg5, avg15: number, cpus: number }`), `disk` (`{ used: number, total: number }` bytes), `uptime` (number, seconds). Rendered by the shared `HostMetrics` presentational component (ui-patterns.md § HostPanel / HOST HEALTH Zone), fed from `useMetrics()` (sidebar `HostPanel`, current-server-scoped) or `useHostMetrics()` (the `/` zone, server-independent — see § Server-independent host-metrics subscription above), both via `SessionProvider` context.

**TopBar** (`app/frontend/src/components/top-bar.tsx`) — the full-width top bar / navbar; reads from ChromeProvider + its props. It spans both columns of the Shell grid (`app.tsx`/`board-page.tsx`) or is pinned above the Host page's scroll container (`host-overview-page.tsx`, no Shell). (`260702-6m46-full-width-topbar-navbar`) Single line (`border-b-[3px] border-border`). LEFT is a breadcrumb `<nav>`: the brand (logo + `hidden sm:inline` "Run Kit" wordmark) as the left-most `<a href="/">` root crumb, then (where a sidebar exists) the hamburger, then the mode-specific crumbs, `›`-separated. RIGHT is a **3-level cumulative button pyramid** (`260704-9o7k`): L1 terminal-only (split ×2 + FixedWidthToggle) → L2 terminal+board (terminal-font `Aa` + close/unpin ✕) → L3 always-in-every-mode (Notification → Theme → Refresh → Help) → the right-most connection dot (rendered in **all four modes**). The brand "Run Kit" anchor is the left-most root crumb, not a right-side element. See ui-patterns.md § Chrome (Top Bar) → Right cluster + § Shell Grid Layout for the full per-mode breakdown and the crumb/affordance vocabulary.

**TopBar `mode` prop** — `mode: "terminal" | "board" | "server" | "host"` (default `"terminal"`) controls the left-nav content. AppShell passes `"terminal"` (server link + session/window dropdown crumbs) or `"server"` (tmux Server — server name as the `aria-current` leaf). `HostOverviewPage` passes `"host"` (brand crumb only — no hamburger, no terminal-font/split/close, and no FixedWidth button; renders the L3 always-block Notification/Theme/Refresh/Help **plus the connection dot**, passing `hostMetricsConnected` as `isConnected`). BoardPage passes `"board"` with `boardName`/`paneCount`/`serverCount`: brand + hamburger + `›` + `BoardModeBreadcrumb` (`Board ▸ {name} ▾` via the shared `BreadcrumbDropdown`) + inline-info `{N} pane[s] · {M} server[s] · ⌘[⌘] cycle`, `hidden sm:inline`, plus the L2 pair (Aa + the ✕, which is a real **close-pane kill** of the focused tile's active pane; unpin lives on the tile-header pin-glyph + palette) and the L3 always-block; board mode also renders the two L1 SplitButtons (wired to the focused tile's window via the slot's `focusedPane`). It passes a `boardConnected` AND-over-attached-servers value as `isConnected`. The connection dot renders in **all four modes**; its per-page meaning ("this page's live data is flowing") is derived by each caller. See ui-patterns.md § Chrome (Top Bar) → Right cluster. (`260702-6m46-full-width-topbar-navbar`, `260715-zs1y-host-tmux-server-rename`, `260704-9o7k-top-bar-button-pyramid`, `260715-6jwn-board-splits-close-pin-icon`)

**BoardPage adopts Shell** — `BoardPage` (`app/frontend/src/components/board/board-page.tsx`) wraps its body in `<Shell>` like AppShell; the bespoke `h-screen w-screen flex` root, the inline mini-header (`Board ▸ {name} ▾`), and the per-route mini-sidebar wrapper are gone. `BoardSwitcherDropdown` moved to/imported by `TopBar` in board mode. BoardPage gets a `<BottomBar>` for the first time — the board route had none pre-change. The `<BottomBar />` invocation is byte-identical across AppShell and BoardPage: the same three callbacks (`onOpenCompose`, `onFocusTerminal`, `onScrollLockChange`) are wired identically. `onOpenCompose` is `toggleComposeStrip` (the `>_` chip toggles the docked compose strip preference); `onFocusTerminal` invokes a ref-tracked `focusFocusedPaneRef.current()` that re-focuses the currently-focused board pane; `onScrollLockChange` plumbs through `DesktopRow`/`MobileCarousel` → `BoardPane` → `TerminalClient.scrollLocked`.

**Sidebar** (`app/frontend/src/components/sidebar/`) — session/window tree with bottom-aligned collapsible panels. The same `<Sidebar>` instance renders for both AppShell (`/$server/...`) and BoardPage (`/board/$name`); BoardPage no longer ships its own mini-sidebar. Sessions are grouped per server — one `CollapsiblePanel`-style group per server in `servers`, each fed by its slice from `sessionsByServer`. The `currentServer` group carries a visual marker; on board routes (`currentServer === null`) no group is marked. Desktop: drag-resizable (default 220px, min 160, max 400, persisted to `localStorage`), collapsible via `☰`. Mobile (< 768px): drawer overlay from the left, triggered by `☰`. Layout: ServerPanel -> Boards section -> per-server session groups (`flex-1 overflow-y-auto`) -> WindowPanel (collapsible, `storageKey="runkit-panel-window"`) -> HostPanel (collapsible, `storageKey="runkit-panel-host"`). The Sidebar reads multi-server state from context (`sessionsByServer`, `sessionOrderByServer`, `isConnectedByServer`, `metricsByServer`); `currentServer` is passed in as a prop (AppShell reads it from context and forwards; BoardPage passes `null`). Action callbacks (create/kill, resize start, select) come in as props.

**BottomBar** (`app/frontend/src/components/bottom-bar.tsx`) — rendered at shell level via `<Shell>`'s `bottombar` grid area on every route that mounts `<Shell>` (single-terminal, board, dashboard). Width tracks the right grid column (page width minus sidebar). Single row of `<kbd>` buttons: modifier toggles (Ctrl/Alt with sticky armed state — Cmd removed), Esc, Tab, arrow keys, Fn dropdown (F1-F12, PgUp/PgDn, Home/End), and the `>_` compose toggle. Buttons: 36px desktop (`min-h-[36px] min-w-[36px]`), 44px touch (`coarse:min-h-[44px] coarse:min-w-[36px]`). Modifier state managed by `useModifierState` hook (Ctrl/Alt only). The `>_` button is an `aria-pressed` accent toggle flipping the `composeStripEnabled` chrome preference (§ ui-patterns § Docked Compose Strip), not a modal trigger; on touch, the ⌨ keyboard button focuses the docked strip's textarea (via the `focusComposeStrip` registry) when the preference is on. Input handlers read `focused?.wsRef` from `FocusedTerminalContext` and send ANSI escape sequences through it. When `focused === null` (Dashboard route, no terminal), input handlers natural-no-op via the `wsRef.current?.readyState !== OPEN` guard — no error, no toast.

**ComposeStrip** (`app/frontend/src/components/compose-strip.tsx`) — a single global, sticky `<textarea>` surface docked at the bottom of the terminal area, above the bottom-bar keys, rendered when the `composeStripEnabled` chrome preference is on. A real `<textarea>` supports iOS dictation, autocorrect, paste, IME, and multiline. Enter sends `text + "\r"` as raw bytes over the live focused pane's relay `wsRef` (Shift+Enter newline, IME-guarded, empty no-op); Escape blurs to the terminal; the strip never steals focus and stays open after send. Draft text + pending attachments live in a module store (`lib/compose-draft-store.ts`, `useSyncExternalStore`) so they survive toggle-off/on and terminal↔board route changes. Full behavior in [ui-patterns](/run-kit/ui-patterns.md) § Docked Compose Strip.

**iOS Keyboard Support** — `useVisualViewport` hook (`app/frontend/src/hooks/use-visual-viewport.ts`) listens to both `resize` and `scroll` events on `window.visualViewport`, setting `--app-height` CSS custom property from `visualViewport.height`. In the single-view model (fullbleed always on), `globals.css` applies `position: fixed; inset: 0; height: var(--app-height, 100vh)` to the app shell. The bottom bar stays pinned above the keyboard; the terminal shrinks via `flex-1` and xterm refits via `ResizeObserver`.

**iOS Touch Scroll Prevention** — Fullbleed is always active in the single-view model. The `fullbleed` class is added to `<html>` by `useVisualViewport` on mount (also present as a static default in `index.html` for FOUC prevention). `globals.css` applies `overflow: hidden` and `overscroll-behavior: none` to both `html` and `body` via `html.fullbleed` selectors, preventing iOS Safari elastic bounce scrolling. The terminal container div uses `touch-none` (`touch-action: none`) so the browser yields touch gestures to xterm.js for scrollback handling.

**Browser title** — `useBrowserTitle` hook sets `document.title` dynamically based on hostname (fetched once from `GET /api/health` on app init) and route params. Dashboard: `RunKit — {hostname}`. Terminal: `{session}/{window} — {hostname}`. Omits hostname suffix when empty. Static `<title>RunKit</title>` in `index.html` remains as pre-hydration fallback.

Single-view model: there are no page transitions or per-page chrome injection. The chrome reads the current selection and renders directly.

## CLI Subcommands (Cobra)

`app/backend/cmd/rk/` uses `spf13/cobra` for CLI management. `root.go` declares `var version = "dev"` (overridden by ldflags) and registers all subcommands. `main.go` just calls `execute()`. Version info via `--version`/`-v` global flag (Cobra built-in, not a subcommand).

**Shared output convention — persistent `--quiet` + `outputSink`** (`260717-f8yv-cli-output-volume-controls`, toolkit Principle 9). A single **persistent `--quiet` bool** is registered on `rootCmd` (`root.go`, bound to package-level `quiet`), so every present and future subcommand accepts it uniformly and inherits it with zero registration work; it is a deliberate no-op on any command not yet routed through the sink (incremental adoption). The convention, decided once, lives in `cmd/rk/output.go` (package `main`, no `internal/` package for a CLI-only concern): **`outputSink{data, chatter io.Writer}`** with `Dataf` (data channel) / `Notef` (chatter channel). **stdout carries data** — machine-consumable results (outcome lines, `--json` documents, requested previews/lists) — never gated by `--quiet`; **stderr carries chatter** — progress/decoration — routed to `io.Discard` under `--quiet`. **Errors always survive** (they flow through `RunE` returns and ungated stderr writes); `--quiet` never changes exit codes; a successful run with nothing to report is silent under `--quiet`. Built on `cmd.OutOrStdout()`/`cmd.ErrOrStderr()` (never bare `os.Stdout`/`os.Stderr`) so gating is unit-testable — the idiom `doctor.go`/`agent_setup.go` already used; `newSink(cmd)` reads `--quiet` off the invoked command (falling back to the package var for a bare test command), `newSinkWriters(data, chatter)` builds a test sink from explicit writers. **Adopted by `update`/`doctor`/`agent-setup`** (the audit-named chatter carriers — see their rows); `reaper` takes a display cap instead of a quiet conversion (its output is all data — see its row). This flipped toolkit Principle 9 to conformant — see [toolkit-standards](toolkit-standards.md) § Requirement: Bounded, high-signal output (Principle 9).

| Subcommand | File | Behavior |
|------------|------|----------|
| *(none)* | `root.go` | Defaults to `serve` (backwards compat) |
| `serve` | `serve.go` | Start HTTP server (foreground-only) — loads config from env vars, chi router, graceful shutdown via SIGINT/SIGTERM. No lifecycle flags (the pre-`260528-5zvv` `-d`/`--restart`/`--stop` flags were removed in a hard break — use `rk daemon ...` instead). Still imports `internal/daemon` for `daemon.LogEnvVar` consumed by `setupSlog`'s tee-to-file logic |
| `daemon` | `daemon.go`, `daemon_start.go`, `daemon_stop.go`, `daemon_restart.go`, `daemon_status.go`, `daemon_portowner.go` | Top-level command tree (sibling of `serve`, not nested) managing the background daemon. Subcommands: `start [--force]`, `stop [--force]`, `restart [--force]`, `status [--json]`. `--force` overrides the port-claim safety check by SIGTERMing a non-daemon port owner (graceful-then-forceful via `terminateOwner`); refuses to kill itself when the owner PID matches `daemon.InnerServePID()`. `status` is read-only and rejects `--force`. Port-owner lookup via `lsof -ti:<port>` → `ss -tlnp` fallback in shared `daemon_portowner.go` (port-only query, host pass-through for display, `exec.CommandContext` 5s timeout). Subcommand vars (`daemonStartCmd`, etc.) injectable in tests via package-level `var findPortOwner = findPortOwnerImpl` and `var innerServePIDFn = daemon.InnerServePID`. See `## Daemon Lifecycle` for full semantics |
| `update` | `upgrade.go` | Alias: `upgrade`. Detect Homebrew install via the shared `internal/selfpath` package (since `260713-4zap-update-notify-one-click-upgrade` — `resolveExeFn` now defaults to `selfpath.Resolve` and detection is `selfpath.IsBrewInstalled(resolved)` / `strings.Index(resolved, selfpath.CellarMarker)`; the `/Cellar/run-kit/` marker + resolver were extracted so this CLI path and `api/update.go`'s `POST /api/update` share ONE brew-detection impl that cannot drift — see § Backend Libraries `internal/selfpath`). The Cellar marker follows the `run-kit` formula name since `260709-gidk-swap-canonical-cli-name-run-kit`. If Homebrew: `brew update --quiet`, check latest version via `brew info --json=v2`, skip if already up to date, else `brew upgrade sahil87/tap/run-kit` + auto-restart daemon via `daemon.RestartWithBinary(brewBinPath)` where `brewBinPath` is derived from the Cellar path (`<brewPrefix>/bin/run-kit`), not stale `os.Executable()`. **Brew invocation discipline** (`260719-er5k-update-version-standards-conformance`, shll `update` standard's brew-handling safety clause): every brew call is constructed by the standalone `newBrewCmd(ctx, args...) *exec.Cmd` helper (unit-testable without spawning brew), and the class is keyed on `args[0]`. **Mutating** subcommands (`brew update`, `brew upgrade`) run under **generous, network-sized bounds** (`brewUpgradeTimeout = 30m`, `brewUpdateTimeout = 10m`) with **graceful termination**: `newBrewCmd` sets `cmd.Cancel` to deliver **`SIGTERM`** and `cmd.WaitDelay = brewCancelGrace` (30s), so on context expiry brew gets a trappable signal plus a 30s grace window to unwind the keg swap before the runtime's final kill — never a `SIGKILL` mid-transaction (a kill between `brew unlink` and `brew link` corrupts the keg; Homebrew 6's un-timed `api.github.com` call can legitimately stall for minutes). **Read-only** brew queries (`brew info --json=v2` here; `internal/updatecheck`'s `brew list --versions`) keep their **short 10s bounds and default cancel** — killing a query corrupts nothing, so fast-fail is correct, and an unmatched brew subcommand inherits that safe default. `exec.CommandContext` with a timeout is retained on all calls (Constitution § Process Execution). The web one-click upgrade (`POST /api/update` → detached `rk update --skip-brew-update`) routes through the same `updateCmd`, so it inherits the discipline. See [toolkit-standards](toolkit-standards.md) § `update` + `version` Standards. Non-Homebrew: print the single fully-qualified reinstall hint `brew install sahil87/tap/run-kit` (never the unqualified `brew install run-kit` — homebrew-core ships an unrelated `run-kit` formula that wins unqualified resolution). **`--skip-brew-update` flag** (local cobra bool, default `false`; since `260531-ckwv-skip-brew-update-flag`): gates ONLY the internal `brew update --quiet` tap-metadata refresh; the `brew info` version check, up-to-date short-circuit, `brew upgrade`, and daemon restart all still run. Default (flag absent) behavior is byte-for-byte unchanged. The three brew call sites and the daemon restart route through package-level seam vars (`runBrewFn`, `restartDaemonFn`, `resolveExeFn`) matching the `innerServePIDFn` idiom so `upgrade_test.go` can stub them without spawning `brew` or restarting a real daemon. **`--quiet`** (`260717-f8yv-cli-output-volume-controls`, toolkit Principle 9 — see § CLI Subcommands intro for the shared `outputSink`): the RunE builds `newSink(cmd)` and routes progress/decoration (`Current version: v…`, `Updating v… → v…`, `Restarting run-kit daemon…`, `run-kit daemon started (…)`) through `Notef` (chatter, dropped by `--quiet`) while routing **outcome lines** (`Already up to date (v…).`, `Updated to v….`, and the not-a-Homebrew-install guidance block — silence there would misreport a no-op as success) through `Dataf` (data, survives). The **streamed brew subprocess output** is the definitional "raw brew output" chatter: the `brewStreams(quiet)` helper selects the `update`/`upgrade` stdout/stderr — under `--quiet` stdout → `io.Discard` and stderr is **buffered** into a `*bytes.Buffer` (non-nil only under quiet), so on a non-zero exit `runBrewFn` **wraps the captured stderr detail into the returned error** (a failing `rk update --quiet` keeps its diagnostics rather than a bare `exit status 1` — R2's errors-always-survive rule; cycle-1 rework). Non-quiet runs stream to the real `os.Stdout`/`os.Stderr` (a nil errBuf — the detail is already on the terminal). The `info` path is unaffected (it captures stdout via `.Output()`; its bytes are data) |
| `doctor` | `doctor.go` | Check runtime dependencies only — `exec.LookPath("tmux")`. Exit 1 if any check fails (worst-check-wins). **`--json`** (`260717-c424-toolkit-standards-conformance`, toolkit Principle 2): emits a structured `{ok, checks:[{name, ok, hint}]}` document to **stdout** (data), where `ok` is the worst-check-wins overall verdict; exit stays 0 all-pass / 1 any-fail. The **human diagnostic output goes to stderr** (`cmd.ErrOrStderr()`, bound as `stderr`) — it is diagnostics, not the data a machine parses — and is unchanged by the flag. The verdict is computed once in the pure `runDoctorChecks() doctorReport` so the human and JSON renderers share one source of truth. **`--quiet`** (`260717-f8yv-cli-output-volume-controls`, toolkit Principle 9): the human path builds `newSink(cmd)` and routes the `Checking runtime dependencies…` banner, per-check `[ OK ]` rows, and the `All checks passed.` tail through `Notef` (chatter, dropped by `--quiet`); **`[FAIL]` rows carry the remediation hint** (actionable error detail) and are written to **ungated stderr** so they survive `--quiet`, along with the non-zero exit. The `--json` path is untouched — `--quiet --json` emits exactly the JSON document to stdout |
| `status` | `status.go` | List tmux sessions with window counts via `internal/tmux.ListSessions()` + `ListWindows()`. No server required. **`--json`** (`260717-c424-toolkit-standards-conformance`, toolkit Principle 2): emits a stable JSON array of `{name, windows}` to stdout via `writeSessionStatusJSON(ctx, cmd, server, sessions)` (context-first arg order); human output unchanged otherwise. **Empty-vs-error semantics** (both mirror the human path, both verified empirically): a **cleanly-absent** server (no tmux server for the `runkit` socket) is empty-success — `[]` + exit 0, stderr empty (deliberate `internal/tmux.ListSessions` behavior — an empty result is data, not a failure); an **errorful unreachability** (stale socket / permission — a genuine tmux failure) surfaces the error on stderr with a non-zero exit and **no partial JSON** on stdout (unlike the human path, which prints a per-session error line and continues, the JSON path fails the whole command so a consumer never parses a truncated document as complete). See [toolkit-standards](toolkit-standards.md) § `status --json` empty-vs-error semantics |
| `url` | `url.go` | **Prints the config-derived run-kit server URL** (`260718-icxz-skill-display-topic-url-retire-context`) — `http://<host>:<port>\n` from `config.Load()` (`RK_HOST`/`RK_PORT`, default `127.0.0.1:3000`, port-validated) to `cmd.OutOrStdout()`, exit 0, empty stderr. `Args: cobra.NoArgs`, `SilenceUsage`. The derivation is **byte-equal to the deleted `context.go` `serverURL()`** (`fmt.Sprintf("http://%s:%d", cfg.Host, cfg.Port)`) and reuses `internal/config.Load()` — no `.env` read, no port-owner/liveness probe. It is a **config-derived heuristic** (what the server *would* bind given this environment), stated plainly in the `Long` text — NOT proof a server is running; smarter port-owner discovery is a deferred enhancement, and `rk url` existing is the seam that keeps that door open. It is the **stable server-URL seam** an agent (or the `rk skill` bundle's "Where am I" recipe) uses in place of the retired `rk context` extraction (`rk context 2>/dev/null \| grep 'Server URL' \| awk '{print $NF}'`). Registered on `rootCmd` in `root.go`; appears in `help-dump` automatically. Covered by `url_test.go` (defaults + `RK_HOST`/`RK_PORT` override, empty stderr, registration) |
| `skill` | `skill.go` | **The toolkit `<tool> skill` contract** (`260717-agst-rk-skill-agent-setup-hooks-only`; gained **topic pages** in `260718-icxz-skill-display-topic-url-retire-context`) — prints run-kit's canonical **static** agent skill bundle (a one-page usage briefing: when to reach for rk, its capabilities, composition, gotchas) as raw markdown to `cmd.OutOrStdout()`, **byte-identical** to `docs/site/skill.md`, empty stderr, exit 0. `SilenceUsage`. No rendering/pager/framing — stdout is data; static-only (carries NO session/pane/server-URL state — an agent derives its location directly via the core bundle's "Where am I" recipe and the server URL from `rk url`, the dynamic residue formerly served by the retired `rk context`), so its bytes never vary by where/when it runs. **Topic pages (`260718-icxz`, per the merged shll skill standard, PR #47):** `Args` widened `cobra.NoArgs` → **`cobra.MaximumNArgs(1)`**; bare `rk skill` prints the core bundle, `rk skill <topic>` prints one topic page (`docs/site/skill/<topic>.md`) under the same byte-identical/stdout-only contract, and an **unknown topic fails fast** — `usageError(fmt.Errorf("unknown topic %q (valid: %s)", topic, …))` → **usage-class exit 2**, error naming the valid topics on **stderr**, **empty stdout** (never a silent empty document, never exit 0). Topics live in a `map[string][]byte` (`skillTopics`, v1: `display` → the panes/iframes/Visual-Display-Recipe depth that would blow the core's ≤150 budget); `skillTopicNames()` returns them sorted for a deterministic error message. Bare `rk skill` **never inlines** any topic page. **Embed mechanism (mirrors shll's `standards`, extended per-topic):** the canonical `docs/site/skill.md` **and each `docs/site/skill/<topic>.md`** sit above the `app/backend/` module root so `//go:embed` cannot reach them directly; `scripts/sync-skill.sh` (`set -euo pipefail`, runs from repo root; also wired as a `//go:generate` directive in `skill.go`) copies **both** the core bundle → `cmd/rk/skill/skill.md` and the display topic → `cmd/rk/skill/display.md` (one `sync` call per file — add a row per new topic), which `//go:embed skill/skill.md` (`skillBundle`) and `//go:embed skill/display.md` (`skillDisplayTopic`) embed — so a clean `go build ./...` (which runs no script) compiles. `skill_test.go` is the drift guard — **one byte-equality + one line-budget test per embedded file**: `TestSkillEmbedMatchesCanonical` / `TestSkillBundleWithinLineBudget` for the core, and `TestSkillDisplayEmbedMatchesCanonical` / `TestSkillDisplayWithinLineBudget` for the topic (each `bytes.Equal`s the embed against its `../../../../docs/site/...` canonical, hinting `scripts/sync-skill.sh` on failure, and pins ≤150 lines — the standard's ceiling; the display topic is 81 lines), plus command tests `TestSkillCmdPrintsBundleByteIdentical` / `TestSkillBareStillPrintsCoreBundle` / `TestSkillDisplayPrintsTopicByteIdentical` / `TestSkillUnknownTopicFailsFast`. Registered on `rootCmd` in `root.go`; appears in `help-dump` automatically (cobra-tree walk); topic pages render at `/run-kit/skill/<topic>` on shll.ai for free on next pull |
| `init-conf` | `initconf.go` | Scaffold default tmux.conf to `~/.rk/tmux.conf` from embedded config and create `~/.rk/tmux.d/` drop-in directory. `--force` to overwrite config (tmux.d contents untouched) |
| `notify` | `notify.go` | `rk notify <message>` (optional `--title` flag) — sends a Web Push notification to all subscribed devices. Resolves the local server base URL via `config.Load()` (`RK_HOST`/`RK_PORT`, default `127.0.0.1:3000` — the same derivation the `url` command exposes) and POSTs `{title, body}` to `{base}/api/notify` under an 8s context timeout. **Fail-silent**: any failure (server unreachable, POST error, non-2xx, timeout) → exit 0 with no stdout/stderr (`SilenceErrors`/`SilenceUsage` set) so a notify failure never stalls the caller (the fab-kit operator loop). Registered on `rootCmd` in `root.go` `init()`. See `## Web Push Notifications` (`260615-xd9r-web-push-notifications`) |
| `riff` | `riff.go` | Create a worktree, open a new tmux window in it, and launch a Claude Code session. Repeatable pane flags: `--skill <skill>` (claude pane), `--cmd <cmd>` (shell pane) — argv order sets pane order; bare forms allowed (blank claude / bare shell). Layout flags: `--layout <name>` accepts 6 canonical tmux layouts + 6 shortforms (`a`/`t`/`h`/`v`/`deck-h`/`deck-v`); default `auto` picks by pane count. Preset flags: positional `rk riff <preset>` or `--preset <name>` resolve config-defined presets (`riff.presets.<name>` in `fab/project/config.yaml`); `--list-presets` prints them and exits. Fan-out: `--fan-out N` spawns N identical windows in parallel, each with its own `wt` worktree. `-- <wt-flags...>` passthrough to `wt create`. Preconditions: `$TMUX` set + `wt` on PATH (fast-fail, exit 1 — the operational/precondition class since `260717-rex1`; was 2). Launcher resolved by shelling out to `fab agent --print` (fab-kit's default-tier session command) via `resolveLauncher`; silent best-effort fallback to `claude --dangerously-skip-permissions` when `fab` is absent/fails. All subprocess calls via `exec.CommandContext` (wt: 30s, tmux: 10s). `tmux.OriginalTMUX` restored in child env so tmux targets the user's current server. Exit codes since `260717-rex1` conform to the toolkit convention (Principle 4): precondition (`$TMUX` unset / `wt` missing) → 1 (operational), validation/usage (unknown layout, invalid `--count`, unknown/conflicting preset) → 2, subprocess (wt/tmux non-zero, parse failure, timeout) → 3. A manual flag-parse error (`rk riff --nope`, `DisableFlagParsing` bypasses the root `FlagErrorFunc`) is wrapped locally as the CLI-local `usageError` (exit 2) so the central `execute()` seam owns the code; the riff-engine `*riff.ExitCodeError` path still `os.Exit`s its own class code directly. See [toolkit-standards](toolkit-standards.md) § principles P4 and `rk-riff.md` for full reference |
| `help-dump` | `help_dump.go` | **Hidden build tooling** (`Hidden: true`) — not in user-facing help, self-excludes from its own dump. Emits the CLI help tree as JSON to stdout, or to a file when an optional `[output-path]` arg is given (`cobra.MaximumNArgs(1)`, stdlib `os.WriteFile` 0o644, no subprocess — pure in-process Cobra introspection per §I). `captureNode` walks `rootCmd.Commands()` recursively to full depth, dropping `completion`, `help`, and any `Hidden` node at every level (a hidden parent's subtree is dropped entirely) via `includeInDump`; leaves serialize `"commands":[]` (non-nil slice), never `null`. Per-node fields `name`/`path`/`short`/`usage`/`text` come from `cmd.Name()`/`CommandPath()`/`Short`/`UseLine()`/`UsageString()` (raw, newlines preserved). The **frozen JSON contract** is `{tool:"run-kit", version, schema_version:1 (const), root:node}`, mirroring `sahil87/shll.ai` `help/wt.json`. **`captured_at` is deliberately NOT emitted** (removed in `260717-c424-toolkit-standards-conformance`): the toolkit `help-dump` standard forbids it as a rule "with teeth" — the capture timestamp is owned by the shll.ai puller (a tool cannot know its own capture time), which stamps it after capture. That fix dropped the `dump.CapturedAt` field, the `nowUTC` timestamp package-var + the `now` param on `buildDump` (now `buildDump(root, version)`), and the `time` import; the pure builder stays the test seam. `tool` became `"run-kit"` with `schema_version` staying `1` — a value change within the frozen shape, not a shape change — when the canonical name flipped in `260709-gidk-swap-canonical-cli-name-run-kit`; `root.name`/`root.path`/`usage`/`text` follow automatically from the Cobra `Use: "run-kit"` root. `version` comes from `displayVersion()` (ldflags `-X main.version`, never hardcoded). shll.ai **pulls** this dump by running the CLI's `help-dump` itself on a schedule and capturing the output — the in-repo release-pipeline does not publish it (pull model, `260603-iak3`, see `## Release Flow & CI/CD`); `help-dump` remains the single contract surface shll.ai depends on |
| `agent-setup` | `agent_setup.go` | Install (`--uninstall`) the agent-harness hooks that write the `@rk_agent_state` pane option; JSON merge with a diff + consent prompt before writing, `--yes`/`-y` (non-interactive consent) + `--dry-run` (preview, wins over `--yes`) + a non-TTY refusal naming `--yes` (`260717-c424`). Full consent flow + hook mechanism in [agent-state](agent-state.md) § `rk agent-setup`. **`--quiet`** (`260717-f8yv-cli-output-volume-controls`, toolkit Principle 9): the RunE builds `newSink(cmd)` threaded through `runAgentSetup`/`applyAgentConfig`/`applyAgentHooks`/`removeLegacySkill`; informational **status lines** (`… hooks already … — nothing to do.`, `… wrote ….`, `… skipped (no changes written).`, the legacy rk-display-skill removal narration) route through `Notef` (chatter, dropped by `--quiet`). The settings **diff routes PER CONSENT MODE** via `consent.diffWriter(sink)`: on the **interactive-prompt** and **`--dry-run`** paths it is **data** (never gated — a consent prompt without the diff it asks about is a dark pattern, and a dry-run's diff is the explicitly-requested output), while on the **`--yes`** path (write already authorized) it is **chatter**, so `--yes --quiet` is fully silent on success while `--yes` non-quiet still shows the diff on stderr (cycle-1 rework — the diff had been written to `sink.data` unconditionally before `authorizeWrite`, printing the full diff to stdout under `--yes --quiet`). The interactive prompt itself (prompt suffix / dry-run note, via `authorizeWrite` on `sink.data`) and the non-TTY refusal (`errNonInteractiveConsent`, an error) are never gated |
| `reaper` | `reaper.go` | Operator-invoked janitor: scans `/tmp/tmux-{uid}/` and reaps every artifact matching `--prefix` (default `rk-test`) — live servers killed, dead sockets/`*.lock` removed; dry-run by default (`--yes`/`--force` to act; `--force` also bypasses the dangerous-prefix guard for an empty/≤3-char prefix; `_rk-ctl`/`rk-daemon` skipped unconditionally). Output all via `cmd.OutOrStdout()` (data — a dry-run list is the requested result, an act summary is the record of a destructive mutation), so **`--quiet` legitimately changes nothing** (no sink conversion). **Default 10-entry-per-list display cap + `--all`** (`260717-f8yv-cli-output-volume-controls`, toolkit Principle 9, mirroring `shll changelog`'s 10-release cap): `renderDryRun`'s candidate list caps at `reaperListCap` (10), and `renderReapSummary`'s `killed` and `removed` lists cap at 10 **each** (`renderCappedNames`, per-list); a **stated truncation notice** `… and N more; pass --all to list all` (`renderTruncationNotice`) prints whenever a list is truncated (silent truncation reads as completeness). The **`--all`** bool restores the full list on either path. The cap is **display-only**: header counts stay **exact** (computed from the full `ReapResult`), `--yes`/`--force` still reap **every** match regardless of what was listed, and the dangerous-prefix guard, `_rk-ctl`/`rk-daemon` skips, and dry-run-by-default behavior are unchanged. The `Long` help text gained a sentence describing the cap/`--all`; `help_dump_test.go` asserts structure dynamically (no golden fixture) |

## Embedded Frontend Assets

`app/backend/build/embed.go` exposes `//go:embed all:frontend` as `build.Frontend` (`embed.FS`). During development, `frontend/` contains only `.gitkeep` (empty FS). Production builds copy `app/frontend/dist/` into `app/backend/build/frontend/` before `go build`.

`api/spa.go` uses dual-mode serving:
- **Production**: `hasEmbeddedAssets()` detects real build output (more than `.gitkeep`), serves from `embed.FS` via `mountEmbeddedSPA()`
- **Development**: Falls back to filesystem-based serving from `app/frontend/dist/` via `mountFilesystemSPA()` (Vite dev server handles frontend)

Both modes include SPA fallback (serve `index.html` for non-matching paths) and API/relay route guards.

## Version Management

- **Source of truth**: `VERSION` file at repo root — plain semver string (e.g., `0.1.0`), no `v` prefix
- **Build injection**: `scripts/build.sh` reads `VERSION` and passes `-X main.version=$(cat VERSION)` via ldflags
- **Go variable**: `var version = "dev"` in `root.go` — defaults to `"dev"` for local `go build` without ldflags
- **Displayed by**: the `--version`/`-v` global flag (Cobra built-in — there is no `version` subcommand; `rk version` exits 1 `unknown command`); also read by `rk update` (shows current version, compares with latest via `brew info --json=v2`)
- **Version output string**: since `260709-gidk-swap-canonical-cli-name-run-kit` both `rk --version` and `run-kit --version` print `run-kit version <v>` (dev builds: `run-kit version dev`). The string flows from Cobra's version template, which prints the root's display name (`Use: "run-kit"`), so it is invocation-name-agnostic — no per-name divergence
- **Exposed to the web UI over the state socket** (since `260713-4zap-update-notify-one-click-upgrade`; transport is the state socket since `260716-qf3j-state-socket` — was the SSE stream): `cmd/rk/serve.go` plumbs the ldflags `main.version` into `*api.Server` via `SetVersion(version)` after `NewRouterAndServer`, which seeds the server-global `version` cached global slot (replayed once after `hello` — the version is fixed for the process lifetime). There is deliberately **no `GET /api/version`** — the socket connect is the moment the client needs it, and the reconnect after a `rk update`-driven daemon restart delivers a *different* version, which is exactly the signal the frontend's auto-reload guard keys on. Also fed to `internal/updatecheck.New(version, selfBrew)` (the running version is the run-kit-row comparison source; `selfBrew` gates its self-match). See § State Socket (global-slot replay), § SSE Hub (`event: version`) and § API Server version/checker wiring below

## Build Pipeline

`scripts/build.sh` encapsulates the full production build (frontend-first for embed):

1. `cd app/frontend && pnpm build` — produces `app/frontend/dist/` (with vendor chunk splitting: `xterm` chunk for `@xterm/xterm`, `@xterm/addon-fit`, `@xterm/addon-web-links`; `router` chunk for `@tanstack/react-router`; plus lazy-loaded component chunks for `CommandPalette`, `ThemeSelector`, `CreateSessionDialog`). `zustand` is bundled as a production dependency.
2. Copy `app/frontend/dist/` → `app/backend/build/frontend/` (Go embed cannot reference `../` paths)
3. Read version from `VERSION` file
4. `CGO_ENABLED=0 go build -ldflags "-X main.version=${VERSION}" -o ../../dist/run-kit ./cmd/run-kit`

Output: `dist/run-kit` — single static binary with embedded frontend assets, tmux config, and baked-in version.

`justfile` recipes: `build` delegates to `scripts/build.sh`, `release` delegates to `scripts/release.sh`.

## PWA Layer

`vite-plugin-pwa` (devDependency) adds Progressive Web App support to the Vite build. Configured in `app/frontend/vite.config.ts` with `registerType: "autoUpdate"`.

**Manifest**: Generated from the `VitePWA` plugin config in `vite.config.ts` — no separate `manifest.json` file. Specifies `display: "standalone"`, `start_url: "/"`, dark theme colors (`background_color` and `theme_color` set to `#0f1117`), and an icon array (192px, 512px, 512px maskable). The plugin injects a `<link rel="manifest">` tag into the built `index.html` automatically.

**Service worker**: Workbox-generated (`sw.js`). Precaches all static assets (JS, CSS, HTML) from the Vite build output. Runtime caching rules:
- `NetworkOnly` for URL patterns matching `/api/` and `/relay/` — SSE streams and WebSocket connections always hit the server
- `navigateFallback: "/index.html"` — ensures TanStack Router client-side routes work when served from cache (e.g., homescreen launch to `/{session}/{window}`)

Updates are silent (`registerType: "autoUpdate"`) — the service worker detects new builds and caches updated assets without user interaction or reload prompts.

**Build output**: `app/frontend/dist/` gains `sw.js` and `manifest.webmanifest` alongside the existing Vite output. These files are copied into `app/backend/build/frontend/` by `scripts/build.sh` and served by the Go backend via the existing SPA static serving — no backend changes required.

**Icons**: Canonical SVG mark at `app/frontend/public/icon.svg` (hexagonal cube, transparent background). Generated variants in `app/frontend/public/generated-icons/`: `favicon.svg` (copy of icon.svg), `icon-192.png`, `icon-512.png`, `icon-512-maskable.png` (PNGs have solid `#0f1117` dark background with 20% padding, maskable has 40%). Generated by `scripts/generate-icons.sh` (uses `sharp` Node library). Run via `just icons`.

## Web Push Notifications

`260615-xd9r-web-push-notifications` lets any process on the box — primarily the fab-kit operator agent via `rk notify` — deliver a real OS-level notification that reaches the user **even when the RunKit PWA tab is closed**. This is the only browser-native mechanism that delivers to a closed tab: the *browser's* push service wakes the registered service worker, which shows the notification. It is the intended eventual replacement for fab-kit's `ntfy.sh` default (one feed across all operators on the box, content stays on infra the user runs).

**End-to-end delivery model**: a shell process runs `rk notify "msg"` → POSTs `{title, body}` to the local server `POST /api/notify` → the server iterates stored `PushSubscription`s and sends each a Web Push via `webpush-go` signed with the server's VAPID **private** key → the browser's push service wakes the registered service worker → `sw.js`'s `push` handler calls `self.registration.showNotification(title, {body, icon, data})` → the user sees an OS notification with the tab closed.

**`Notify` signature carries an optional deep-link URL (`260714-r7rq`)**: `push.Notify(ctx, title, body, url string)` — the 4th `url` param is threaded into the `payload` JSON as `url,omitempty` (empty ⇒ omitted, and the SW falls back to the app root on click). The only URL producer today is the waiting-push watcher (§ Web Push on Sustained Waiting → deep-link URL, `/{server}/{N}?view=chat` for chat-capable waiting windows); the generic `/api/notify` path (`api/push.go`) and `rk notify` (`cmd/rk/notify.go`) pass `""`.

**Service worker** (`app/frontend/public/sw.js`): a hand-written service worker served at the origin root `/sw.js` (whole-app scope). Its `push` handler parses the JSON payload `{title, body, icon?, url?}` (default title `"RunKit"`, default icon `/generated-icons/icon-192.png`) and tolerates an empty / non-JSON payload by falling back to defaults; it stores the deep-link `url` on the notification via `showNotification(title, { body, icon, data: { url } })`. **Its `notificationclick` handler focuses an already-open RunKit tab and NAVIGATES it to the deep-link target** (or `openWindow`s a new tab at the target), falling back to the app root `/` when no `url` was carried (`260714-r7rq`). Two safety details: (a) the URL is normalized through `sameOriginPath(value)` — it must start with `/` but **NOT `//`** (a protocol-relative `//evil.example` resolves to an EXTERNAL origin), and the resolved `new URL(value, origin).origin` is belt-and-braces compared to the SW's own origin — so a malformed/hostile payload can never redirect off-origin; (b) `client.navigate()` REJECTS for uncontrolled clients (`matchAll` uses `includeUncontrolled: true`) and may be unavailable in some browsers, so the call is chained `.catch(() => client.focus())` — a rejection must never propagate into `waitUntil` (it would surface as an unhandled SW error). **This is a separate file from any Workbox/`vite-plugin-pwa`-generated SW** — the current frontend ships only this hand-written `public/sw.js` and a static `public/manifest.json` linked from `index.html` (the `## PWA Layer` section above describes the earlier `vite-plugin-pwa` build path; the manifest/SW generation tooling is not wired in the current tree). Registered on app load via `navigator.serviceWorker.register('/sw.js')` from `app/frontend/src/main.tsx`, guarded by `'serviceWorker' in navigator` so unsupported / insecure-context environments silently skip registration.

**Secure-context constraint**: service workers and `PushManager` require a **secure context — HTTPS or `localhost`**. The user typically hits run-kit on `localhost:3000` (or behind a TLS reverse proxy such as Tailscale Serve), both secure contexts, so it is satisfied in practice — but raw-IP / plaintext non-localhost access cannot subscribe (registration is skipped silently, no error).

**State persistence** (Constitution §II — No Database): the `internal/push` package owns two JSON files under `~/.rk/` — `vapid.json` (the VAPID keypair, private key written mode **`0600`**, never served) and `push-subscriptions.json` (the subscription array, de-duped by `endpoint`). See § Backend Libraries. There is no `/api/push/unsubscribe` in v1; dead subscriptions are pruned server-side on `404`/`410` during send.

**Fail-silent discipline** (end-to-end, constitution-aligned): every layer fails silently on its own prerequisite being absent. `rk notify` exits 0 with no output on any failure (server unreachable / non-2xx / timeout) so a notify failure never stalls the operator loop; the send fan-out tolerates individual subscription failures and prunes dead endpoints; the frontend subscribe flow aborts silently when permission is denied or the context is insecure / unsupported. The opt-in is a Cmd+K palette action with a terminal-themed label (NOT a bell) — see `ui-patterns.md` § Notifications (Web Push opt-in).

## Release Flow & CI/CD

**Release script** (`scripts/release.sh`): accepts bump level (`patch`/`minor`/`major`), increments `VERSION` file semver, commits with message `v{version}`, creates git tag `v{version}`, pushes commit + tag. Tag push triggers CI.

**GitHub Actions** (`.github/workflows/release.yml`): triggers on `v*` tag push. Steps: checkout → setup Go (from `go.mod`) → setup Node 20 + pnpm → install frontend deps → build frontend → copy dist to backend → cross-compile 4 targets → create GitHub Release with tarballs → update Homebrew tap.

Cross-compile targets: `darwin/arm64`, `darwin/amd64`, `linux/arm64`, `linux/amd64`. Each target built with `CGO_ENABLED=0` and ldflags. Output: `rk-{os}-{arch}.tar.gz` tarballs uploaded to GitHub Release via `softprops/action-gh-release`.

**Help-tree publish to shll.ai — pull, not push (`260603-iak3-teardown-shllai-publish-ci`):** the release job does not publish the help tree. shll.ai's integration model is **pull**: shll.ai runs `rk help-dump` itself on a schedule and captures the output. A **push** step (each toolkit CLI producing its help JSON in CI and PR-ing it into shll.ai) is intentionally absent — it would be redundant work and a redundant attack surface (dual writers to `help/run-kit.json` could race). CI carries no `SHLLAI_TOKEN` reference. The hidden `rk help-dump` subcommand is the single contract surface shll.ai pulls from (see `## CLI Subcommands`). The `release` job's final step is **Update Homebrew tap**.

**Homebrew tap update** (the **final** step in the `release` job): computes SHA256 for all 4 tarballs, clones `sahil87/homebrew-tap` via the `HOMEBREW_TAP_TOKEN` secret (exported as `TAP_TOKEN`), generates `Formula/run-kit.rb` from `.github/formula-template.rb` (placeholder substitution via `sed`), commits with message `run-kit ${version}`, and pushes. The output path/filename and commit message follow the `run-kit` formula name; tarball artifact names stay `rk-{os}-{arch}.tar.gz` with a single `rk` member (the physical binary is not renamed; the formula renames it at install time). (`260709-gidk-swap-canonical-cli-name-run-kit`)

## Homebrew Distribution

**Formula**: `Formula/run-kit.rb` in `sahil87/homebrew-tap` (generated by CI from `.github/formula-template.rb`; the formula class is `RunKit` and the file/name are `run-kit`). (`260709-gidk-swap-canonical-cli-name-run-kit`) Public repo — plain URL downloads, no auth token needed. Platform detection via `on_macos`/`on_linux` + `on_arm`/`on_intel`. Version and SHA256 values substituted by CI. **Sequencing dependency** (out of this repo's scope, but binding): `sahil87/homebrew-tap` must gain `formula_renames.json` mapping `"rk": "run-kit"` (and drop the old `Formula/rk.rb`) before/with the next release so existing `rk` installs upgrade seamlessly via brew's rename redirect.

Install flow: `brew install sahil87/tap/run-kit` (fully qualified — the shll meta-CLI always installs qualified, so the unqualified-`brew install`-core-collision constraint does not apply). Update: `rk update` (or `run-kit update`).

**Canonical command name — `run-kit`, with `rk` as the permanent alias**: `run-kit` is the **canonical** command; `rk` is a permanently-supported, fully-interchangeable short alias. The Homebrew-core unqualified-install conflict that would otherwise force the short name does not apply — the shll meta-CLI always installs fully qualified. (`260709-gidk-swap-canonical-cli-name-run-kit`, `260707-ook7-run-kit-command-alias`) What the canonical-name model entails:

- **Formula real-vs-alias**: `def install` does `bin.install "rk" => "run-kit"` then `bin.install_symlink bin/"run-kit" => "rk"` — the tarball's `rk` member is **renamed at install time** to `run-kit` (the real binary), and `rk` becomes the symlink back. The formula class is `RunKit`, published as `Formula/run-kit.rb`; the `test do` block asserts BOTH `#{bin}/run-kit --version` and `#{bin}/rk --version` match `"run-kit version"` (the `--version` flag, NOT a `version` subcommand; see § Version Management).
- **Cobra root**: `Use: "run-kit"` + matching `Short` (static string — argv[0]-dynamic `Use` was rejected for help-dump determinism, since shll.ai regenerates the help JSON on a schedule and its output must not depend on which name invoked the CLI). Version output prints `run-kit version <v>` for both invocation names.
- **help-dump**: `tool: "run-kit"` (`schema_version` stays `1`) — see § CLI Subcommands (`help-dump` row).
- **`upgrade.go` moved wholly to `run-kit` markers**: `/Cellar/run-kit/` install-detection marker, `sahil87/tap/run-kit` brew refs, `/bin/run-kit` daemon-restart bin path. **No dual-marker back-compat** in code: an old installed binary runs its OWN old logic (self-resolves under `/Cellar/rk/`, brew's `formula_renames` redirects the upgrade to `run-kit`, and the persistent `rk` symlink still exists for the daemon restart), so the transition completes without new-binary back-compat.
- **Shell completion binds BOTH names** (zsh/bash): after the `Use` swap cobra generates completion for `run-kit` only, so `shell_init.go` appends an extra `compdef _run-kit rk` (zsh) and an extra `complete … rk` line reusing `__start_run-kit` (bash) so the daily-typed `rk` keeps tab completion. fish/powershell keep cobra's single-name binding.

**Invariants — internals stay `rk`**: the Go module path (`module rk`), `cmd/rk/` directory, `RK_*` env vars, `rk-daemon` socket/session names, `~/.rk/` config dir, `dist/rk`/`bin/rk` build outputs, and release-artifact/tarball names (`rk-{os}-{arch}.tar.gz`, single `rk` member — the physical binary is not renamed; the formula renames at install time) are all unchanged. `rk` remains a real on-PATH executable name **indefinitely** — installed agent-setup hooks embed `/opt/homebrew/bin/rk` and fab-kit skills gate on `command -v rk`. Both names stay fully interchangeable for every subcommand. The effect is **release-gated** (reaches installed users on the first release after merge) and requires the tap-repo `formula_renames.json` `{"rk": "run-kit"}` follow-up to land before/with that release (see § Homebrew Distribution).

## Boards Feature

Pane boards are named collections of pinned tmux windows rendered as a horizontal pane dashboard at `/board/$name`. Since `260718-co9z-link-based-board-pinning` the model is **link-based and server-scoped**: a pinned window is `link-window`'d into its own single-window session `_rk-pin-<id>` while staying a member of its home session (dual presence — visible in SESSIONS AND on the board), and a board is the **set of pin-sessions sharing an `@rk_board` SESSION var** (not a tmux session itself, and not a `@rk_board` server-option encoding). Boards are server-scoped because `link-window`/`move-window` can't cross tmux servers — the board *list* is summarized across reachable servers, but there is no cross-server window union. A board exists only while ≥1 pin carries its name (no empty boards, no registry). Unpin is a `kill-session` on the pin-session (the window survives via its home link) with a last-link recovery path when the pin link is the window's only link. See `tmux-sessions.md` § Pin Sessions and § `@rk_board` for the full pin/unpin/reorder contract, the three session vars (`@rk_board`/`@rk_home`/`@rk_board_order`), order keys, and the pin-session-first direct-attach relay.

### Route Placement

| Route | View | Layout |
|-------|------|--------|
| `/board/$name` | Cross-server pane dashboard | Wrapped in the shared `<Shell>` grid (same wrapper as AppShell). Sidebar grid area = unified `<Sidebar currentServer={null}>`; topbar = `<TopBar mode="board">`; content = `DesktopRow`/`MobileCarousel`; bottombar = shared `<BottomBar>` (new on this route) |

`/board/$name` is registered as a child of `rootRoute` in `app/frontend/src/router.tsx`, peer to `serverLayoutRoute`. It does NOT mount AppShell — boards aggregate windows across servers, so AppShell's single-server chrome semantics (server-scoped breadcrumbs, server-scoped command-palette actions) do not apply. As of `260509-17m3-rotated-shell-layout`, BoardPage shares the AppShell `<Shell>` grid wrapper and renders `<TopBar mode="board">` + `<BottomBar>` in the shell's named areas — the route reuses the chrome topology while routing different breadcrumb / pane-area content into it. BoardPage retains its own `<CommandPalette>` mount because board-route-only entries (Switch / Leave Board View / Cycle Pane Focus) need a registration site, and the AppShell palette doesn't mount on `/board/<name>`. `SessionProvider` lives at the root and exposes per-server state, so the board route renders `<Sidebar currentServer={null} ...>` directly with no special-case. The Sidebar's per-server session groups + Boards section serve discovery and entry from any route. See ui-patterns.md § Boards View for the layout.

### Backend Surface

| Layer | File | Responsibility |
|-------|------|---------------|
| Storage | `app/backend/internal/tmux/board.go` | link-based `Pin` (STAMP-BEFORE-LINK + `LinkWindowToSession`) / `Unpin` (kill-session normal path + last-link recovery: link-into-live-home / recreate-dead-home / collision-guarded `recovered<id>`) / `Reorder`, `pinEntry`, `ListBoardEntries`/`ListBoards`/`GetBoard` (derived from `_rk-pin-*` session vars), the recovery helpers `resolveHomeSession`/`recoverPinToRenamedSession`/`clearMembershipOptions`/`killPinSessionIfPresent`, `ComputeOrderKey`/`nextAppendKey` (lowercase-`a..z` fractional indexing), `BoardOption`/`HomeOption`/`BoardOrderOption` session-var keys, validators (`ValidBoardName`, `ValidWindowID`, `ValidOrderKey`). Pin state lives in `_rk-pin-*` session vars, not a `@rk_board` server-option encoding. (`260602-qn62-move-based-board-pin-sessions`) Pin-session naming (`PinSessionPrefix`/`PinSessionName`/`WindowIDFromPinSession`/`ListPinSessionNames`) lives in `tmux.go` |
| HTTP handlers | `app/backend/api/boards.go` | `handleBoardsList` (rank-aware sort via the pure `sortBoardsByStoredOrder` helper + `settings.GetBoardOrder`), `handleBoardGet`, `handleBoardPin`, `handleBoardUnpin`, `handleBoardReorder`, and `handleBoardOrderPost` (`POST /api/boards/order` — full-list validate/dedup/persist/broadcast, since `260708-a2qd`) — register in `router.go` `buildRouter()`; the pin/unpin/reorder trio each emits its own per-server `board-changed` SSE event, while `handleBoardOrderPost` emits the server-global `board-order` event |
| Interface | `app/backend/api/router.go` `TmuxOps` | `ListBoards`, `GetBoard`, `ListBoardEntries`, `PinBoard`→`tmux.Pin`, `UnpinBoard`→`tmux.Unpin`, `ReorderBoard` (uses `lookupNeighbourKeys` + `ComputeOrderKey` then `tmux.Reorder`). `260602-qn62` removed `NewGroupedSession` and `SetSessionOwnerPID` from the interface + `prodTmuxOps` + `mockTmuxOps`. **Cross-server neighbour resolution** (`260708-rmiq-board-pane-reorder`): `lookupNeighbourKeys` enumerates `ListServers` and aggregates the board's `windowId → orderKey` map across EVERY reachable server (mirroring `GetBoard`/`handleGetBoard`'s cross-server aggregation, `boards.go`), NOT just the moved pane's own server — because a board spans servers (`move-window` can't cross servers, but a board is the union of `_rk-pin-*` sessions sharing an `@rk_board` on ANY server). The `400 neighbour window not found on board` (`neighbourNotFoundError`) fires ONLY when the `before`/`after` windowId is absent from the board on every server. Before this fix the lookup was server-scoped, so on a mixed-server board any move whose new neighbour was pinned from a different server 400'd — failing the reorder and permanently desyncing the client's optimistic preview. A per-server `ListBoardEntries` error is `slog.Warn("board: ListBoardEntries failed", ...)` + skipped (log-and-continue like `GetBoard`/`ListBoards`), so an unreachable server leaves a trace rather than silently degrading to a 400 |
| SSE | `app/backend/api/sse.go` | `BoardEntriesFetcher` (now a one-method `ListBoardEntries` interface for test stubbing), `broadcastBoardChanged(server, payload)`, `event: board-changed` (kebab-case; `change` ∈ `pin`/`unpin`/`reorder` only). Since `260602-qn62`: NO `previousBoardJSON` cache, NO bootstrap-on-first-poll, NO cached-snapshot replay, NO window-kill `cleanup` diff — a killed pinned window's pin-session just disappears from the next live `ListBoardEntries` read. **Separately, `broadcastBoardOrder(order)` + `event: board-order` + the single `cachedBoardOrderJSON` replay slot** (since `260708-a2qd`) — the server-global board-DISPLAY-order broadcast, distinct from the per-server `board-changed`; see the § SSE Hub `broadcastBoardOrder` note |

### Constitution Alignment

- **II (No Database)** — pin state lives only in tmux: the `_rk-pin-*` session structure + its `@rk_board`/`@rk_home`/`@rk_board_order` session vars (a deliberate shift since `260602-qn62` from "a tiny derived server-option value" to "tmux session structure IS the record"). Browser `localStorage` holds only view-local pane widths
- **IV (Minimal Surface Area)** — adds exactly one route (`/board/$name`) with one rendering path (`TerminalClient`/`/relay/{windowId}`); no relay ephemeral subsystem, no `@rk_board` encoding, no startup sweep, no SSE board-cleanup/bootstrap (`260602-qn62`)
- **V (Keyboard-First)** — pin/unpin/switch/cycle reachable via Cmd+K palette; pane focus cycle via Cmd+[/]
- **VI (Tmux Sessions Survive Server Restarts)** — pin state persists with the tmux server across rk-go restarts, so there is NO restore-sweep (since `260602-qn62`); `tmux kill-server` loses the boards on that server (expected and acceptable). An emptied home session (its only window pinned away) persists via the `exit-empty off` backstop (`260602-a1wo`) so unpin can restore the window to it
- **VII (Convention Over Configuration)** — no new env vars, no new config files; reuses the established `@rk_*` user-option pattern

## Design Decisions

- **Go backend + Vite SPA over Next.js monolith** — decouples frontend and backend for independent iteration. Go backend is a stable, long-lived API that outlives any individual frontend. Multi-client API support (web, mobile, CLI) without split API surface
- **Single port architecture** — Go serves API, WebSocket relay, and SPA static files on one port. The two-port split (Next.js :3000, relay :3001) was a Node.js artifact — separate processes required separate ports. Go serves everything in one binary
- **chi over stdlib ServeMux** — chi for middleware chaining (CORS, logging, recovery). Go 1.22+ ServeMux has pattern matching but lacks ergonomic middleware composition
- **TanStack Router over React Router** — type-safe params and search params, built-in loader pattern. Single route `/:session/:window` in the new frontend
- **Vite proxy in dev (not CORS)** — single browser URL, no CORS config needed. WebSocket upgrade works transparently. Go includes chi CORS middleware for production/non-browser clients
- **SPA fallback in Go** — Go serves standalone; TLS termination handled externally via Tailscale Serve when needed
- **SSE (not WebSocket) for session state** — simpler, server-push only, naturally resilient. Module-level hub deduplicates polling across tabs (one `FetchSessions()` per server per interval). Clients indexed by server name (`map[string][]*sseClient`) — broadcast iterates only the target server's slice. `sync.RWMutex` with `RLock` for read-only poll operations, `Lock` for writes. SSE data includes `isActiveWindow` per window, enabling UI sync when users switch tmux/byobu windows via terminal shortcuts
- **Full snapshots (not diffs)** — small payload (<100 sessions), simple client logic
- **Independent panes per browser client** — no cursor fights, agent pane untouched. The relay pty follows tmux window switches natively (runs `tmux -L runkit attach-session`)
- **Every tmux session is a project** — no config, no "Other" bucket. Project root derived from window 0's `pane_current_path`
- **Config via env vars (not YAML)** — `.env` committed with defaults (`RK_PORT`, `RK_HOST`), `.env.local` for overrides, loaded via `.envrc` (direnv). Go and Vite read `RK_PORT`/`RK_HOST` directly. `dev.sh` translates `RK_PORT+1` for the backend subprocess. No relay port — single port serves everything
- **Dedicated tmux server (`-L runkit`)** — run-kit sessions live on a named tmux server `runkit` with its own config (`internal/tmux/tmux.conf` loaded via `-f`). The default tmux server is also queried for session discovery (read-only display of external sessions). This replaces byobu integration: `CreateSession()` uses plain `tmux new-session` on the runkit server (no byobu dependency). The `runkit` server provides isolation, a custom status bar matching run-kit's dark theme, and byobu-style F-key keybindings (F2/F3/F4). `SessionInfo` carries a `Name` field; `ProjectSession` has `Name` and `Windows` fields. The caller passes the target server name to each tmux operation
- **Multi-server session enumeration** — `ListSessions(ctx, server)` queries the specified tmux server. The API layer calls it once per server (e.g., `runkit` and `default`), merging results. Session-group filtering applies to both servers. See `docs/memory/run-kit/tmux-sessions.md`
- **Derived chrome (not slot injection)** — Single-view model means only one chrome state (terminal-focused). Top bar and bottom bar derive content from the current session:window selection. No `setLine2Left`/`setLine2Right`/`setBottomBar` setters. Split React Context preserved for performance (state vs dispatch).
- **Root-mounted multi-server SessionProvider over one state socket** — One `SessionProvider` instance lives at the root above `<Outlet />` (in `RootWrapper`) and is shared by every route. State is keyed per server (`Map<string, T>`); `currentServer: string | null` is dispatched from the matched route via `useMatches()`. The provider drives ONE `StateSocket`: servers are subscribed lazily — current server eager, others via `attachServer(name)` — over the single wire. Provider survives server-route switches (no remount, no state rebuild) and lets the Board route render the same unified `<Sidebar>` as AppShell with `currentServer === null`. Cross-server `board-changed` events are multiplexed through `subscribeBoardChange` so cross-server hooks (`useBoards`, `useWindowPins`) add no separate connections. Rejected: per-route providers bridged via a sibling cross-server context — adds two contexts, double-fetches `/api/servers`, doesn't solve BoardPage sidebar reuse cleanly. Rejected: `Record<string, T>` instead of `Map<string, T>` — Maps give clear "server unknown" vs "server known with empty value" semantics. (`260508-dc0t-multiserver-session-provider`, `260716-qf3j-state-socket`)
- **Single-view layout (sidebar + terminal/dashboard) replaces three pages** — Dashboard and Project page functionality subsumed by the sidebar + Dashboard view. Terminal is the main content on `/:session/:window`; Dashboard renders on `/`. No page transitions.
- **Dashboard as inline component in app.tsx (not separate route layout)** — The Dashboard renders in the terminal area via a conditional branch (`sessionName && windowIndex ? <TerminalClient/> : <Dashboard/>`). This reuses the existing chrome skeleton (top bar, sidebar) and avoids duplicating the app shell layout. Rejected: separate route with dedicated layout — would require lifting sidebar/chrome into a shared layout component and restructuring the route tree.
- **POST-only API client with path-based intent** — Each mutation is a separate function with its own URL (e.g., `killSession(session)` → `POST /api/sessions/:session/kill`). No multiplexed `action` field in request bodies. Formalized as constitution §IX (Uniform HTTP Verb) and brought into full conformance by `260529-jad6` (the last five `.Put(` routes migrated to `POST`; CORS `AllowedMethods` → `[GET, POST, OPTIONS]`). Semantics that would conventionally map to `PUT`/`PATCH` (partial update) live in the path + body contract instead of the verb.
- **Shared chained-`set-option` primitive + "validate-all-then-one-atomic-invocation" partial-merge** (`260529-jad6`) — `WindowOptionOp{Key; Value *string}` + `appendOptionOps(args, target, ops)` is a single reusable primitive for emitting any sequence of `set-option -w` set/unset ops as one `\;`-chained tmux invocation. Both `SetWindowOptions` (the `POST /options` endpoint) and `CreateWindowWithOptions` (window creation) consume it — there is no separate inline option-map construction path.
