The `POST /options` handler pairs this with a strict ordering contract: **all keys are validated (allowlist + per-key rules) before any tmux subprocess is spawned**, so a single invalid key aborts with `400` and zero tmux calls (no partial application), and the merge that does run is one atomic chained invocation the SSE poll can never observe half-applied. This validate-all-then-atomic pattern is the reusable shape for future multi-key tmux mutations. *Why*: partial-merge (present key sets, `null` unsets, absent untouched) avoids the "client clears a field it didn't echo" bug class that a full-replace PUT re-introduces; the key allowlist (`@color`/`@rk_url`/`@rk_type`) bounds the option-name surface passed to `tmux set-option` (§I). *Rejected*: a generic action-dispatcher for all window verbs (weaker per-action validation, fuzzier §I audit surface); PATCH/PUT full-replace (violates §IX / re-introduces the cleared-field bug); passing through arbitrary `@`-prefixed keys (unvalidated surface).
- **Session as server-derived disambiguation context for REST `/select`** (`260529-jad6`) — `handleWindowSelect` resolves the owning session server-side (`ResolveWindowSession`) and issues a session-scoped `select-window -t <session>:@N` (`SelectWindowInSession`) rather than a bare `select-window -t @N`. *Why*: a bare window-id target is ambiguous inside a tmux session group (members keep independent active-window state, so tmux may activate the window on the wrong member — the wrong-window-highlight symptom, live since #198 made tmux the sidebar's source of truth). The session is derived only where tmux semantics require it; the client never sends it (consistent with dropping `$session` from the URL). *Rejected*: a bare-target select with a client-supplied session (puts the session back in the client-facing identity).
- **Sidebar + drawer pattern on mobile** — Desktop sidebar is drag-resizable (default 220px, min 160, max 400, localStorage persist), collapsible. Mobile (< 768px) uses a left-side drawer overlay triggered by `☰`. Preserves session/window tree layout across breakpoints.
- **Prebuilt binaries over build-from-source Homebrew formula** — ship cross-compiled binaries via GitHub Release. Zero build dependencies on user's machine (no Go, Node.js, pnpm). Faster install. Rejected: build-from-source formula (like tu) which requires all build tools. (`260317-ukyz-homebrew-deployment`)
- **`embed.FS` with copy step over restructuring repo** — copy `app/frontend/dist/` into `app/backend/build/frontend/` at build time because Go's `//go:embed` cannot reference files outside the package directory. Simple build-time operation. Rejected: colocating frontend output with Go source (breaks dev workflow). (`260317-ukyz-homebrew-deployment`)
- **VERSION file + ldflags over Go constant** — version sourced from `VERSION` file, injected via `-X main.version=...`. Shell scripts can read/write plain text. No code changes for version bumps. Rejected: Go constant (requires code change per release). (`260317-ukyz-homebrew-deployment`)
- **Cobra over custom CLI parsing** — industry standard, auto-generates help, 5 subcommands is the sweet spot. Rejected: stdlib `flag` (no subcommand support), custom parsing (unnecessary). (`260317-ukyz-homebrew-deployment`)
- **SPA handler dual-mode (embedded FS vs filesystem)** — `hasEmbeddedAssets()` checks whether `frontend/` contains more than `.gitkeep`. Production uses `embed.FS`, dev uses filesystem (Vite handles frontend). Automatic detection, no build tags or env vars needed. (`260317-ukyz-homebrew-deployment`)
- **Active window sync — tmux truth, URL as bookmark** — tmux is the sole source of truth for "current window" per server. The URL is a resumable bookmark used only on mount (and reload); after mount it is derived state, rewritten by an SSE-driven `navigate({ replace: true })` whenever the server-reported `isActiveWindow` differs from the URL. Mount-time alignment fires exactly one `selectWindow` to align tmux to a deep-linked URL (gated by `hasAlignedToUrlRef`). All clients on the same server converge ("yank" semantics) — cross-server tabs stay independent. Sidebar clicks are pure mutations (`selectWindow` only); no client-side timer or debounce (there is no client-owned selection state to protect, so a debounce like the retired 3-second `userNavTimestampRef` must not be re-added). Push channel is tmux control mode (`tmux -CC`) via the `internal/tmuxctl/` package; primary latency target sub-500ms, with a 12-second safety-net poll as backstop. Board cleanup tracks control-mode latency. Rejected: per-tab current window (reintroduces a second writer, doesn't match the dashboard model). Rejected: hooks + `rk notify` + lockfile (incompatible with PR #197's Constitution §II Non-Goal). (`260528-nvlp-active-window-sync`)
  - The `isActiveWindow` that drives this writeback is **event-derived per session group** (two-tier: event-tracked `@wid` authoritative, base `#{window_active}` cold-start/reconnect fallback), not read from the base session pointer alone. The base pointer goes stale when an `rk-relay-*` ephemeral / `rk riff` / external `new-window` moves the active window (group members keep independent pointers), so reading it alone lags the highlight. The derivation lives entirely in the read path — no creator or the ephemeral model is involved, and the frontend writeback is unchanged. See § Active-Window Event Derivation. (`260530-v6hm-active-window-event-derivation`)
- **Sticky modifier state via useRef + forceUpdate** — `useModifierState` uses a ref for the authoritative state and a counter state to trigger re-renders. Ensures `consume()` reads the latest value atomically without stale closure issues.
- **Docked compose strip as native textarea (not xterm input)** — xterm renders to `<canvas>`, blocking OS-level input features. The docked compose strip provides a real `<textarea>` where dictation, autocorrect, paste, and IME all work; Enter sends the buffer plus a trailing `\r` as raw bytes over the focused pane's relay stream. It is a single global, sticky surface with a live focused-pane target, NOT a modal frozen at open. (`260718-dhdj-docked-compose-strip`)
- **Armed modifiers bridge to physical keyboard** — When bottom-bar modifiers (Ctrl/Alt) are armed, a capture-phase `keydown` listener intercepts physical keypresses, translates them to terminal escape sequences (Ctrl+letter → control characters, Alt → ESC prefix), and sends via WebSocket. Prevents xterm from receiving the unmodified key. Ignores real Cmd/Ctrl/Alt held by the OS.
- **File upload via server filesystem (not terminal binary injection)** — Browser uploads file to `POST /api/sessions/:session/upload`, server writes to `.uploads/` in the target window's worktree, path auto-inserted into the docked compose strip's textarea. Works because run-kit server and tmux are always co-located; the browser is the remote part. Session identified by URL param (consistent with other session-scoped endpoints, replaces legacy form field approach)
- **Handler files split by resource domain (not monolithic routes.go)** — Each handler file owns one resource: `sessions.go`, `windows.go`, `directories.go`, `upload.go`, `sse.go`/`state_ws.go` (session-state), `terminals_ws.go` (pane relay mux, since `260717-803u-relay-mux`), `spa.go`, `health.go`. `router.go` owns middleware, dependency interfaces, and route registration only. (`260312-r4t9-go-backend-api`) *(`relay.go` — once the `handleRelay` home — now holds only the shared `upgrader` + `forceTERM`, both consumed by `terminals_ws.go`; folding them in and deleting `relay.go` is a noted deletion candidate since its name no longer matches any endpoint.)*
- **Dependency injection via interfaces for handler testability** — `Server` struct holds `SessionFetcher` and `TmuxOps` interfaces, plus `hostname` (computed via `os.Hostname()` in `NewRouter()`, empty string on failure) and `*metrics.Collector` (created and started in `NewRouter()` with the server context). `TmuxOps` interface includes `SetWindowOptions(ctx, windowID, server, ops []tmux.WindowOptionOp)` and `CreateWindowWithOptions(session, name, cwd, server, ops []tmux.WindowOptionOp)` for the batched/chained window-option operations (the singular `SetWindowOption`/`UnsetWindowOption` and the dedicated `SetWindowColor`/`UnsetWindowColor` remain on the interface with no production callers; window-targeting methods take `windowID string`, create stays session-scoped). `SelectWindowInSession` serves the session-scoped REST `/select`. (`260529-jad6`, `260529-chgz-window-id-routing`) `NewRouter()` wires production implementations; `NewTestRouter()` accepts mocks (including hostname). Enables `httptest.NewRecorder` tests without live tmux. (`260312-r4t9-go-backend-api`)
- **Hostname via health endpoint (not a dedicated endpoint)** — hostname is an OS-level value computed once at startup and stored in `Server` struct. Exposed via `/api/health` response (adding a field to an existing endpoint) rather than a new `GET /api/hostname` route. Minimal surface area, consistent with the single-port architecture. (`260320-uq0k-hostname-browser-title`)
- **Per-window fab enrichment via `fab pane map` (replaces per-session file reading)** — Single `fab pane map --json --all-sessions` subprocess call per SSE tick replaces per-session `.fab-status.yaml` + `.fab-runtime.yaml` file reads. Provides per-window resolution (each worktree window shows its own change/stage) instead of per-session (all windows inherited session-level state). Decouples from internal file formats. `internal/fab` package deleted entirely. The subprocess invokes the `fab` router on PATH (not a hardcoded kit binary path) with `cmd.Dir = repoRoot` so the router can resolve the project's `fab_version` from `fab/project/config.yaml`. (`260313-3vlx-pane-map-enrichment`, `260417-5nok-fix-sidebar-fab-state`)
- **Backend settings file over localStorage-only** — `~/.rk/settings.yaml` via `internal/settings/` package + `GET/PUT /api/settings/theme` endpoints. Survives browser cache clears, works across devices accessing the same server. localStorage kept as synchronous cache for instant reads before API responds on page load. Simple `key: value` text parsing (not yaml.v3) — one field currently, avoids re-adding a heavyweight dependency. Settings are global (not per-server, no `?server=` param). (`260323-7wys-ansi-palette-theme-rework`)
- **Full ANSI palette over minimal color set** — 22 canonical terminal colors per theme enables three consumers from one source: CSS (8 derived colors via `deriveUIColors`), xterm.js (full 22-color theme via `deriveXtermTheme`), and tmux (auto-themed via ANSI colour indices in static tmux.conf). Rejected: 8-color model with separate xterm colors (duplicative, inconsistent). (`260323-7wys-ansi-palette-theme-rework`)
- **Static tmux.conf with ANSI indices over runtime `tmux set -g`** — tmux.conf uses `colour0`-`colour15` indices. Changing xterm.js palette auto-themes tmux chrome (status bar, pane borders, pane-border-format). Zero backend involvement for theme switching. Rejected: runtime tmux commands (complex, fragile, requires backend communication). (`260323-7wys-ansi-palette-theme-rework`)
- **`run-kit.yaml` at git root for per-project preferences (not env vars or server config)** — `config.FindGitRoot()` walks up from `pane_current_path` to locate the git root, then reads/writes `run-kit.yaml` there. Session color is a per-project user preference, not server configuration (which uses env vars per constitution). File is gitignored by convention. Simple line-by-line parsing (no yaml.v3 dependency). (`260416-jn4h-session-window-color-tinting`)
- **Dual storage: `run-kit.yaml` for session color + tmux `@color` for window color** — Session colors need persistence across tmux restarts (file-based). Window colors are ephemeral and tmux-native (user options survive session lifetime but not server restart). Rejected: all in `run-kit.yaml` (would require tracking per-window state in a file, complex synchronization with tmux window lifecycle). (`260416-jn4h-session-window-color-tinting`)
- **Separate SSE event type for metrics (`event: metrics`) over embedding in sessions payload** — Metrics are server-wide (one payload for all clients), while sessions are per-tmux-server and deduplicated. CPU samples change every tick (dedup logically impossible). Separation avoids inflating session payloads and allows independent evolution. Rejected: embedding in sessions payload (sent N times per server, complicates dedup). (`260411-z63r-sidebar-host-window-panels`)
- **Server-side ring buffer with full history per tick over client-side accumulation** — New SSE clients immediately get complete 60-sample CPU sparkline history. No reconnection logic needed to rebuild history. At 60 float64s, ~500 bytes per tick is negligible. Rejected: client-side accumulation from deltas (reconnection complexity, frontend state management). (`260411-z63r-sidebar-host-window-panels`)
- **Path-based reverse proxy over subdomain routing** — `/proxy/{port}/*` keeps all traffic on one origin, avoiding CORS complexity and DNS configuration. Per-port `ReverseProxy` instances cached in `sync.Map` (read-heavy, single-digit entry count). `ModifyResponse` rewrites localhost/127.0.0.1 URLs in HTML `src`/`href`/`action` attributes to proxy paths; handles gzip decompression. JS-constructed URLs are not rewritten (acceptable v1 gap). Rejected: subdomain routing (requires DNS/hosts setup), service worker injection (fragile). (`260416-6b0h-iframe-proxy-windows`)
- **Tmux user-defined options for iframe state over database/config file** — `@rk_type` and `@rk_url` as tmux window options preserve constitution principles II (no database) and VI (sessions survive restarts). State is co-located with the tmux window lifecycle — kill the window, lose the metadata. Reactive via existing SSE polling (no new transport). Rejected: database/config file (violates constitution), window name encoding (fragile). (`260416-6b0h-iframe-proxy-windows`) **`@rk_type` demoted from identity to a default-view HINT (`260714-t97o-web-view-lens`)** — under the window-view lens model (`docs/specs/window-views.md` R1/R5, `ui-patterns.md` § Window Views (Lens Model)), "which view am I in" is per-viewer client state (`?view=` + localStorage), NOT the window's identity. `@rk_type=iframe` now only seeds `defaultView` ("default view = web" when `@rk_url` is also set); the frontend no longer reads it as a render gate and no longer mutates it on a view switch. `@rk_url` stays global substrate state (the shared content address, edited via the web lens's URL bar). Both options and the `POST /options` plumbing are otherwise unchanged (no backend/API change).
- **Extend existing create endpoint with optional rkType/rkUrl over new endpoint** — Adding optional `rkType`/`rkUrl` to `POST /api/sessions/{session}/windows` reuses the existing creation flow. When `rkType` is present, uses `CreateWindowWithOptions` for atomic `\;`-chained tmux command (prevents SSE seeing window before metadata set). When absent, behavior unchanged (standard terminal window). Rejected: separate `POST .../windows/iframe` endpoint (unnecessary surface area). (`260416-6b0h-iframe-proxy-windows`)
- **procfs direct reading over external monitoring tools** — `internal/metrics` reads `/proc/stat`, `/proc/meminfo`, `/proc/loadavg`, `/proc/uptime` directly. No dependency on `top`, `htop`, or monitoring agents. `syscall.Statfs` for disk. All readers return zero values on non-Linux (macOS dev graceful degradation). No new Go dependencies. (`260411-z63r-sidebar-host-window-panels`)
- **In-memory PR-status collector with wholesale-rebuild cleanup + network-isolated three-layer split** — `internal/prstatus.Collector` (mirroring `internal/metrics.Collector`) makes ONE batched `gh api graphql viewer.pullRequests(states: [OPEN, MERGED, CLOSED], orderBy: UPDATED_AT DESC, first: 100)` call on a slow 90s background tick, REPLACES its `byNumber` map wholesale each refresh, and serves a deep-copied `Snapshot()`. Three layers on separate cadences keep the 2.5s SSE hot path network-free: (1) `PrURL`/`PrNumber` are derived from the pane's branch via the `prstatus` background branch refresher (register + snapshot-join, off the hot path — see § Branch→PR Derivation and the next decision); (2) the collector fetches live status behind the 90s tick + on-demand POST; (3) the SSE hub joins status onto any window with a derived `PrURL` via a pure `Snapshot()` read, keyed on the canonical URL. *Why include MERGED/CLOSED, not just OPEN*: a just-merged PR is recently updated, so it sits near the top of the `UPDATED_AT DESC` window and shows its `merged` (purple) state instead of dropping to a bare PR number — the merged dot is reachable and is the most useful signal on a change-bound window. *Why wholesale rebuild*: the `first: 100` recency cap is the eviction — a merged/closed PR shows its terminal state while it stays in the top-100 window, then ages out and drops from the next wholesale rebuild (along with killed windows) — cleanup for free, no eviction logic or window-lifecycle hook (the deciding factor when "how does cleanup happen?" was raised in design). *Why GraphQL not `gh search prs`*: the intake's literal `gh search prs --author @me` argv ERRORS — that subcommand doesn't expose `statusCheckRollup`/`reviewDecision` JSON fields; `gh api graphql` is the standard cross-repo batched mechanism and serves the identical one-call/O(1)/full-status intent (apply-time correction, plan Assumptions #8). *Why in-memory not tmux-option*: re-derivable in one call (Constitution §II — no DB/disk/tmux-option); restart-survival has little value for a 90s cache and a tmux-option would add a two-writer race + manual pruning. *Why injectable `ghExec`/`available` seams*: matches the codebase's exec-seam test pattern, lets table tests stub `gh` output deterministically. *Rejected*: per-PR `gh pr view` polling (doesn't scale — 10 tasks = 10 calls), webhook receiver writing `.status.yaml` (overkill, contradicts fab-kit's poll-free design). gh absent/unauth is a silent no-op (matches `command -v rk`). (`260610-596o-pr-status-sidebar`)
- **Two-tier agent-state + branch-derived PR links (own-your-signals over consuming `fab pane map`)** — run-kit stops consuming Claude-only, fab-root-coupled signals through `fab pane map` and derives them itself: agent lifecycle state (Tier 2) reads the `@rk_agent_state` pane user option written by any harness's hooks (Tier 1 — change/stage — stays fab's), and PR links are derived server-side from the pane's branch. *Why*: the most notification-worthy state (`waiting` — blocked on a human) was invisible in the old two-state `active|idle` model, non-Claude agents showed nothing, and PR visibility was limited to fab-change-bound windows; per constitution Principle X (amended here) hooks carry only the underivable, so PR links (derivable from the branch) must NOT ride a push pipeline. *Reconciler at parse-time*: the shell-command reconciler runs in `internal/tmux.parsePanes` (which already has the pane command + option value on one line) — colocated + unit-testable, mirroring the pure-parse convention; rollup/duration live in `internal/sessions`. *Branch→PR is a NEW per-`(repoDir,branch)` resolver alongside the viewer-wide URL-keyed collector, not a replacement*: the existing `gh api graphql viewer.pullRequests` query has no branch/repo/cwd seam so it cannot express `gh pr list --head`; the two compose (derive URL → join live status by URL). *Rework (T007/T008)*: the resolver was moved OFF the FetchSessions/SSE hot path into a background `BranchRefresher` (register + snapshot-join) after review flagged inline `gh` execution breaking the zero-network-call invariant + the 5s API cap — a shared process-wide `DefaultBranchRefresher` + package-level `Register`/`SnapshotBranchPR` façade keeps `FetchSessions`' signature unchanged. *Clean swap, no dual-source fallback*: agent columns read `—` until `rk agent-setup` runs (single-operator rollout; fallback code contradicts §IV). *Explicit installer, not silent sync*: `rk agent-setup` shows a diff + confirm before mutating user-global config, idempotent marker-keyed merge, `--uninstall` (plus `--yes`/`-y` non-interactive consent and `--dry-run` preview, and a non-TTY refusal naming `--yes` — added by `260717-c424-toolkit-standards-conformance`; full consent flow in [agent-state](agent-state.md) § `rk agent-setup`). *Rejected*: reconciling in `internal/sessions` (duplicates the shell-name set); extending the single graphql query for branch→PR (no scoping seam, misses non-viewer PRs); silent hook sync (surprising for user-config mutation). Full design: [agent-state](agent-state.md), spec [`docs/specs/agent-state.md`](../../specs/agent-state.md). Unblocks fab-kit backlog `[ioku]` (fab pane send/map become convention readers). (`260705-dmex-generic-agent-state-tier`)
- **Toolkit update-notify + one-click upgrade: delegated `shll check-updates` detection + scoped `shll update`, no new deps/routes/DB** — the daemon execs `shll check-updates --json` once per ~6h (`internal/updatecheck`), consumes the per-tool verdicts it returns, and broadcasts the notable-tool set + composite key over the server-global `event: update-available`; the running version rides a set-once `event: version` slot; a `POST /api/update` spawns a **detached** scoped `shll update <matched…>` (fallback `rk update` self when shll is absent); a `POST /api/updates/check` runs the same pass on demand and returns the fresh verdict synchronously. run-kit is the only toolkit tool with a daemon + UI, so it is the only place a passive reminder for the WHOLE toolkit (shll, wt, idea, tu, hop, fab-kit) can live. *Why delegate the check to `shll check-updates` (`260720-n2ai`)*: run-kit previously reimplemented shll's canonical check logic (a manifest HTTP fetch of `https://shll.ai/versions.json`, a `brew list --versions` join, and a hand-rolled sibling threshold evaluation) — two places for the notify policy, roster, and manifest schema to drift as the toolkit evolves. One exec of `shll check-updates --json` replaces those three code paths with a single subprocess under rk's standard discipline (`exec.CommandContext`, argv slice, 30s bound — §I), so the check is defined ONCE, on the shll side (§III Wrap, Don't Reinvent). *Why two backends, not one filtered verdict (`260720-wb3n`)*: the ambient loop and the default `run-kit: Check for Updates` command use shll's `released` manifest source (flag-free — its default, keeping the invocation valid across shll's `--released`→`--source` consolidation); the `incl. patches` command uses the FRESH `--source github` release-tags source because the shll.ai manifest refreshes ~daily and can lag a just-cut release. A github check runs as a SIDE-CHANNEL query — `CheckNow(ctx, SourceGithub)`, no cache write, no `OnQualify` — so the chip, dismissal key, and scoped `shll update` argv stay bound to the notify-policy-bearing released source (the github contract carries no `notify`/`notable`; every row lands `notable=false`, so caching it would wipe a legit released chip and starve the scoped-update argv). The two commands thus stop being "same data, two filters" and become TWO BACKENDS: the default can report all-up-to-date while incl.-patches lists updates, purely from manifest lag — deliberate. *Why the run-kit row is still re-compared locally*: shll can only see the brew-VISIBLE version, but run-kit's restart-relevant truth is the RUNNING ldflags version (brew's on-disk version can legitimately be ahead between upgrade and daemon restart), so rk consumes shll's `latest`+`notify` for that one row but does the comparison locally (producing BOTH `update_available` and `notable`), and keeps its `selfBrew` gate (a go-install/dev rk can't self-update through brew, so its own row is omitted). Sibling verdicts are trusted VERBATIM. *Why the retained semver helpers*: `crossesThreshold`/`anyIncrease`/`parseMajorMinor` survive ONLY as the machinery for that one local run-kit comparison and `New`'s suppression parse — the sibling-wide evaluation moved behind `shll check-updates`. *Why dual failure posture (ambient fail-silent, manual fail-loud)*: the ambient 6h loop skips a failed pass silently and retains the previous verdict (stale-while-revalidate) — a background reminder must never crash or nag on a transient shll hiccup; but a MANUAL `POST /api/updates/check` deserves an honest answer, so `CheckNow` surfaces the failure as a `502`/`409` the client turns into an error toast. *Why an on-demand check endpoint at all*: the only prior surfaces were the ambient chip and a force-update that fired blind — a user could not ask "is anything updatable right now?"; the endpoint runs the SAME code path as the loop and converges on the SAME cached verdict (so a manual notable finding lights the chip immediately). *Why scoped `shll update` not `rk update`*: updating run-kit alone can skew cross-repo contracts (run-kit ↔ fab-kit share `@rk_agent_state`); `shll update <matched…>` keeps the matched tools moving together and delegates to `rk update --skip-brew-update` for run-kit's daemon-restart side effect (§III). It CANNOT run in-process (the restart kills the serving process mid-request), so `POST /api/update` responds `202` then `exec.Command(shllPath, "update", <matched…>)` with `SysProcAttr{Setsid: true}` (log → `~/.rk/update.log`) — **deliberately NOT `exec.CommandContext`-bound** because a detached child must outlive the server and §I's timeout rule only guards against a subprocess *blocking* the server, which a detached spawn cannot. *Why the post-remediation re-check (R17)*: a siblings-only `shll update` never restarts the daemon, so nothing naturally cleared the consumed match — the chip stuck on `updating…`, the cached SSE slot replayed a stale match to every new tab, a later click 409-ed. Firing `OnQualify` on ANY key change (incl. →empty), broadcasting the cleared verdict into the slot, clearing frontend state on key change, and a ~2min post-spawn `RecheckAfter` close the loop end to end. *Why SSE cached slots not a `GET /api/version`*: the two events reuse the exact `server-order`/`board-order` fan-out + cached-on-connect machinery (all clients incl. `?metrics=1`), and the connect IS the moment the client needs the version (§IV). *Why extract `internal/selfpath`*: the brew marker + self-path resolver were duplicated byte-for-byte in `upgrade.go` and `update.go` — the shared package means brew-install detection cannot drift between the CLI and web entry points. *Accepted*: until a shll release carries `check-updates` the not-on-PATH path keeps the checker silent (fail-silent-retain leaves the verdict empty → the chip stays hidden — safe to merge in either order; the PR body notes the feature goes live only with a shll release); a failed brew upgrade leaves the chip on `updating…` until the verdict changes (escape hatches: the palette force path + a page reload); no in-flight lock. *Rejected*: reimplementing the check in rk (drift risk — §III); a github check that WRITES the shared cached verdict (would wipe the released chip + 409 the scoped update — the side-channel posture is load-bearing); silently treating an unknown `source` as released (masks a client bug — 400 instead); an invented client-side boolean instead of echoing `report.Source` (the echo doubles as a defensive check); a shll-side change (the github contract already omits `notify`/`notable` and self-identifies `"source":"github"`); in-process upgrade (restart kills the server); `GET /api/version` (needless surface); a semver DEPENDENCY (the ~20-line hand-rolled compare backs only the one local run-kit row); a frontend-only `updating` timeout (leaves the stale verdict up to 6h); tracking the detached child's exit (it deliberately outlives the daemon); Web Push for update notices (reserved for waiting agents — update notices must not buzz phones, user-decided). Cross-repo: `shll check-updates` is added by shll change `260720-puxw-check-updates-command` (contract only — that repo owns the check logic + policy values; the JSON contract is vendored in rk as `testdata/check-updates.json`). Frontend: `useUpdateNotification()` hook + top-bar L3 UpdateChip (single/multi form) + palette parity (two check commands, `Update Now` as the single update action) — see [ui-patterns](/run-kit/ui-patterns.md) § Update Notification. (`260713-4zap-update-notify-one-click-upgrade`, `260718-d15e-toolkit-manifest-update-notifications`, `260720-n2ai-shll-check-updates-delegation-palette-checks`, `260720-wb3n-github-source-patches-check`)
- **Terminal relay mux (`/ws/terminals`) with per-stream queues + a fair scheduler — one socket per tab, retire `/relay/{windowId}`, keep it SEPARATE from `/ws/state`** — Change 2 of the socket-unification plan collapses N per-pane `/relay/{windowId}` sockets onto ONE `/ws/terminals` connection per tab (binary `[u32 BE streamId][payload]` data frames + JSON `open`/`opened`/`resize`/`close`/`closed` control ops; client-allocated u32 stream ids), so a board holds a fixed 2 WebSockets total (state + terminals). *Why per-stream bounded queues + a non-FIFO fair scheduler are a v1 requirement, not an optimization*: on a muxed socket a shared FIFO gives 1.66s interactive echo p50 under a co-stream flood, vs 32ms with per-stream queues + control/short-frame-priority round-robin at identical goodput (spike 2, `docs/findings/relay-mux-hol.md`) — head-of-line blocking is the mux's one real risk and this fully mitigates it. *Why a full queue pauses the PTY reader (backpressure) rather than dropping bytes*: dropping mid-stream corrupts VT state; the pause pushes the stall into tmux's per-client buffering, the same mechanism a stalled per-pane TCP socket exerted before the mux. *Why stream-level failures become `closed` control events, not socket closes*: one bad window (4004) or attach failure (4001) must not tear down the other panes' streams — the socket outlives any single stream. *Why retire `/relay/{windowId}` with no deprecation shim*: the frontend is the sole consumer (personal tool, no API-compat contract; constitution IV — minimal surface). *Why keep it separate from `/ws/state` (D6, decided against merging)*: bulk binary terminal output must not share a send buffer/scheduler with state events — the terminals scheduler is tuned for interactive-echo fairness under flood, a concern `/ws/state` does not have. *Why the async attach with a placeholder-under-lock (rework S2)*: the per-stream resolve (≤5s) + select + attach must not serialize on the socket read loop behind other panes' keystrokes/opens, so it dispatches to a goroutine after registering a placeholder stream synchronously, keeping duplicate-id/racing-resize/close deterministic. *Why `opened` rides the stream's own queue before data (rework M2)*: the client arms its deferred per-stream reset on `opened`, so a data-before-`opened` ordering wiped the reset; enqueuing `opened` on the stream's own bounded queue (channel FIFO + short-frame priority) guarantees opened→data. *Rejected*: shared FIFO across streams (the 1.66s regression); merging into `/ws/state` (D6); dropping bytes on a full queue (VT corruption); a bespoke window-ID validator (would reintroduce the #205 drift — the mux reuses `validate.ValidateWindowID`). Frontend `RelayMux` singleton + `TerminalClient` port — see [ui-patterns](/run-kit/ui-patterns.md) § Terminal Relay (frontend). (`260717-803u-relay-mux`)
- **Chat live stream as a `kind:"chat"` subscription on `/ws/state`, backfill demoted to the GET (D5), chat SSE retired (D2) — the socket-unification goal state (2 WS + 0 SSE, D6)** — Change 3 of the socket-unification plan moves chat's incremental stream off its dedicated per-view `EventSource` (`GET /api/windows/{id}/chat/stream`) onto the state socket as one more subscription kind, subscribed on chat-lens enter / unsubscribed on leave. Chat was the app's LAST `EventSource` — one HTTP/1.1 pool slot on plaintext origins, the exact starvation class socket-unification exists to eliminate; retiring it takes every route to a **fixed 2 WS + 0 SSE**. *Why demote backfill to the existing `GET /api/windows/{id}/chat` (D5), not snapshot-in-ack*: a rotation can target a large resumed session (`claude --resume` re-stamps `@rk_chat`), so pushing a `Conversation` over the shared socket would head-of-line-block session-state events and break bounded-event-size; the GET gains an additive byte `offset` and the subscribe carries `from:<offset>`, so `GET(offset)→subscribe(from)` composes gap-free/duplicate-free via the byte-offset-tailed JSONL adapter (no client id-dedup overlap window). *Why a per-subscription producer goroutine, not the poll set*: transcript appends generate no tmux events (the recorded reason chat was ever a dedicated stream), so chat cannot ride the tmux poll routing; it owns a `chatProducer` (TAIL/DORMANT machine, ~2s re-resolve) tracked separately from `subs`. *Why rotation goes DORMANT and never re-tails from 0 (rework MUST-FIX)*: re-tailing a rotated-to ref from `from:0` re-streams a whole conversation over the socket and the early `chat-reset` 404-wedges the client's re-compose; going dormant + gating the single `chat-reset` on the rotated-to transcript existing fixes both and preserves lazy-transcript not-yet tolerance. *Why `TailFrom` supersedes the self-priming `Tail`*: `Tail`'s first-`Reset`-with-`Conv` contract existed only for the SSE `chat-backfill`; with backfill on the GET, keeping it is dead code. *Retired*: `handleChatStream`, the `chatStream` struct + `run`/`reresolve`/`subscribe`, `emitChatUpdate`, `writeSSE`/`writeSSEJSON`/`writeSSEError`, `sseHeartbeatPeriod`/`maxLifetime`, and the adapter `Tail` method. *Untouched*: the GET backfill (beyond the offset field), POST chat/send + probe/lock, `POST /keys`, the parser/schema. *Rejected*: snapshot-in-ack / full backfill on `chat-reset` (unbounded event size, D5); merging `/ws/state`+`/ws/terminals` (D6). Frontend `use-chat-subscription.ts` (successor to the deleted `use-chat-stream.ts`) — see [ui-patterns](/run-kit/ui-patterns.md) § Chat View and [chat](/run-kit/chat.md) § Live stream. *Residuals (recorded at hydrate, non-blocking)*: a swallowed subscribe `error` frame wedges the lens un-acked until a lens toggle / socket reconnect (should-fix, OPEN); byte offsets carry no file identity (a rotation landing on an existing longer transcript at a coincident line boundary can tail a different conversation with no reset — record-only); chat frames route by `windowId` alone client-side, so a stale cross-server frame can briefly route into the wrong lens, self-healing on backfill REPLACE (record-only). (`260717-vhvz-chat-on-state-socket`)
- **`currentWindowEverSeen` gate on kill-redirect over unconditional "gone → redirect"** — The redirect in `app.tsx` that fires when `currentSession` or `currentWindow` is null treats every SSE payload as authoritative by default, but the first payload after a navigation is not: the SSE hub can replay a cached snapshot before delivering fresh data, and tmux window-list enumeration can lag by one poll tick when a session was just created. Unconditionally redirecting on either transient state tears down `TerminalClient` mid-mount. The gate (a ref keyed on `${server}|${session}|${window}`, flipped true the first time `currentWindow` resolves non-null, reset on URL change) defers the redirect until the URL target has been observed as valid at least once. Rejected: inspecting SSE payload identity or delaying `isConnected` (both push complexity into the hub layer and would not distinguish real kills from stale catch-up). Rejected: adding a fixed startup debounce (arbitrary delay, races with fast tests). The gate preserves fast-redirect behavior for genuine kills (seen flag stays true after first valid observation) while eliminating the startup race. (`260417-g9uo-mobile-tap-focus-regression`)
- **CSS Grid topology for the rotated shell over nested flex** — The shell rotation makes the sidebar a column that spans all three rows (topbar, content, bottombar). Expressing "sidebar full-height; right column is a 3-row stack" with nested flex requires either a sibling sidebar with explicit height management plus a flex-col right column, or a 2-row layout with sidebar nested inside row 1 — neither matches the visual model and both diverge as future cells are added. Grid encodes the topology directly via `grid-template-areas: "sidebar topbar" "sidebar content" "sidebar bottombar"`; collapse becomes a one-line column-width change (`${sidebarWidth}px 1fr` ↔ `0 1fr`) animatable as a single `grid-template-columns` transition. Modern browsers (Safari 14+, Chrome 100+) animate `grid-template-columns` reliably. (`260509-17m3-rotated-shell-layout`)
- **Sidebar collapses to 0px, not a 48px rail** — Maximum content width when collapsed, accepting a small visual layout shift on toggle (the hamburger appears to "move" from sidebar-adjacent to page-adjacent, though structurally it always lives at TopBar.left — see next decision). Rejected: a 48px icon rail (VS Code/Linear/Slack convention) — avoids the visual relocation but consumes content width for a usability gain that diverges from the user's stated preference for max content width. (`260509-17m3-rotated-shell-layout`)
- **Hamburger statically rendered at TopBar.left** — Makes the visual relocation on collapse a free side effect of the grid column collapsing — no component-level relocation logic, no conditional mount/unmount, no animation orchestration. The hamburger's home is always TopBar.left; the column is what changes. Rejected: state-conditional placement (hamburger inside sidebar when open, inside topbar when closed) — adds a state-dependent component-tree mutation that complicates focus management and adds animation responsibility. (`260509-17m3-rotated-shell-layout`)
- **Single `sidebarOpen` boolean over `sidebarOpen + drawerOpen`** — The pre-rotation distinction between "sidebar open on desktop" and "drawer open on mobile" was a rendering-form difference, not a state difference. The user's intent ("show me the sidebar") is one boolean; the renderer picks the form (grid column vs absolute overlay) by viewport width. Collapsing the two booleans simplifies persistence (one localStorage key, `runkit-sidebar-open`), removes a class of "they're out of sync" bugs, and makes the keyboard chord a single state mutation. Rejected: keep two booleans — preserves a historical artifact at the cost of doubled persistence/reset logic and a confusing surface for new contributors. (`260509-17m3-rotated-shell-layout`)
- **`<Shell>` as a shared wrapper over per-route shell components** — Both AppShell and BoardPage need the identical 3-row × 2-column grid, sidebar collapse, mobile overlay, and visual-viewport handling. A single `<Shell>` (`src/components/shell/shell.tsx`) lets both routes consume a uniform topology; collapse animation, mobile overlay, and the topbar/content/bottombar geometry stay in one place. `Shell` renders the desktop `sidebar` grid area itself (from `sidebarChildren` + optional `sidebarResizeHandle`); consumers place only the `content`/`bottombar` grid areas via `style={{ gridArea: "content" | "bottombar" }}` elements. Rejected: per-route shell components — guaranteed to diverge over time (different collapse timings, drift in mobile overlay handling), defeats the rotation's "one topology, many routes" goal. Pattern note: future routes that need the same chrome should adopt `<Shell>` rather than reimplementing the grid. (`260509-17m3-rotated-shell-layout`)
- **`Shell` owns the desktop sidebar aside; the resize handle rides an opaque node slot** — `Shell` renders the desktop `<aside style={{ gridArea: "sidebar" }} aria-label="Sidebar">` (gated `!isMobile && sidebarOpen && !!sidebarChildren`) and exposes an optional `sidebarResizeHandle?: ReactNode` rendered at the aside's right edge; `border-r border-border` is applied only when no handle is passed. Both `<Shell>` consumers (AppShell, BoardPage) previously duplicated the aside scaffolding, the grid-area placement, and the `!isMobile && sidebarOpen` gate, and the two copies had drifted (AppShell flex-row + drag handle; BoardPage border-r + a different `aria-label="board sidebar"`). Shell already reads `sidebarOpen`/`isMobile`, so the branch moved in with zero new data dependencies, and the uniform `aria-label="Sidebar"` also gave AppShell's aside its previously-missing accessible name. The one per-caller divergence — AppShell's drag handle — rides through the opaque slot, so all drag state/handlers stay in AppShell and Shell stays dumb about drag logic. Rejected: a render-prop (`sidebar={(ctx) => …}`) — no caller needs Shell-provided context, so a plain node prop is simpler; Shell owning the drag handle — it would pull `handleDragStart`/width persistence into Shell and couple it to AppShell-only state. (`260719-rwqf-shell-sidebar-slot`)
- **`FocusedTerminalContext` as a separate, dedicated context (not a slice of ChromeContext)** — When BottomBar moved up to shell-level, it needed a way to target the focused terminal regardless of route. Folding the focused-terminal target into ChromeContext would mix UI state (sidebar open, fixed-width) with terminal-WS state and force every Chrome consumer to re-render whenever focus changes. A small dedicated context with its own provider (`FocusedTerminalProvider` mounted in `RootWrapper`) keeps the dependency narrow: only the shell-level BottomBar and the docked `ComposeStrip` read `focused` from it. The context carries only `focused`/`setFocused` — the compose surface's enablement is a persisted `composeStripEnabled` chrome preference, and the strip reads `focused.wsRef` LIVE at send time (a live target following pane focus, mitigated by an always-visible `→ {window}` label — deliberately reversing the earlier modal's frozen-target snapshot, `260718-dhdj`). Pattern note: future multi-input UIs that need a single shared input target should follow this "lift focused-input target to context" pattern rather than prop-drilling. (`260509-17m3-rotated-shell-layout`)
- **Read-only setter pair for in-memory + persisted state (`setSidebarWidth` + `persistSidebarWidth`)** — Drag-resize fires per-pointermove (potentially 60+ events per second). Persisting on every event would write localStorage 60 times per second per drag — unnecessary I/O and cache thrash. Splitting the dispatch into `setSidebarWidth(width)` (in-memory state) and `persistSidebarWidth(width)` (localStorage write) lets the drag handler call the cheap one in the loop and the expensive one once at drag-end. Convention note: future state with the same shape (live in-memory updates + final commit to persistence) should follow this two-setter pattern rather than debouncing inside the dispatch (which couples state lifecycle to a timing heuristic). (`260509-17m3-rotated-shell-layout`)
- **Mobile sidebar overlay positioned via grid (`gridRow: "2/4"`), not `fixed inset-0`** — The spec's literal phrasing was `fixed inset-y-0 left-0 z-50`, but the project convention recorded in `fab/project/context.md` and the existing `mobile-layout.spec.ts` assertion (`sidebarBox.y > 0`) requires the mobile overlay to leave the topbar visible — the topbar has the hamburger which closes the overlay, so covering it would be a usability regression. The implementation uses a grid-row-spanning child with `position: absolute` (not `fixed`) so the overlay anchors below the topbar inside the Shell. Pragmatic resolution: spec-wording "fixed-position overlay with backdrop" is satisfied — the overlay is fixed-position-style (absolute inside the Shell that itself is full-viewport), it has a backdrop, it carries `role="dialog" aria-modal="true"`. (`260509-17m3-rotated-shell-layout`)

## Testing

### Go Unit Tests

Go `testing` package with table-driven tests. Test files co-located with source using `_test.go` suffix. Test scripts: `go test ./...` from `app/backend/`.

Current Go test coverage (`app/backend/`):
- **Internal packages**: `internal/validate` (input validation + tilde expansion + filename sanitization), `internal/config` (env var reading, port validation, defaults), `internal/tmux` (listSessions parsing + byobu filtering, listWindows activity computation), `internal/sessions` (pane-map JSON parsing, per-window fab field join, graceful degradation on pane-map failure, `fab` router not on PATH via `TestFetchPaneMapFabNotOnPath`, end-to-end subprocess invocation via `TestFetchPaneMapIntegration` gated on `exec.LookPath("fab")`)
- **CLI command tests**: `cmd/run-kit/root_test.go` (no-args defaults to serve), `cmd/run-kit/version_test.go` (version output format), `cmd/run-kit/doctor_test.go` (LookPath-based dependency check)
- **Handler integration tests**: `api/health_test.go`, `api/sessions_test.go`, `api/windows_test.go`, `api/directories_test.go`, `api/upload_test.go`, `api/sse_test.go`, `api/spa_test.go` — all use `httptest.NewRecorder` with the chi router and mock `SessionFetcher`/`TmuxOps` interfaces for tmux isolation. Cover response shapes, validation errors, URL param parsing, content-type enforcement. `api/terminals_ws.go` (the pane relay mux, `260717-803u-relay-mux`) has `api/terminals_ws_test.go`: the HOL scheduler test (`TestScheduler_EchoNotHeadOfLineBlocked` — paced-writer seam, no real network) plus per-stream behavior against a live-tmux `/ws/terminals` dial (`opened` precedes data, initial-size attach + TERM forcing, resize, client-close→`closed` 1000, bad/missing window→`closed` 4004 with the socket still open). The 4001 attach-failure path has no dedicated test (forcing `StartWithSize` to fail needs a seam that does not exist — accepted). `api/relay_test.go` was ported to these `/ws/terminals` equivalents (its `withRelayTmux`/`relayServerWithProdTmux` helper names outlived the retired endpoint — a cosmetic-rename deletion candidate)

### Frontend Unit Tests (app/frontend/)

Vitest with jsdom environment. Config at `app/frontend/vitest.config.ts`. MSW mocks all API endpoints (`app/frontend/tests/msw/handlers.ts`). Test files co-located with source using `.test.{ts,tsx}` suffix. Since `260716-qf3j-state-socket`, `session-context.test.tsx` drives a `MockWebSocket` speaking the state-socket protocol (hello/subscribe/ack/event/gone) — the behavioral assertions (per-server isolation, server-order re-sort, server-gone teardown, host-metrics dedup, `hostMetricsConnected` debounce, `serversLoaded`, `pendingServer`, `shouldReloadOnVersion`, StrictMode re-subscribe) are preserved.

Test coverage includes: sidebar (expand/collapse, window selection, kill session, activity dots, duration display, info popover), breadcrumb dropdowns (open/close, selection), drawer (open via hamburger, close on selection), command palette (Cmd+K), modifier state, touch targets (44px on `coarse`), API client (correct URL construction for each endpoint).

### Playwright E2E Tests (app/frontend/tests/e2e/)

Thin suite (3-5 tests) for API round-trip validation. Config at `app/frontend/playwright.config.ts`. Self-managed tmux sessions in `beforeAll`/`afterAll` hooks.

E2E test coverage: create/kill session via UI, state-socket delivers real data, sidebar navigation, sidebar window sync (external window creation/rename reflected within 5000ms, kill-then-create at same index does not suppress new window via stale optimistic context). A `connection-budget.spec.ts` guard asserts each route holds **≤ 2 WebSockets total — 1 `/ws/state` + (0 or 1) `/ws/terminals`** (Host and bare-server routes hold only state; Terminal and Board routes add exactly one terminals socket) and **zero `text/event-stream` responses** — **including a chat-lens route case (`?view=chat`)** (`260716-qf3j-state-socket`, `260717-803u-relay-mux`, `260717-vhvz`): the last `EventSource` is gone, so even a chat view is 2 WS + 0 SSE (the chat-lens budget case runs `?view=chat` on a window with no `@rk_chat`, so the lens falls back to tty — documented in the `.spec.md`). Sockets are counted as opened − closed via each ws close event (a duplicate same-URL socket is detectable; Vite HMR WS excluded). `803u` replaced the per-pane `/relay/` classifier with a `/ws/terminals` classifier — a board with N panes now shows ONE terminals socket, not N relay sockets. A shared `_state-socket-mock.ts` `routeWebSocket` helper (answering `hello`→global-replay + `subscribe`→`ack`, extended by `260717-vhvz` to answer a `kind:"chat"` subscribe with an ack carrying `offset` + optional `chat`/`chat-state`/`chat-reset` emits) backs the specs migrated off `page.route(...text/event-stream...)` mocks; `chat-view.spec.ts` dropped its `**/api/windows/*/chat/stream*` `text/event-stream` route mock for the extended state-socket mock + a plain `GET /api/windows/*/chat*` backfill `page.route` (`260717-vhvz`); `multi-server-sidebar:70` (the long-standing UNFIXED attachServer→SSE flake) now passes DETERMINISTICALLY — the subscribe/ack protocol structurally fixed the race. Acceptance A-014 (two board panes, one flooding, the other stays interactive — the HOL scheduler in vivo) was verified via a throwaway e2e probe (echo ~421ms under a sustained ~10MB/s co-pane flood, the flood stream kept flowing, zero `closed`/socket churn), not a committed spec.

## Security

- All subprocess calls use `os/exec.CommandContext` with argument slices (never `sh -c` or shell strings)
- All `exec.CommandContext` calls include timeout via `context.WithTimeout` (10s tmux, 30s build). Terminal relay attach uses `context.WithCancel` (long-lived, cancelled on disconnect)
- User input validated via `internal/validate` before reaching any subprocess
- Directory listing restricted to `$HOME` via `ExpandTilde()` — rejects `..` traversal, absolute paths outside home, and `~username` syntax. Symlinks under `$HOME` are not resolved (accepted risk for local dev tool)
- File uploads: filename sanitized via `SanitizeFilename()` (strips path separators, null bytes, leading dots, collapses dot sequences); 50MB size limit enforced server-side via `http.MaxBytesReader`; writes via `os.Create` (not subprocess)
- CORS: permissive by default (`*` origin) for multi-client API flexibility. TLS handled by Tailscale Serve in production
- Web Push: the VAPID private key (`~/.rk/vapid.json`) is written mode `0600` and is **never** returned to any client — only the public key is served via `GET /api/push/vapid-public-key`. The subscribe/notify endpoints validate JSON shape and bound the request body (64 KiB); no subprocess execution is introduced by the push path (`260615-xd9r-web-push-notifications`)
